# 太上慈悲道场消灾九幽忏

*The Great Supreme’s Compassionate Daoist Ritual for Dispelling Calamities and Repenting in the Nine Dark Realms*

**Title:** *The Great Supreme’s Compassionate Daoist Ritual for Dispelling Calamities and Repenting in the Nine Dark Realms* (*Taishang Cibei Daochang Xiaozai Jiuyou Chan*). Ten fascicles. Originally compiled by Ge Xuan of the Han, as transmitted and collected. Base text from *Zhengtong Daoist Canon*, *Dongxuan* section, *Weiyi* category.

**Preface to *The Great Supreme’s Compassionate Daoist Ritual for Dispelling Calamities and Repenting in the Nine Dark Realms***
Composed by Li Hanguang, Master of the Three Caverns and Master of Mystic Stillness

In the beginning, when the Crimson Clarity first dawned, cloud-script took form at the celestial pole. After the rise of the Flame Emperor’s Han, sacred texts gradually spread among humankind. In the western lands of Shu, the golden palaces bequeathed their teachings; in the eastern realm of Wu, the Great Ultimate transmitted its doctrine. Thus, secret scrolls of the Great Existence and jade chapters of the Cavern Realms emerged—Zhang and Xu revealed them in earlier times, while Tao and Lu disseminated them later. Master and disciple followed in succession, and generations produced such figures.

*The Great Supreme’s Compassionate Daoist Ritual for Dispelling Calamities and Repenting in the Nine Dark Realms* originated with the Left Immortal of the Great Ultimate, Ge Xuan, during the reign of Emperor Huan of the Later Han. Dwelling in reclusion on Mount Yushan of Tiantai, he cultivated the Dao in seclusion. The Perfected One of the Great Ultimate, Xu Laile, descended into the Immortal’s chamber and bestowed upon him the *Lingbao Celestial Writ*, the *Jade Script of Cavern Reality*, the *Cavern Mystery*, the *Cavern Spirit*, and the thirty-six divisions of precious scriptures. The Immortal, abiding in the mountains, refined his thoughts and stilled his mind. Over decades, he communed with spirits and moved the sacred. Mountain spirits and tree ghosts guarded and bowed in reverence.

The wandering souls and lost spirits all attain transcendence and rebirth. This was deemed the profound essence of the Great Vehicle, capable of enlightening sentient beings and rescuing those drowning in suffering. Thus, from within the Three Caverns, the Immortal distilled their essential teachings, compiling repentance texts to ensure that all beings of the present age might hear and witness them. For future generations of scholars, these would be easily understood and practiced, extending even to the boundless.

In the icy nights of Fengdu’s Avīci Hell, the Three Paths and Five Sufferings, the Eight Difficulties and Nine Dark Realms—where tormented souls languish in confinement—none would remain trapped. Whether living, past, or yet to come, all who have committed fresh transgressions or carried ancestral sins, whose karmic entanglements and calamities have bound them, would receive the moistening grace of the Dharma, assembling in the realm of true perfection. Thus, this teaching spread.

Thereafter, those drawn to evil causes numbered barely two or three in a hundred, while those awakening to virtuous conditions reached eight or nine in ten. Hence, the ranks of immortals were fully established, and the work of transformation and guidance was complete. This text is therefore set at the beginning of the scroll.

---

*The Great Supreme’s Compassionate Daoist Ritual for Dispelling Calamities and Repenting in the Nine Dark Realms*, Scroll One
Compiled by the Left Immortal of the Great Ultimate, Ge Xuan

The Primordial and the Jade Emperor, supreme sages, respond to beings by manifesting forms and establishing teachings according to circumstance. Without the treasure of scriptures, the dust of delusion cannot be dispelled. From their mouths flow jade texts, expounding these sacred mysteries, returning to purity and simplicity—this depends on the heart. For those who seek learning, the method is here revealed.

The *Scripture of the Chapter on Generating the Spirit* states: In the Dragon Han kalpa, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy expounded the twelve divisions of the *Cavern Reality* scriptures:
1. *Supreme*
2. *Wondrous Grove*
3. *Great Clarity*
4. *Penetrating Vision*
5. *Highest Clarity*
6. *Transformation and Enlightenment*
7. *Primordial Yang*
8. *Wondrous Perfection*
9. *Opening the Mountain*
10. *Ten Immortals*
11. *Jade Grove*
12. *Yellow and Lao*

These scriptures are stored within the Great Cavern’s Jade Clarity Realm.

In the Crimson Brightness kalpa, the twelve divisions of the *Cavern Mystery* scriptures were expounded:
1. *Spiritual Harmony*
2. *Numinous Treasure*
3. *Communion with Spirits*
4. *Immeasurable*
5. *Assembly of Immortals*
6. *Inner Secrets*
7. *Utmost Perfection*
8. *Gathering Virtue*
9. *Refining Essence*
10. *Life and Death*
11. *Palace Diagrams*
12. *Dispelling Demons*

These scriptures are stored within the Great Cavern’s Highest Clarity Realm.

In the Kaihuang kalpa, the twelve divisions of the *Cavern Spirit* scriptures were expounded:
1. *Great Perfection*
2. *Utmost Virtue*
3. *Yellow Court*
4. *Refining Qi*
5. *Dao and Virtue*
6. *Primordial Spirit*
7. *Great Kalpa*
8. *Inner Simplicity*
9. *Divine Invocations*
10. *Three Sovereigns*
11. *Subduing Demons*
12. *Lesser Kalpa*

These scriptures are stored within the Great Cavern’s Great Clarity Realm.

Thus, the thirty-six divisions of the Three Cavern scriptures are arrayed upon golden tablets, with the Seven Sages setting forth the model, illuminating the royal canon. Once in ten thousand kalpas, the Dharma emerges in accordance with humanity.

The Three Caverns may be summarized as the One Vehicle. Therefore, the *Orthodox Unity* states: Though the Three Caverns are three, when encompassed together, they form the Dao of the One Vehicle. The *Great Mystery* is the Great Vehicle, the *Great Peace* the Middle Vehicle, and the *Great Clarity* the Small Vehicle. *Orthodox Unity* permeates all three.

In terms of rank and illumination, the Three Caverns correspond to the Three Clarities. The *Great Mystery* governs the three palaces above, the *Great Peace* the three palaces in the middle, and the *Great Clarity* the three palaces below.

These Three Cavern scriptures fully elucidate the profound canon, teaching and transforming according to circumstance, delivering humans and devas, and guiding all beings. In the human world, conduct varies in elevation, and the Dharma varies in depth, yet they enable the Six Paths to return to truth and the Three Vehicles to awaken to realization.

Now, contemplating the ages to come, I see those ascending and descending through the Six Paths, the four kinds of birth in the dark and manifest realms, the icy nights of the Nine Dark Realms, the Fengdu and Five Sufferings, the languishing souls and spirits—all enduring karmic retribution, suffering in life, unable to escape the demons of grievance. Therefore, from the Three Cavern scriptures, I have compiled and expounded the *Compassionate Daoist Ritual for Dispelling Calamities and Repenting in the Nine Dark Realms*, a work of ten scrolls, establishing its principles and completing its chapters.

By investigating the profound and abstruse meanings, whether living or deceased, those who revere the sages and repent their transgressions will immediately depart the Three Evil Paths, ascend to the Nine Clarity Realms, awaken to non-action, and return to the Great Dao.

The *Great Mystery Scripture* states: Formerly, the Lord of the Azure Youth declared, "To practice the Dao is苦, and not to practice the Dao is also 苦." Consider how, from birth to old age, from illness to death, the suffering of protecting the body is boundless, and the accumulation of vexations and sins only ceases at death. Many prayers fail to prolong life.

As for the苦 of practicing the Dao: maintaining purity and preserving truth, guarding the mysterious and contemplating the numinous, seeking teachers and upholding the Dharma, diligently cultivating the heart without laziness, and resolutely applying the will—this too is a 苦 endeavor. Regard the ranks of feudal lords as passing guests; regard gold and silk as mere pebbles...

Regard the esteem for plain silk as coarse cloth. This may be called the ability to inquire into the Dao.

The Lord of Western Citadel declared: "After death, to fall into the Three Evil Realms is easy; to obtain a human rebirth is difficult. Having obtained a human rebirth, to depart from the female form and become male is difficult. Having become male, to possess a complete and sound body is difficult. Having attained a complete body, to be born in the Central Kingdom is difficult. Having been born in the Central Kingdom, to encounter sagely rulers and parents is difficult. Having encountered sagely rulers and parents, to be born in an age where one may study the Dao and cultivate a heart of benevolence and kindness is difficult. Having cultivated a heart of benevolence and kindness, to believe in the virtue of the Dao and the attainment of long life is difficult."

Now, the Three Evil Realms are hell, the realm of hungry ghosts, and the realm of beasts—difficult to escape and be reborn as a human, instead becoming birds, beasts, insects, or livestock. If one seeks to avoid these, by what virtuous power may it be done?

The Heavenly Worthy said: "If one seeks to avoid the Three Evil Realms, one must first broadly vow before my manifested images of true sages, then eliminate the Three Actions and Six Roots, and afterward take refuge in the Three Treasures. Thereafter, dedicate the merit, confess one’s transgressions, and inquire into repentance—thus attaining the divine within the human and joining the Dao of celestial immortals."

**Chapter One: Broadly Vowing Aspirations**
Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, together with the repentant patron so-and-so, reflect that in this life, we have obtained human form, dwell in the floating world, and have encountered the true teaching. Gazing upon the sacred countenance, we bow our heads in reverence and take refuge, vowing great aspirations:

First, we vow that from this day forward, we and all in this assembly shall establish myriad virtuous practices, transforming the six destinies and four births, that all may equally attain liberation and forever depart from the defiled and chaotic realms of the world.

Second, we vow that life after life, we shall leave the household, forsake worldly attachments and affections, follow conditions to beg alms, broadly cultivate fields of merit, constantly practice compassion and forbearance, and forever transcend the distinctions of self and other.

Third, we vow to constantly encounter noble friends who guide and instruct us.

Fourth, we vow to meet enlightened masters and receive the supreme Dao.

Fifth, we vow to hear the true Dharma and practice it as taught.

Sixth, we vow to behold the Heavenly Worthy and personally receive the sacred decree.

Seventh, we vow to deliver all beings, placing others before ourselves.

Eighth, we vow to widely proclaim the Dharma to the ignorant and benighted.

Ninth, we vow that all sentient beings shall awaken the intention for the Dao, believe in and venerate the scriptures and images, construct numinous temples, and offer incense, flowers, lamps, and candles according to their means.

Tenth, we vow that our hearts shall remain steadfast and unwavering. By this virtuous power, may demonic forces be subdued, and the realm attain peace and tranquility. May those who have not heard hear, and those who have not seen see. May those who delight in the Lesser Vehicle not doubt the Middle Vehicle; may those who have entered the Middle Vehicle not doubt the Great Vehicle; and may those who have entered the Great Vehicle wish all sentient beings to hear the wisdom of enlightenment. May those who have not yet awakened awaken; may those who have awakened grow further; and may those who have grown become eyes and ears for others, Dao guides, parents, elder brothers, and friends—gathering in the Dao altar, joining as companions in the Dharma.

We further vow that all sentient beings, before the scriptures and the venerable, in their own bodies and others’, in all inner and outer Dharma, shall not generate minds of transgression, arrogance, anger, jealousy, or stinginess.

We further vow that all the merit we cultivate shall not be for ourselves alone but shall universally extend to all. Upon seeing the orphaned, solitary, imprisoned, or ailing, may we arise with minds of rescue, salvation, the Dao, and sincerity.

We further vow that the hidden and manifest true sages shall together bestow their protection and deliverance. May the repentant patron so-and-so and all of us in this assembly fulfill our broad vows, our hearts aligning with the true sages. May the power of our vows extend to our parents of past, present, and future lives, our six relations, and all living kin—may they all attain peace and happiness. May those who have passed not be reborn in evil realms, and may those yet to come not accumulate grave transgressions. May all equally realize the fruition of the vows we make today.

**One bow**

**Chapter Two: Eliminating the Three Actions and Six Roots**
Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, each turning their minds, together with the repentant patron so-and-so, reflect that in this life and past lives, we have not heard the true Dharma, often arising perverse thoughts, our discerning natures lost in confusion, failing to seek the ultimate principle.

The *Sutra of Karmic Retribution* states: "All that has form is transient and illusory. Thought after thought perishes, never pausing for even a moment. Suffering and affliction revolve endlessly; unawakened and unenlightened, we traverse the Three Ways, enduring myriad kalpas of bitterness. Receiving one body after another, we are bound by the fetters of affliction—all due to the Three Actions."

For there are Six Roots: the eye root, ear root, nose root, tongue root, body root, and mind root. These roots give rise to all actions, hence the Six Roots are like grasses and trees, producing myriad flowers and fruits, endlessly generating one another. Thus arise the Six Passions, Six Desires, Six Defilements, Six Entrances, Six Thieves, Six Dusts, and Six Consciousnesses. Yet form, sound, fragrance, flavor, touch, and dharmas are fundamentally empty and tranquil, neither moving the body nor disturbing the mind. It is sentient beings who cling and grasp, vainly harboring preferences and aversions, thought after thought racing in competition, afflictions binding the body. By these causes and conditions, we drift and wander through birth and death.

If one can purify wisdom and carefully reflect, awakening to these Six Roots before my image, then all roots shall be exhausted.

The Three Actions are: bodily action, mental action, and verbal action. We in this assembly, together with the repentant patron so-and-so, have indulged the Three Actions and Six Roots for countless kalpas, never once awakening. Today, before the image of the true sages, we arouse the mind of wisdom, generate the intention to awaken, and pledge to eliminate them.

First, we repent the sins of bodily action: from birth, we have killed, stolen, and indulged in lust, greedily seeking fine and smooth things. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not commit killing or stealing, nor crave fine and smooth things, nor indulge in lust, seeking liberation from the fetters of desire. May we encounter the scriptures and, before the images, bathe in fragrant waters, purifying body and spirit, contemplating the Dao and reflecting on truth. Striking the Dharma drum, we visualize the Three Treasures, repenting for all sentient beings, forever seeking the fruit of purity.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of mental action: from birth, our minds have been driven by greed, anger, ignorance, and attachment, racing with scattered thoughts.

The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not give rise to greed or anger, nor generate delusion or attachment, nor entertain perverse thoughts, ever aspiring to the true and authentic. May we encounter the scriptures, focus our minds with single intent, as though before the Three Treasures, universally guiding all to take refuge, attaining the fruit of non-action.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of verbal action: from birth, our mouths have uttered frivolous speech and falsehoods, engaged in harsh words and slander. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge in divisive speech, nor harbor thoughts in the mind, but ever maintain purity, forever severing slander. May we encounter the scriptures and, before the sacred images, concentrate our thoughts with precision, universally enabling all to hear and know, eternally realizing the fruit of immortality and sagehood.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of the eye faculty: from birth, our eyes have been false and unreal, never truly authentic, wantonly generating conditions, falsely beholding forms. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge our eyes in generating conditions or coveting perceptions of form. With true and proper vision, we shall see all appearances as empty, seeking the inconceivable fruit of ultimate attainment.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of the ear faculty: from birth, our ears have heard the five tones, discerning purity and impurity. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge our ears in hearing sounds, lest they disturb body and mind, entangling us in afflictions. May we realize the fruit of quiescence.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of the nose faculty: from birth, our noses have distinguished fragrance and stench, perceiving the flow of qi. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge our noses in smelling fragrances, discriminating between the foul and the aromatic, mingling and confounding primordial qi, agitating the numinous terrace. May we realize the fruit of mystery and emptiness.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of the tongue faculty: from birth, our tongues have craved the five flavors, insatiable and unfulfilled, speaking slander and falsehoods, maligning the loyal and flattering the virtuous. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge our tongues in savoring flavors, nor engage in quarrels or gossip, nor incite defamation. May we realize the fruit of truth and authenticity.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of the body faculty: from birth, our bodies have sought only sensual pleasure, unaware of the suffering to come after death. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge the body’s conditions in coveting illicit pleasure or pursuing wanton delight, but ever seek to withdraw and deliver others. May we return and realize the fruit of the Great Dao.

**One bow**

Next, we repent the sins of the mind faculty: from birth, our minds have lacked steadfast constancy, shifting and unpredictable, like apes or horses, akin to fire and wind. The repentant patron so-and-so vows that from this day forward, we shall not indulge the mind’s faculty, maintaining constancy from beginning to end, with movement and stillness undisturbed. May we enter and realize the fruit of spontaneity.

**One bow**

Today, the assembly of this Daoist ritual, each directing their minds, together with the repentant patron so-and-so, repent the sins of the three karmic actions and six faculties as above. We universally vow to the Most High Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Ten Directions, all the venerable and sagely ones, all perfected and immortals, all the great sage assemblies who have attained the Dao, and all the concealed and manifest honored sages of the ten directions: may you arouse the mind of protection and extend your compassionate intent. May the repentant patron so-and-so, from kalpas past to this very day, have all sins and karmic offenses, from the moment this mind of resolve is generated, completely extinguished. May this extend even to our parents in this present life, our masters who have guided us to liberation, our countless ancestors, siblings, and six relations, our in-laws and kin—those living in this world and those yet to come—who, by virtue of this repentance, have all their transgressions dissolved. For those already departed, may they not sink into evil destinies or dwell in dark obscurity, but swiftly attain rebirth in the Land of Eternal Bliss.

**One bow**

**Section Three: Taking Refuge in the Three Treasures**

Today, the assembly of this Daoist ritual, each directing their minds, together with the repentant patron so-and-so, have heard the words of the Great Canon: all sentient beings, born between heaven and earth, know not the sheltering and supporting [of the Dao]. Though they receive the Great Dao, they are unaware of their true origin. Turning away from brightness toward darkness, pursuing the superficial and abandoning the fundamental, reverting from correctness to perversity, estranging themselves from truth and embracing falsehood, they defile the Three Luminaries and perpetually commit the ten evils, never generating shame or remorse, but constantly harboring venomous thoughts. Now, those who cultivate goodness and establish merit must first take refuge in the Three Treasures. Thus, the scriptures say: if one does not take refuge in the Three Treasures, then good dharmas have no foundation to rely upon. The Three Treasures are the Treasure of the Dao, the Treasure of the Scriptures, and the Treasure of the Masters. Though their paths differ, their fruits and causes vary.

The Treasure of the Dao: throughout the three realms and ten directions, it manifests in myriad forms. Sometimes as a sovereign, sometimes as an imperial teacher, it establishes heaven and earth, nurturing and sustaining living beings, absolving the roots of transgression, dissolving and dispelling calamities. Riding dragons and appearing in forms, driving chariots and soaring through the void, it abides in non-action and spontaneity—thus is the Treasure of the Dao honored.

The Treasure of the Scriptures: inscribed in purple characters on flowery terraces, written in mysterious texts on soaring trees, concealed in the secret repositories of celestial and immortal officials, bound in azure dragon’s precious scrolls, encased in white phoenix’s jade boxes, comprising four divisions and five thousand [scrolls], inscribed on jade tablets and golden slips, resting on stands of mystery and emptiness, wrapped in frost-like silk veils, they encompass the ultimate Mahāyāna—thus is the Treasure of the Scriptures honored.

The Treasure of the Masters: without understanding the Dharma’s principles, how can one distinguish the roots of things? Desiring to cross the river of craving and reach the shore of the Dao, without a ladder or a boat, how can one attain fruition without the aid of a teacher? Only by accomplishing the precepts can one establish this Dharma-body—thus is the Treasure of the Masters honored.

Today, the assembly of this Daoist ritual, together with the repentant patron so-and-so, prostrate ourselves for peace and to offer posthumous deliverance. Before the true and the images, we repent our sins and transgressions, bowing our heads in submission, taking refuge and paying reverence.

We bow our heads and take refuge in the Treasure of the Dao of all ten directions.

**One bow**

We bow our heads and take refuge in the Treasure of the Scriptures of all ten directions.

**One bow**

We bow our heads and take refuge in the Treasure of the Masters of all ten directions.

**One bow**

Today, the patrons and the great assembly of this Daoist ritual universally vow to the Most High and all the authentic Three Treasures of the ten directions. We humbly pray that your compassion universally descends, your wondrous responses follow the needs of beings. The repentant patron so-and-so prostrates for peace and posthumous deliverance, relying on the Three Treasures and reverently serving the Most Perfect and True. We humbly pray that the power of your mysterious light and wisdom constantly delivers the four kinds of birth, steadily ferrying the vessel of compassion, eternally responding to the three realms. May this bring joy to humans and spirits, and may the hidden and manifest alike receive your grace.

**May all who hear or witness this, and those who enter the karmic conditions of the Dharma to pay reverence, awaken to the Dao.**
**One bow**

**Chapter Four: Dedication and Adornment**

Today, the patrons and the great assembly of this Daoist ritual, each directing their minds, prostrate in reverence to the Three Clarities and Four Realms, the Eight Poles and Nine Empyreans, the Thirty-Six Heavens and Thirty-Two Emperors, the Four Quarters and Six Directions, the Five Directions of the Boundless, the Ten Directions’ Most High Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy, the Perfectly True Radiant August Dao Lord, the Most High Lord Lao, the Venerable Lords, the Twelve Immortal Lords, the great holy hosts of the Ten Directions who have already attained the Dao, the Central Heaven’s Three August Star Emperors, the Sun and Moon and Five Agents, the Twenty-Eight Constellations, the Southern Palace and Northern Dipper, the Revolving Balance and all luminaries, the Five Peaks and Four Waterways, the Four Seas and Nine Provinces, the lords of famous mountains and great marshes, the Perfected of Highest Truth, the Directors of Destiny and Registrars of Life, the Three Officials and Five Emperors, the bureaus of the netherworld, the Nine Dark Prisons of Fengdu, the Six Palaces and Nine Courts, the officials of the earthly realms above and below, the Nine Lands’ Thirty-Six August Lords, the dragon spirits and all worthies and sages of this realm.

We humbly pray that they collectively descend without partiality, jointly respond with discernment.

The repentant patron so-and-so, with utmost sincerity in heart, purifies the ritual space, commissions scriptures and invites sacred images, kindles lamps and burns incense, prostrates and offers devotion, beseeching our assembly to universally venerate the Heavenly Worthies of the Ten Directions—manifest in boundless transformations and under myriad appellations.

We only pray that the great Perfected and Sages, the great divine immortals, the great lords and rulers, the great dragon kings, and the numinous consciousness of empty space, bear witness to this repentance, rescue sentient beings, and universally enable all who hear or know to awaken to the Great Dao.

The repentant patron so-and-so, prostrating with all five limbs to the ground, single-mindedly invokes and prostrates to the Merciful Honored Ones, reverently saluting the Perfected and Sages.

With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Clarity who bestows blessings.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who rescues from suffering upon hearing cries.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of the Jade Treasure August.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who generates boundless fortune.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who extends lifespan and increases years.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who preserves life and protects destiny.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who dispels calamities and resolves misfortune.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of the Eight Trigrams who shields the body.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of the Nine Palaces who wards off misfortune.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of Purple Clarity who descends blessings.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who augments great fortune.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of the Dharma Bridge who universally ferries.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who protects life and shields the body.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who rescues from suffering.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who responds to needs and attends to karmic conditions.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy whose forms flow through billions of kalpas.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who divides forms into myriad transformations.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion who protects the state.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy who enables rebirth according to wishes.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merits.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Perfected of the Ocean of Empty Wisdom.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Perfected who universally attains wondrous practices.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Perfected of Great Compassion who rescues from suffering.
With sincere mind, we reverently salute the Perfected of Great Mercy who extricates from transgressions.

Today, the patrons and the great assembly of this Daoist ritual humbly pray to the Most High Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Eastern Direction, all the honored ones and sages, all the great Perfected, all the great youths, who pervade the boundaries of the Ten Directions, fill the realms of the Mysterious Void, and manifest in all honored and sagely forms.

The repentant patron so-and-so first dedicates these merits to universally adorn and ascend in offering to the imperial house, the myriad ancestors and ten thousand forebears, the imperial father and mother, the revered spirits of the seven ancestral temples, that their souls may ascend to the Purple Empyrean, refine their essences in the Vermilion Mound, bathe in the jeweled pools, repose in the wondrous gardens, don robes of crimson auroras, wear crowns of emerald clouds, ride the Threefold Plain Clouds, drive the Eight-Phoenix Chariot, transcend the Flowery Towers, serve in the Jade Clarity, face the "Vacuous August One," stand shoulder-to-shoulder with the highest sages, be promoted to the ranks of divine Perfected, have their names inscribed in the celestial registers, dwell in the upper realms, bring benefit and peace to the lower lands, eternally protect the ancestral line, perpetually flourish the sacrificial rites, and enjoy boundless offerings—may all under heaven rejoice in this great fortune.

Next, we pray for the present emperor: may the dragon’s chart shine resplendent, the phoenix’s calendar flourish, his blessed reign be without end, his grand foundation eternally firm, myriad virtues gather like clouds, a thousand auspices descend like mist. May his sagely body enjoy fine health, his imperial mind radiate wisdom, the sky of Yao eternally shelter, the sun of Shun forever shine. With his sagely wisdom, perfect and all-pervading, his virtue and teachings widely bestowed, he is hailed as the pinnacle of prosperity. As in ancient times, may his grace extend to Hua and Yi, his benevolence reach the remote frontiers. May his ministers be enlightened and upright, his royal plans well-ordered, his civil and military officials of heroic talent, diligently cultivating the imperial enterprise. May the five marquises and nine governors, the hundred officials and myriad functionaries, secure the state and pacify the people, serve the public and follow governance, eradicate the ills of the age, harmonize the realm, ensure abundant harvests of grain and beans, quell weapons of war, and together enjoy peace and prosperity—all singing the praises of sagely brilliance.

Next, we pray for the imperial heir: may he be endowed with the weight of primal goodness, his Dao radiate layered brilliance, his virtue align with Heaven, his brightness match the sun, aiding and sheltering all beings, assisting in the perfection of sagely governance. May his moral and heavenly wealth abound, rites and music daily renew, his light illuminating the royal plans, his grace moistening the common people. May the golden branch flourish, the jade leaves extend their fragrance.

For the empress, the six palace consorts, and imperial concubines, the imperial daughters and moonlike maidens, may they rival the beauty of the Golden Mother, match the years of the talisman of firm Qian, eternally unwaning, their earthly virtue enduring, accumulating merits and piling up virtues, inwardly sagely and outwardly kingly.

For the imperial princes and royal clans, the heirs and feudal lords, the noble relatives and court worthies, the provincial governors and regional commanders, the frontier inspectors and their aides, the county magistrates and overseers—ever bearing toil and labor, ever cherishing loyalty and filial piety—may they, through this rite of repentance, have bodies as steadfast as mountains, lifespans as vast as the deep sea, eternally guard the inner citadel, forever rest on the unshakable stone. May their utmost virtue be pure and profound, their kindness extend to the black-haired and swarthy, lost treasures return like beasts, pheasants tame and pests cease. May their light align with the Dao, perfectly aiding non-action.

Next, may all beings—scholars, farmers, artisans, merchants, and every class—throughout the land under heaven, whether noble or base, exalted or humble, equally partake in the Dharma of repentance, mutually rely upon and extol it, each attaining peace and well-being, universally increasing joy and contentment.

Moreover, may all creatures—those that creep, fly, or stir—every sentient being, be freed from entanglements, all receive the moisture of the Dharma, forever dissolve karmic obstacles, face the sacred and the true, sharing the same vow and the same bliss.

Next, may the nine generations of ancestors of the repentance sponsor, certain, along with clan kin, those who have passed before or transformed after, new souls and old acquaintances, by virtue of the precious marks, universally cross the Dharma bridge, directly reach the Vermilion Mound, swiftly transcend the fires of refinement, their souls purified and luminous, receiving retribution with clarity, ascending the ranks of immortals, all illuminating the ancestral line.

May the living—elders and youths, inner and outer kin—each attain longevity, their ancestral temples blessed with auspiciousness, all bathed in compassionate grace, forever dwelling in the sagely age, together meeting the conditions of the Dao.

Moreover, may those in the three wretched paths, the five sufferings, the eight difficulties, and the nine dark realms, no longer linger at the round gate, transcend to the pure and adorned, all by the power of the Dao, turning toward the mysterious merit.

May all wishes be perfectly fulfilled, together ascending the shore of the Dao.

One bow.

**Chapter Five: The Recitation of Repentance**

Today, in this grand Daoist sanctuary, each person directs their mind, gazing reverently toward the Merciful Honored One, reciting and inquiring in repentance.

The repentance sponsor, certain, joins hands before the heart, kneels lengthily, and listens attentively.

The *Scripture of Ascending the Mystery* states: All sentient beings, from immeasurable kalpas past until this day, have turned and turned in the world, revolving through birth and death, drifting on the river of desire, sinking in the realm of sound and form, deluded by existence and non-existence.

The repentance sponsor, certain, does not know the past karma—from what cause it arose; does not awaken to the karmic conditions of former lives—from what they were obtained; does not awaken to the true and real—how to escape birth and death. Today, by good fortune, encountering this rite of repentance, bows in homage, takes refuge, and seeks to listen and receive with discernment.

The *Scripture of Karmic Retribution* states: Once, in the Hall of Cold Radiance and Cinnabar, the Supreme Heavenly Worthy, moved by compassion for sentient beings suffering the sins of birth and death, divided his body throughout the Three Realms, scattered his form in the ten directions, traversing heaven above and earth below, nowhere not journeying. Arriving at the Heaven of Accumulated Virtue in the World of Mount Sumeru, seated upon a seven-jeweled radiant throne, he rejoiced with the great assembly of sages who had attained the Dao across the three times, the Heavenly Emperors, Flying Celestial Kings, Perfected Ones, Divine Lads, and countless hosts, expounding the Dharma.

At that time, the Perfected One of Universal Salvation, rising from the seat of fearlessness, sighed: "For immeasurable kalpas, I have never seen the Merciful Honored One as joyful as today, bestowing the great Dharma clouds, pouring the great Dharma rain, universally enabling those present to attain awakening, each receiving benefit according to their portion, inconceivable."

Wishing to rely on divine penetrations to observe the karmic conditions of good and evil in the boundless worlds, to reveal the future, enabling knowledge of past lives, the three times—past, future, and present—having spoken thus, prostrated and bowed to the ground, gazing up at the Merciful Countenance.

The Heavenly Worthy addressed the Perfected One of Universal Salvation: "You now can generate this vow, arouse the great mind of goodness, benefiting all, inconceivable. By this karmic condition, he immediately emitted nine-colored radiance, penetrating and illuminating the heavens and the hundred million worlds, even the boundless lands below, the majestic spirit pervading without obstruction, shining clearly before the eyes, as if on the palm of the hand."

The Perfected One of Universal Salvation and the great assembly, riding this majestic light, beheld above the heavens the divine play of the host of sages, their necks bearing perfect halos, bodies complete in marks, transforming appearances at will, large or small as suited. Some rode upon the light soaring through the void, mounted dragons or cranes, carefree and responsive, their divine penetrations unobstructed. They saw celestial youths and maidens, jade lads and maidens, countless in number. They saw phoenixes and peacocks, lions and apotropaic beasts, attending to the left and right. They saw golden halls and jade palaces, jeweled terraces and pearl pavilions, celestial music and celestial flowers, celestial fruits and celestial trees, jeweled ponds and golden gardens, immortals at play, venomous dragons and fierce beasts, markets encircling the city walls, celestial kin and celestial offerings, a hundred flavors arrayed, banners, flowers, parasols, and canopies, adorned with a hundred treasures. They saw flying terraces and traveling lodges, shifting within the void, celestial robes and cloud canopies, welcoming in the empty firmament. They saw lands entirely transformed into seven treasures—gold, silver, pearls, and jade—palaces and gardens, bamboo groves, the sounds of birds and beasts, songs and music, clothing, mats, carpets, and cushions, all naturally arising, not crafted by human hands. They saw immortals consulting on Dharma marks, heavenly kings inquiring about fortune and misfortune, hundreds, thousands, even ten thousand million jeweled seats, expounding the Great Vehicle, flying immortals, celestial immortals, and those newly learning immortality questioning the Dharma and debating its subtleties. They saw such realms of blessedness, joy, and freedom, manifold and beyond naming.

Moreover, they saw below the heavens the great sages and lofty perfected ones riding clouds and driving through the void, bearing banners and holding tablets, inspecting the records of sentient beings' sins and blessings. Flying celestial kings and spirits of good and evil, celestial lads, daily roaming the human realm, recording good and evil, reporting to the heavens. The cloud palaces and star offices, the palaces of the sun and moon, the lords of mountains, rivers, peaks, and streams, examining the people, assessing the merits and demerits of good and evil. They saw the five planets lose their courses, the seven luminaries deviate, the twenty-eight constellations not adhering to their celestial fields, inauspicious stars and baleful luminaries encroaching upon the imperial throne. They saw nations where warfare arose on all four fronts, the people rebelling, floods, droughts, locusts, fierce winds, and violent rains. They saw people whose years were entangled by inauspicious stars, whose fortunes were afflicted by malevolent stars, harmed by heavenly nets, plagued by earthly snares, their households troubled, their populations perishing, the five pestilences and seven afflictions causing calamities, local deities and tomb ghosts clinging to grasses and trees, wrongful deaths and demonic disturbances, falsely acting as ancestors, possessing spirits causing turmoil, water and wood spirits creating havoc, men and women without children or with children who do not live to maturity. They saw men and women in cangues and fetters, imprisoned, flogged and tortured, entangled in lawsuits and disputes, impoverished and distressed, with none to pity them, bedridden with chronic illness, desiring life yet not living, desiring death yet not dying, afflicted with leprosy, epilepsy, madness, and malignant diseases, foolishness and confusion, bodies incomplete.

They saw those struck by lightning and thunder, their bodies covered in sores, those harmed by blades, weapons, water, and fire—burned, scorched, hacked, or shot. They saw those devoured or stung by venomous insects and fierce beasts, their cries swallowed in the maw of struggle. They saw the orphaned and widowed suffering cold and hunger, bearing hardship alone. They saw men and women parted midway through life, never to reunite in this body, mothers and children torn asunder, made into slaves and bondservants, their forms misshapen and hideous, shunned by all, their lives cut short, their arms cradling untimely death. They saw men and women born incomplete—hands and feet twisted or lame, ears deaf and eyes blind, mute and afflicted with every malady. They saw men and women with bodies split open, festering with pus and blood, lips and mouths shattered, noses collapsed, loathed by all. They saw upon the earth and among men the mountains and rivers, the peaks and streams, the Yangtze and Huai, the seas and oceans, the birds in flight and beasts on land, the creatures of water rising and sinking, all living things, all creeping things, every kind of strange being.

And in the depths beneath the earth, within the Nine Dark Hells and the Fengdu Prisons, they saw sinners enduring every manner of torture, their torments beyond naming, their suffering bitter and piercing, cutting to the bone and wounding the heart—places of karmic retribution.

Thereupon, the Perfected One of Universal Salvation, beholding all the heavens and all the earths, saw how these causes and conditions differed in sin and blessing, suffering and joy. They knew not what cultivation in past lives had brought this, nor what transgressions in this life had wrought; what blessings in former lives had been, nor what sins in this life had arisen. Was it the natural endowment of the body? Was it the consequence of karmic retribution? Was it the work of the Three Agents? Was it the cause of parents? Was it the lot of this present life? Was it the seed sown in past lives? Was it sin borne by one alone? Was it calamity passed to descendants? Could it be that through cultivating goodness one might be delivered? Or was it simply the natural course of fate?

Only wishing that the Heavenly Worthy, in great compassion, would deign to grant enlightenment, that all beings might awaken to the causes and conditions of past lives.

The Merciful One replied: All living beings are children of the Dao. When a child is in pain, parents grieve; when the child’s illness is cured, parents find peace. Since such suffering exists, it must be treated. Excellent, Perfected One of Universal Salvation, that you have aroused such a profound mind, enlightening and benefiting all, awakening every kind. Your question truly accords with my heart. Had you not spoken, I would have still explained. Your compassion is no different from mine. Your merit and virtue are beyond conception. You are the field of blessing for the world, the boat and oar for the world, the father and mother of the world, the guide and teacher of the multitudes, the leader of the people, the master of the Dharma, the arbiter of cause and effect. Now take your seat again, and I shall expound.

Today, the master of this repentance rite has heard from the beginning of the kalpa the words of the Supreme Perfected One, inquiring of the heavens above and the earth below, of the suffering and joy of beings, the manifold causes of sin and blessing, the unfathomable conditions of past lives. Now, the master of this repentance rite, for the sake of peace and deliverance, performs this rite of repentance, prostrating body and mind, wholeheartedly arousing devotion. Bowing to the Merciful One, they reverently honor the Perfected and Sacred.

With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Clarity who bestows blessings.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who saves from suffering at the sound of a cry.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jade Treasure, Supreme in Heaven.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy, Teacher of the Three Realms.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Manifestation and Self-Mastery.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Radiant World.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who transmits the True and illuminates all.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy, vast source of the Dharma.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who extends life through vast kalpas.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of boundless compassionate shade.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Dharma Treasury.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who broadly opens expedient means.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who delivers beings from distress.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who saves from the Eight Difficulties.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms the Three Wretched Realms.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who prospers the nation and transforms the people.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who saves from suffering.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who preserves life and protects destiny.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion who guards the nation.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of boundless reach.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy, ocean of merit and virtue.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of carefree joy.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to one’s wishes.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected One of the Empty Sea and Treasury of Wisdom.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected One of Universal Virtue and Wondrous Conduct.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion who saves from suffering.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion who extracts transgressions.

Today, the patron of this ritual and all the assembly humbly pray that the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the East, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected Ones, all the Great Divine Youths, throughout the ten directions and the farthest reaches of the empty void, all the manifest and hidden honored and sacred ones, may universally bestow their compassionate light and together dispense the medicine of the Dharma. May they elevate and advance the ancestral lines of the nation, the seven clans and three ancestral halls, safeguard the lord of the empire, the king, and his ministers and aides. May they deliver the master of this repentance rite, ourselves, our parents of three lifetimes, our teachers and kin, from the nine generations above to the seven generations below, all benefactors and donors, all those who dwell in realms yet unilluminated by the sun and moon, the flying and walking, the sinking and floating, the souls suffering in the Nine Dark Hells and all prisons, that they may be freed from calamity and together ascend the shore of the Dao.

One bow.

Today, the assembly of this ritual has heard that in a past kalpa, the Perfected One of Universal Salvation inquired of the heavens above and the earth below, of the manifold sufferings and joys, the causes of sin and blessing. The master of this repentance rite humbly prays that today, offering sincerity, they may come to hear the words of the scripture. What the Perfected One of Universal Salvation once asked—of the heavens above, the multitudes of sages and perfected ones, in golden halls and jade palaces, jeweled terraces and pearl pavilions, celestial palaces—where they roam freely, carefree and transforming, in every manner of indescribable joy.

The Merciful One said: This comes from cultivating the Dao through vast kalpas, step by step ascending the ranks, attaining the status of immortality.

Beneath the heavens, the great sages and exalted ones ride clouds and mount the void, recording the good and evil of the human realm, reporting to the heavens above, receiving Our teachings and commands—some to promote, some to punish. Thus, in those places, within the boundaries of lands and states, floods and droughts, locust plagues, fierce winds and violent rains, the fourfold rise of warfare—all arise from civil and military officials who, relying on their ranks and positions, defy the laws of the land, oppress the myriad people, pervert justice under the guise of public duty, and manipulate the king’s law, thereby incurring such retribution.

As for the people, men and women alike, who in this life suffer manifold illnesses and hardships, various demonic calamities, peril, distress, and adversity, whose bodies are incomplete—those who are poor and lowly, who upon death enter hell, endure all manner of karmic retribution, sink for ten thousand kalpas, and remain in the evil destinies—all this stems from immeasurable kalpas past down to the present kalpa, to this very life and day. Some suffer due to the deeds of their parents, some due to their own actions, the consequences flowing downward and extending onward, creating the three karmas, the six senses, and the ten grave evils. Generation after generation, they inherit all manner of bitter retribution; age after age, they endure every kind of demonic affliction.

What We speak of—the karmic deeds of sentient beings—is such that even a single deed encompasses hundreds of variations. To speak of it briefly would be to leave much unsaid.

At that time, Universal Salvation, having heard the Most High consent to reveal the causes and consequences of good and evil, the matters of karmic retribution, prostrated and bowed to the ground, saying: The Most High has said that sentient beings are foolish and benighted, sunk in the snares of the world, unable to awaken, bound only to karmic conditions, flowing through birth and death, enduring all manner of sin and suffering. We humbly pray that the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy may take pity and deliver them, so that future sentient beings may turn their hearts toward the good Dao, avoid bitter retribution, and escape the nine dark hells of Fengdu and the myriad prisons, where they endure all manner of torture.

The Most High said: If there are men or women who can arouse the natural intention of the Dao, purify their dwellings, and keep their bodies clean and adorned; who set up canopies and seats, install Our image, surround it with banners and flowers, keep lamps burning continuously, burn incense and scatter flowers in offering, sit or walk in mindfulness of the Dao; or who invite Dharma masters, or themselves, for the sake of protecting the state and bringing peace to the people, harmonizing winds and rains, averting disasters and delivering from hardship, safeguarding their dwellings, seeking to extend blessings and longevity, dispelling ghosts and expelling evil; or for the sake of their parents or themselves in times of illness or calamity, when stars and constellations exert their influence, seeking children, or ransoming and liberating those who have left the household life; or for the sake of uncles, brothers, wives, and children; or to console the earth spirits and tomb guardians, protect servants and livestock, and all manner of wealth; or for the sake of masters, lords, Dharma kin, the nine generations of ancestors—parents, brothers, uncles, wives, children, and the six relations—who have passed away, to provide offerings and deliverance; if they but come before Our image, bow to the sacred names of the Heavenly Worthies who manifest in infinite response across the ten directions, offer sincerity like melting snow, and with body and mind repent the sins of immeasurable kalpas, of lives past and present, of every rebirth down to this very day—then their sins shall be extinguished as they wish.

The transformative names of Us, recorded in the scriptures and spread among humankind, dispel heavenly disasters above, eradicate earthly calamities below, and benefit the people in between. In this life and the next, their merit shall never cease. They shall attain peace and stability for the realm, longevity for the emperor, harmony in the stars and constellations, and timely winds and rains. Demons, thieves, and enemies shall become good friends. Venomous creatures and fierce beasts shall harbor no ill intent. Wind, water, fire, and warfare shall cause no harm. Their wishes shall be fulfilled, their prayers answered. The suffering souls in the nine dark hells shall escape their dark prisons and be reborn in the heavenly realms. The four kinds of birth and six destinies shall all attain liberation.

At that time, the Perfected One of Universal Salvation, having heard the Most High expound this repentance Dharma for the deliverance of sentient beings, rejoiced in body and mind beyond all measure, extolling the Heavenly Worthy with these verses:

Excellent is the Primordial Beginning Worthy,
Revered by all in the Three Realms.
His sacred power is beyond thought,
His wisdom and virtue peerless.

Upon the natural seven-jeweled throne,
He manifests in the flowering grove.
Complete in form and appearance,
Unobstructed as the empty sky.

To reveal the profound mystery,
He opens the gates of myriad wonders.
Having realized the supreme Dao,
He turns the wheel of the Great Vehicle.

With skill he expounds the Dharmas,
Universally reviving all beings.
Having heard this Dharma,
Our hearts are purified, our defilements removed.

Overcome with joy,
We bow our heads to the Jade Void.

Today, the assembly of this ritual, along with the repentance master, from immeasurable kalpas past until now, have never before encountered this repentance Dharma. Today, humbly offering prayers for peace and deliverance, we reverently face the compassionate Worthy, the scriptures, and the sacred image, arousing boundless resolve and infinite intention. With our five limbs touching the earth, we wholeheartedly invoke:

We bow our heads to the Compassionate Worthy, reverently honoring the Perfected Sages.

With sincere hearts, we bow to the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy who bestows blessings.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who rescues the suffering upon hearing their cries.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jade Treasure Emperor.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to names and transforms.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Net who manifests in transformation.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who divides into millions of bodies.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who extends compassion through vast kalpas.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Ten Thousand Jeweled Lights.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Inexhaustible Lamp Light.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who manifests boundlessly.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Universal Deliverance.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms with sovereign ease.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, Master of the Three Realms.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who transmits the truth and universally illuminates.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who opens the way for sentient beings.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who takes pity without end.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who rescues the suffering.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who preserves life and protects destiny.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion who guards the state.

With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Expanse.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Vows.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Perfected One, Treasury of Wisdom in the Vastness of Space.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Perfected One of Universal Virtue and Wondrous Conduct.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion Who Rescues the Suffering.
With sincere hearts, we bow to the Perfected One of Great Mercy Who Removes Transgressions.

Today, the patrons of this Dao altar, together with the great assembly, reverently pray to the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the East, to all the Venerables and Sages, to all the Great Perfected Ones, and to all the Great Divine Youths—those who pervade the ten directions and fill the boundless realms of mystery, manifesting or concealed in all their majesty.

Through the power of great compassion, the power of inconceivable deliverance, and the power to bring peace to sentient beings, may all beings—whether dwelling in the heavenly realms—be elevated to the Formless Realms; whether in the divine realms, ascend to the Two Form Realms; whether in the human realm, attain the First Desire Realm; and those in the hells, hungry ghost, or animal realms, be reborn as humans, forever freed from suffering and retribution.

We further pray that the Compassionate Venerable, leading all disciples, may manifest and proclaim merit and virtue in this place of ritual repentance, so that:
countless lands receive blessings,
countless beings attain liberation,
countless realms of dharma come to know,
countless superior beings embody the Great Vehicle,
countless middling beings perform offerings,
countless lesser beings generate faith,
countless heavenly dragons guard this place,
and countless vajras sever demonic delusions.

The repentance master [Name], from kalpas without measure past, has cast off bodies and received bodies, taking birth in various realms, up to the present life. Today, may all sins—from the slightest thread or hair, a single name or kind, to those as numerous as the sands of the Ganges—be utterly extinguished from this day forward, with the arising of a single thought. May parents, teachers, uncles, brothers, oneself, spouse, children, the six relations, and all kin, through this act of repentance, together attain liberation and be spared from suffering and affliction. May all beings realize the supreme Dao.

**First Bow**
Thus concludes the first fascicle of *The Supreme Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Disaster Dispelling and Ninefold Darkness*.
**Second Fascicle of *The Supreme Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Disaster Dispelling and Ninefold Darkness***
Compiled by Ge Xuan, Left Immortal of the Great Ultimate

**First Chapter: The Mirror of Compassionate Reflection**

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, together with the repentance master [Name], reverently join hands and listen attentively to the scriptural words.

The Compassionate Venerable has taught that all sentient beings, in committing even a single deed, generate hundreds of karmic consequences—too many to enumerate in full, so let us speak briefly.

Then the Perfected One of Universal Salvation addressed the assembly, vowing to elucidate the myriad transgressions of future beings before the image of the Compassionate Venerable, repenting each one in turn. Though the causes may not yet be fully expounded, may they be broadly explained, so that beings of endless kalpas may find refuge.

The Compassionate Venerable said: Men and women of the world, casting off bodies and receiving bodies through kalpas without measure, take rebirth due to the sins constructed by the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and mind—killing, stealing, sexual misconduct, reckless indulgence, stinginess, greed, anger, ignorance, delusion, deceitful speech, falsehood, harsh words, divisive speech, envy of those superior, obstructing all things, consuming meat and wine, violating scriptural precepts, damaging sacred images, neglecting fasting rituals, disrespecting teachers, turning from truth to falsehood, believing in perverse views, cursing spirits, failing to honor the Three Treasures, slandering the worthy, scorning the empty and absurd, indulging in sounds and forms, becoming attached to fragrances and flavors, sinking into transgression, creating karma inwardly and outwardly, perpetuating cycles of mutual generation. The six senses arise in turn, compounding faults; the roots of sin grow, and with each thought, wrongdoing forms. There are boundless, immeasurable sins, their number like the dust of the earth, long-accumulated habits residing within. From past causes to present, kalpa after kalpa, with the arising of a single thought, all may be purified—like a bright mirror, where countless particles of dust, from before and behind, even the grease and grime of myriad impurities, accumulate to form obscuring films, dimming inner and outer clarity. Yet once it encounters a skilled craftsman, who wipes, polishes, and refines it, its surface and interior become radiant, reflecting near and far, resplendently clear, restored to its original state. Why? Because its nature is fundamentally pure.

So too are sentient beings: the spirit is originally pure, without defilement. But after receiving form, inner and outer dusts gradually stain it, turning it evil. The six roots, six emotions, six entrances, six defilements, six thieves, six dusts, six desires, six consciousnesses—discriminating and creating delusion—generate a filthy, encumbered body. Inner obscurations and outer afflictions arise, losing the true nature, drifting in the cycle of birth and death, sinking deeper into sin, meeting retribution through karmic conditions, and thus plunging into hell, enduring all manner of suffering, submerged for ten thousand kalpas.

Out of great compassion, I pity sentient beings, and so from kalpa to kalpa, I revolve through the human realm—sometimes in China, sometimes among barbarians; sometimes old, sometimes young; sometimes ordinary, sometimes sacred; sometimes female, sometimes male; sometimes noble, sometimes base—manifesting in various forms, teaching and transforming with skillful means, delivering sentient beings. The scriptural teachings spread, awakening all, enabling them to escape suffering and forever depart from the hells of mud and fire. Yet beings are dull-witted and cannot comprehend. Now, for your sake, I will broadly reveal the causes and conditions, further distinguishing them, so that future beings may turn their hearts toward the good path.

Upon hearing this parable and its distinctions, Universal Salvation’s body and mind leapt with joy. Praising the Compassionate Venerable, he spoke this verse:

Excellent, Primordial Beginning Venerable,
True Father and Mother of all beings.
You expound again the three and six roots,
And further illustrate with the mirror parable.
With skillful means, You rescue the submerged,
With compassion, You deliver from suffering.
Having heard this Dharma,
Our bodies and minds understand all causes.
For endless kalpas in the Dao altar,
You are the Master who preaches for the assembly.

Today, the repentance master of this Dao altar, [Name], prostrates for peace and in supplication for the departed. Having heard the verses and their instructions on the repentance Dharma, this is inconceivable. With five limbs touching the earth, I listen single-mindedly. Bowing my head to the Compassionate Venerable, I reverently pay homage to the true sages.

With devout heart, I pay homage to the Jade Clarity Bestower-of-Fortune Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Responding-to-Cries Deliverer-from-Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Life-Nurturing Savior-of-Lives Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Unmoving Radiance Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Great Penetration Spirit-Responding Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Supreme Virtue Radiance Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Flowing King Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Unobstructed Sound Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Eternal Dharma-Wheel Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Turner-of-All-Adversities Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Boundless Luminance Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Virtue-Luminous King Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Serene Wondrous Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Fragrant Luminance Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Square-Flower Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Pure Contemplation Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Mind-Detachment Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the World-Walking Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Longevity Preserver-of-Life Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Great One Deliverer-from-Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Universal Compassion Protector-of-the-Nation Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Boundless Horizon Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Ocean-of-Virtue Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Carefree Joy Heavenly Worthy.
With devout heart, I pay homage to the Wish-Fulfilling Rebirth Heavenly Worthy.

Today, the patrons of this Dao altar and the great assembly, gazing upward, vow to the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southeast, to all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected, all the Great Immortals, all the Great Divine Youths—pervading the ten directions, filling the boundless void, past and future, manifest and hidden, all true sages. May the rain of sweet dew wash away all dust and defilement. May the power of compassionate light deliver all beings, guiding them to the other shore, ultimately pure.

Through this repentance text offered by the repentance master [Name] for peace and in supplication for the departed, may the power of deliverance from suffering, the power of support, the power of salvation and protection, the power of disaster elimination, the power of virtue, and the power of peace ensure all wishes are fulfilled. May all sentient beings universally repent together and return to realize the Dao fruit.

One bow.

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar and the repentance master [Name] once more offer utmost sincerity, listening attentively to the scriptural words. The world in which all earthly beings dwell—the Sahā world—is floating, illusory, defiled, and impure. Hells, hungry ghosts, and animals fill the land of retribution. Few cultivate goodness; many commit evil.

In such a world, the four seasons pass and change, reckoning human lifespans, some long, some short. Spring, summer, autumn, winter—wind, rain, cold, heat—day and night, darkness and light, sun and moon hasten by. The land is of sand and gravel, uneven and treacherous. Mountains and rivers are perilous and obstructed; grasses and trees bear thorns. Not one thing brings joy.

The human body we receive is subject to birth, aging, illness, and death—a temporary aggregation of impurities, fragile and insecure. Because we have bodies, we seek clothing and food, yet often they are insufficient. Hunger, thirst, exhaustion, and deprivation afflict us. The laws of rulers drive us relentlessly; we cannot be at ease. Stubborn and dull-witted, our vision is shallow and clumsy. We associate with unwise companions.

Our eyes see evil forms, our ears hear evil sounds, our noses smell foul odors, our tongues taste bitter flavors, our bodies endure harsh touches, our minds contemplate wicked dharmas—such matters are boundless. Life is impermanent, truly fearful. Thoughts pass in succession, never pausing for even a moment. Swift as a spark from struck stone or a flash of lightning, a hundred years pass in but a few days.

Amidst such countless sufferings, there is no moment of peace. Moreover, beings’ karmic marks persist unbroken. Their natures are stubborn and hard, like earth mixed with tiles and stones. Those of many desires, seeking much profit, suffer greatly. Those who are ever content, though dwelling on earth, are at peace. Those who know no contentment, though in heaven, remain unsatisfied.

Moreover, long-accumulated evil causes sever good roots. Delusion and attachment blind them, preventing awakening. The darkness of ignorance veils their eyes. Some are entangled by new karma; others face retribution for past grievances. As ministers, they are disloyal; as children, unfilial. Their hearts harbor hidden malice; they secretly slander and curse. Evil spirits assail them, leading to repeated illnesses. Unexpected slander arises; misfortune strikes without warning. Careers stall; desires go unfulfilled. Water, fire, and weapons cause harm. Separation and death bring suffering. Countless sorrows and griefs cannot be fully recounted.

Moreover, the hindrance of afflictions is heavy; good fruits are rarely encountered. Even when seen or heard, they do not seek or desire to transcend suffering and be reborn. Instead, they rely on youthful beauty, family and children, towering mansions, and various pleasures, merely preserving their lives. Yet in an instant, all collapses. Regardless of wealth or nobility, the great limit approaches—what use are such pursuits?

Moreover, beings do not realize the world is empty and false, that human and heavenly realms are like dreams. Illness, suffering, and fragility bind them; sorrows entangle them. Time fleets by; cold and heat alternate. Not a moment is spent awakening and cultivating goodness. They only wish to drift endlessly in the sea of suffering, long mired in birth and death.

I pity beings more than parents pity their children. Parents’ love for their children lasts but one lifetime; my compassion for beings spans eternal kalpas. When parents see their children are unfilial, their hearts grow distant. When I see beings are unvirtuous, my compassion only deepens.

Should beings descend into the Nine Dark Hells of Fengdu or the Avīci and other infernal realms of suffering, I ever preach the Dharma, taking their torments upon myself. Now, seeing the questions you have raised concerning the karmic causes of beings’ sins and blessings, it is as though I have swallowed iron and stone, as though an arrow has pierced my heart. My thoughts of compassion and mercy never cease for even a moment. Today, I expound this repentance ritual to rescue those sunk in delusion. You must diligently practice it and broadly deliver beings in future kalpas.

Thus, the Universal Savior proclaims these gāthās anew:

The Primordial Beginning, Supreme and Unsurpassed First Honored One,
Transcends the Three Realms, peerless and without equal.
For countless kalpas, you have accumulated sublime practices,
Perfecting the pure and virtuous causes of blessings and wisdom.
All afflictions and habitual defilements are severed;
Ultimately, old karma is not recreated anew.
Your spiritual penetrations and mighty powers know no fear;
You perceive the Three Times with clarity, discerning the mundane and the real.
Your wisdom and all virtues are perfectly complete,
Gathered into this wondrous Dharma-body.
Though dwelling in hell, you take the place of beings,
Enduring the boiling cauldrons, searing furnaces, and scorching coals.
Frigid waters and icy springs do not harm your body;
Sword trees and blade mountains do not rend your flesh.
Seeing their anguish, your heart is filled with sorrow,
Yet you rejoice in suffering for their sake.
Thus, you attain this wondrous reward-body,
Like the moon cradled in the vast sea, its light serene and clear.
It embraces all without obstruction,
Nurturing the myriad things without exhaustion.
Roaming within the Three Clarities’ Dharma-positions,
Your heart transmits the flow of compassionate transformation without end.
Our praises cannot suffice to extol you,
For your boundless grace spans kalpas beyond reckoning.

Today, in this Dharma-assembly, let each person direct their mind. The repentance-master, so-and-so, acknowledges the emptiness of the Four Great Elements, the transience of the Three Realms, the uncertainty of life’s span, the fragility of the body’s form, and the entanglements of karmic burdens—all offenses are of my own making. Today, encountering this repentance ritual, I vow with utmost sincerity, bowing my head in reverence. May the fires of the Three Poisons be extinguished, and the mind of a hundred virtues arise. Prostrating with five limbs to the ground, I wholeheartedly listen with devotion, seeking peace and offering this repentance text in memorial.

I bow my head to the Merciful Honored One, paying homage to the true sages.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Jade Clarity Bestower of Blessings Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves Upon Hearing the Sound.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Cherishes Life and Delivers Beings.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Perfection in the Great Net.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Jeweled Light Pervading Illumination.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Subdues Demons and Dispels Afflictions.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Goodness and Protection.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Union with the Dao.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Loving Practice of the Dao.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Primordial Subtle Body.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Commands the Directors of Destiny.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Extracts the Ten Sufferings.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Compassionate Love.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Contemplates the Wondrous.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Attains Auspiciousness.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Three Qi.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Myriad Perfected.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mysterious Origin.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Delivers from Calamity.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Grotto.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Vaidūrya.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merits.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Limits.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and Nation-Protection.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Bliss.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Accords with Wishes for Rebirth.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Perfected of Wondrous Practice.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Perfected of Vast Faith.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Perfected of Great Compassion Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere heart, I pay homage to the Perfected of Great Mercy Who Extracts Transgressions.

Today, the Dharma-assembly’s sponsor, so-and-so, together with the great assembly, reverently beseech the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southeast, all the honored ones and sages, all the great perfected, all the great youths, and all the true sages throughout the ten directions and the vast expanse of the unseen, manifest and hidden. May they bestow their minds of vast compassion, mercy, deliverance, disaster-dispelling, blessings-gathering, and suffering-rescue, so that the repentance-master’s aspirations may harmonize with their heart, that they may ride the fruit of true sages, uplift sentient beings, and ascend together to the supreme Dao.

One bow.

**Chapter Two: Repentance of Deluded Thoughts**

Today, in this Dharma-assembly, let each person direct their mind, reverently facing the Merciful Honored One to repent the karmic offenses of deluded thoughts. The repentance-master, so-and-so, gathers their mind, kneels, and listens attentively to the scriptural words.

All beings, from the moment their bodily forms are born, are stained by the impurities of the dust. Eyes behold the five colors, noses smell the five fragrances, tongues taste the five flavors, ears hear the five sounds—all are but chaotic distractions. The true sound is not discerned; the true color is not seen. The mind arises in coarse violence, sinking into infatuation and attachment, giving rise to the roots of manifold karmic deeds, all stemming from deluded thoughts.

Whether man or woman, once the mind’s thought arises and turns toward me, repenting all manner of karmic offenses, first repent deluded thoughts and doubts, then repent all karmic deeds.

The Universal Savior asks, “What are deluded thoughts?”
The Merciful Honored One replies, “Beings’ deluded and inverted thoughts all arise from the mind.
