Forcibly making distinctions, they fixate on the body, and upon encountering circumstances, delusion arises—every thought is false. For this reason, contemplate the body with wisdom: bones, flesh, skin, bodily form, hair, the six sense faculties, the Four Great Elements, the five viscera, and the hundred spirits. Reflect carefully—there is no true substance to be found. They are merely a temporary aggregation of shared illusions, coalescing to form the body. Searching within and without, where am I to be found? Since the body is illusory, the mind becomes empty. Emptiness and illusion are not real—all are deluded thoughts. The body being a deluded thought, all dharmas are likewise. Self and other, right and wrong, love and hatred, grasping and rejecting, forms, sounds, fragrances, tastes, jealousy, stinginess, greed, killing, stealing, sexual misconduct, frivolous speech, harsh words—all karmic deeds, in an instant, are dissolved. Within and without, all is pure and empty, naturally uniting with the true Dao. All such beings, if before the Three Treasures they practice repentance of deluded thoughts...”

Or before the Dao altar, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before the scriptures and dharmas, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before the lectures and praises, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before heaven and earth, the empty void, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before the sun, moon, and stars, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before the images of all sages and revered ones, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before kings and emperors, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before civil and military officials, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before the Dharma-body of those who have left the household, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before parents, uncles, brothers, and all kin, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before teachers, masters, and Dharma-kin, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before the virtuous and wise, they entertain deluded thoughts.
Or before sacred altars and holy traces, they entertain deluded thoughts.
All such deluded thoughts—whether already entertained or yet to arise—once conceived in mind and intent, incur grave transgression.
The mind generates deluded thoughts, and the body bears the karmic burden, afflicting the present household.
It invites demonic adversities, entanglement in the six illnesses, thwarted aspirations, compounded hardships, calamities extending to the seven generations, and fault binding life after life.
Failing to awaken to the true Dharma, not comprehending the real principle, one descends into the fiery gloom of hell.
Enduring myriad torments, one is reborn in a body neither male nor female.
Without repentance, one sinks into eternal perdition.

Then the Merciful One spoke in verse:
*"In life, the mind’s deluded thoughts deceive and mock all things.
At death, one enters the fiery gloom of hell, where form and visage char and rot.
Reborn as neither man nor woman, hideous and despised,
one lives in folly, never hearing the Dharma of true principle."*

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, together with the repentant one, from limitless kalpas past to this very life and day—teachers, fellow disciples, disciples, parents, brothers, and one’s own flesh and blood—have harbored deluded thoughts yet unrepented.
Now, prostrating in reverence, we offer this repentance text for peace and merit-transference, bowing with the five limbs to the earth.
With single-minded focus, we listen attentively, bowing our heads to the Merciful One, paying homage to the true sages.

With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Jade Clarity Bestower of Blessings, Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Answers Cries for Help.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Cherishes Life and Delivers Beings.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Wisdom.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Unobstructed Spiritual Power.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Radiant Wisdom.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Receives Prophecy.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Dustlike Marvels.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of True Sage Wisdom.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Majestic Radiance.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Transforms Qi.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Countenance.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of True Wandering.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Contemplation.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Eight Poles.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of True Sages.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of True Transformation.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Rescues from Suffering.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Protects the Realm.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Dharma Comprehension.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Perfected One of the Great Ultimate.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Great Compassion Who Rescues from Suffering.
With devoted heart, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Great Mercy Who Removes Transgressions.

Today, the sponsor of this Dao altar and the great assembly reverently beseech the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southeast, all revered sages, all great Perfected Ones, all great youths, and all true sages across the ten directions, the infinite void, past and future, manifest and hidden.
By the power of the great Dao-mind, the true sage-mind, the boundless mind, the unobstructed intent, the inconceivable intent, and the power of merit,
may the repentant one—from beginningless time through rebirth after rebirth to this very life and day, the nine ancestors and seven generations, one’s own kin, both living and deceased—have all deluded thoughts and inverted karmic causes dissolved through this repentance.
From this day forward, may they realize the true sage-mind and walk the Way of Non-Action.
May evil thoughts and evil karma never again be created.
Further, by the power of the sages and the power of the Dao, may all beings enter the realm of attentive hearing, attain peace and bliss, and awaken to the great Dao.

One bow.

**Chapter Three: Removing Doubts**

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, each directing their minds, reverently face the Merciful One to repent the karmic offenses of doubt.
The repentant one gathers their thoughts with utmost sincerity, listens attentively to the scriptural words, and reflects: though the body of beings is fleeting and illusory, it possesses form—pain and itch, ache and soreness, hunger and cold, heat and dampness, inner disturbances and outer contacts, each thought assailing the next.
The mind unbalanced, sorrow and affliction arise together.
How, through contemplation, can these be swiftly eradicated?

The Merciful One says: doubt is but delusion and falsehood.
All that has form is fleeting and illusory, each thought impermanent.
Beings cling to it, falsely perceiving it as real.
If one knows the body is not real, all sufferings vanish.
Simply forget the self, and all delusions are extinguished—how then could pain and itch, ache and soreness remain?

The Universal Savior says: the doubts of beings are deeply entrenched; to suddenly forget the self is truly unattainable.
What expedient means can gradually reveal the causes and conditions?

The Merciful One says: one must resolve the will, contemplate the body with wisdom, listen and reflect carefully—finding no true substance—and yet still generate doubt, which leads to sinking and drowning.
These beings, their karmic actions impure, receive differing retributions.
Like form scattering shadow, like echo responding to sound,
nobility and baseness, good and evil, must manifest in gradation.

Though these gradations exist, beings fail to comprehend their fundamental nature.
They see the long-lived yet do not know their longevity arises from diligent observance of precepts.
They see the short-lived yet do not know their brevity arises from slaughter.
They see the wealthy and noble yet do not know their fortune arises from aiding the poor and relieving suffering.
They see the impoverished and lowly yet do not know their plight arises from greed, theft, and insatiability.
They merely see the long-lived and desire longevity for themselves;
they merely see the wealthy and desire wealth for themselves.
Such yearnings—who is without them?
Unknowing of past karmic causes and conditions, their fate is already determined at birth.
This is called delusion—such are these beings.

Whenever they encounter scriptures and repentance rites, they cannot recite or deeply believe them, thus giving rise to scorn and slander.
They see the realms beyond the Three Realms yet do not believe them to be blissful;
they see the realms within the Three Realms yet do not know them to be suffering.
Beyond the Three Realms lies effortless freedom, heavenly joy, celestial raiment and sustenance, and longevity spanning kalpas—yet they call this suffering.
Within the Three Realms, sun and moon hasten, cold and heat alternate, the four hundred and four illnesses afflict, laws and prisons constrain, blades and warfare rage, floods and fires consume, birth, aging, sickness, and death prevail—yet they call this bliss.
Their nature and perception differ, giving rise to delusion.

They see others observing long fasts and eating plain fare, eschewing adornment, wearing coarse garments and partaking of simple food, their forms like withered wood and their hearts like cold ash—yet do not recognize their transcendence and liberation, only desiring to inflict harm upon themselves.
They see others upholding precepts, reciting scriptures, and practicing the Dao with unwavering diligence, praying for the nation’s peace and their own liberation—yet dismiss it as pointless, thus bringing suffering upon themselves.
They see beauty and conceive slanderous thoughts.
They see others copying scriptures and sacred images yet do not generate faith; instead, they knit their brows and cast sidelong glances, joining in disparagement.
Though incapable of such practices themselves, they harbor doubt in all things.

Before the Three Sages, they raise doubts;
before the Dao altar, they raise doubts;
before the scriptures, they raise doubts;
before the true images, they raise doubts.
Such beings exhaust body and mind in ceaseless toil, their thoughts and intentions ever stirring, their resolves and imaginings giving rise to endless doubt.
When will they ever pause?
Unknowing how to seek the true principle and dispel their doubts, they indulge their karmic roots and wallow in hesitation.
Those who recognize the truth find demonic delusions naturally dispelled;
those who do not recognize it find their doubts ever deepening.
Such people, upon death, enter the Wind-and-Thunder Hell, where they receive differing retributions.

The Merciful One, moved by compassion, once more proclaims this gāthā:
Born into the world with a doubting heart,
they die and enter the Wind-and-Thunder Hell.
Their limbs severed inch by inch,
they weep in sorrow day and night.
They traverse sword trees and blade mountains,
their pain piercing bone and marrow.
Reborn in the bodies of birds and beasts,
their retribution knows no end.

Today, in this grand Dao altar, if any among you remain hesitant and doubtful, failing to sever such thoughts in this life, they will only grow in the next.
It is through the accumulation of good deeds that one attains freedom from transgression.
You have not yet escaped the cycle of birth and death, the turning wheel of rebirth.
If you receive such retribution, what regret will suffice?

Now, having encountered this Dao altar’s repentance rite, you may cleanse past transgressions.
With sincere devotion, prostrate yourselves.
The repentance master, so-and-so, knows that life is fleeting, the body uncertain.
A lifetime is but a moment; how many days are there in a hundred years?
From kalpas immeasurable, you have cast off lives and taken new births, until this present life and day.
Indulging the six senses, you have given rise to doubts.
Together with your teachers, fellow disciples, parents, uncles, brothers, and all kin—those living and deceased—you have accumulated deluded and karmic transgressions, never awakening to them.
Today, we prostrate for peace and offer this repentance rite.
With five limbs touching the earth and a single mind, listen attentively.
We bow our heads to the Merciful One, reverently honoring the true sages.

With devoted hearts, we bow to the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy, Bestower of Blessings.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves Through Sound.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Cherishes Life and Delivers Beings.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Tablet and Dharma Treasury.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Reveals the Luminous Pearl.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Vast Transformation, the Primordial Sovereign.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great One’s Dharma.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Purple Ultimate.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of True and Wondrous Form.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Immeasurable Life.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Measure.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Virtue and Dao.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, Supreme Perfected King.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Radiant Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to the Perfected.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Mysterious Response.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Pristine Perfection.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Prolongs Life.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Preserves Life and Safeguards Destiny.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, the Great One Who Saves from Suffering.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Universally Protects the Nation.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Reach.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wish.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Great Recluse Perfected.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Perfected Who Delivers from Suffering.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Great Compassionate Perfected Who Saves from Suffering.
With devoted hearts, we bow to the Great Merciful Perfected Who Eradicates Transgressions.

Today, the altar’s sponsor, so-and-so, and all present reverently beseech the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southeast, all the venerable sages, all the great perfected, all the divine youths, those who pervade the ten directions, fill the boundless cosmos, and encompass past, future, hidden, and manifest—all true sages—to practice the method of gathering thoughts.

May the repentance master, so-and-so, and all kin from nine generations and seven lineages, both living and deceased, who have given rise to doubts and received this repentance rite, attain liberation and enter the gate of faith.
May they steadfastly uphold their resolve, take aspiration as their heart, perceive both inner and outer dharmas, cultivate goodness and perform meritorious deeds, copy scriptures and make offerings to sacred images—without giving rise to doubt or encountering obstacles.

Upon beholding men and women of upright bearing, as well as all manner of good deeds in the world, one vows to forever revere, comply with joy, and encourage such persons, wishing them to attain good fruit. May this extend universally to all beings—those of the four modes of birth and six paths of existence—so that together they may transcend and realize the supreme Dao.
*One bow*

**Chapter Four: Extinguishing the Fire of the Mind**

Today, within this Daoist sanctuary, each member of the assembly directs their mind, gazing reverently toward the Merciful Honored One, repenting and extinguishing the karmic offenses of the mind’s fire.

The repentance master, so-and-so, joins palms, bows in full prostration, kneels, and listens attentively to the scriptural words. All sentient beings, from the first division of south and north, gradually recognize east and west. They cherish the fine and despise the coarse, delight in wealth and resent poverty, their convictions shaping their actions. They fail to measure short and long, covet profit and forget gratitude, estrange kin and favor outsiders. At the sight of adornments, they are insatiable; upon hearing plain truth, they react as if to a foe or enemy. Mountains are likened to sin, while wind resembles good fruit.

Moreover, their wisdom is narrow and shallow, their qi coarse and foolish. They act with abandon, clinging to their own rightness in speech. Greed knows no bounds, and vexation is endless. They regard goodness as an enemy and rejoice at evil. Though they amass vast wealth, they still claim destitution; though their karmic deeds are deep and numerous, they insist all is just. From beginning to end, they neither perceive nor comprehend. Months and years accumulate, yet they neither repent nor regret.

Doubt and delusion arise from the mind itself; ignorance, attachment, greed, and anger also spring from the mind. The mind generates anger and joy, yet ancestral roots and fundamental integrity remain unsteady. They indulge in wine and take life, reveling in their desires. Though their attire is refined—silks adorning their forms—lustful thoughts arise, bringing ruin to families and nations. They boast of youth and strength, flaunting splendor, scorning virtuous friends while clinging to wicked companions. From dawn to dusk, they wallow in confusion, sinking into night’s delirium. They fail to recognize kin or honor parents. Once deluded, they do not turn back—like fire consuming a mountain, wind and flame raging fiercely, nearly impossible to extinguish.

Wind stirs atop fire, its intent rooted in the human heart. Fire blazes, wind rises, the mind pursues, and intention follows. Foolish and common, they cling to defilement as truth. Thoughts stir the wind, blending into illusion.

Thereupon, the Merciful Honored One expounded further in verse:

> Anger’s thoughts are demonic foes,
> Words diverge, discord grows.
> Wills clash, countenances darken,
> Glowering eyes, brows slanted—
> Like the five-hued serpent’s glare.
> Death comes in an instant,
> Entangling one in hell’s torment.
> Exhort all beings to reform and repent,
> Lest they linger in prison’s snare.
> But if the great Dao-mind is aroused,
> All karmic obstacles dissolve and fade.

At that time, the Merciful Honored One addressed the assembly of universal salvation, saying: “The offenses of sentient beings arise from the mind and are extinguished by the mind. With but a single thought, all may be dispelled. Karma’s bonds cling to the body like a rope binding a bird. Though it may wander east, west, south, or north, it flies only as far as the rope allows, feeding wherever it lands, believing itself free. Yet it does not perceive the one who holds the rope, drawing it near to seize it. Only when captured does it know terror. Once in hand, its life and death rest with another. Though it cries and pleads, flapping in distress, there is no escape, no savior.

The karmic deeds of humans are likewise. Failing to restrain the six senses, they indulge the seven consciousnesses, committing all manner of evil without reflection. Karmic bonds form, and they are reborn according to their deeds. The invisible rope of karma binds their minds. Though born into wealth and nobility, or among animals, hungry ghosts, sickness, and evil destinies—wherever they transform, they find fleeting joy, believing themselves content, utterly unaware. Their former creditors, the karmic adversaries, await in the unseen realm, tracking their deeds to claim them. Disaster strikes unseen. Suffering and affliction arise, yet they do not awaken. They blame the gods, embrace false views, kill living beings in sacrifice, endure past misfortunes, and forge new enmities. In that moment, there is no savior, no recourse.

Today, all within this Daoist sanctuary, as the scriptures describe, must reflect deeply and stand in awe. The invisible rope of karma is none other than unwholesomeness. The suffering of rebirth is wrought by the mind. Without repentance, how can it be dispelled? Just as form and shadow arise from ignorance and vanish with its cessation, one must cultivate shame and remorse, purifying body and mind, and repent with utmost sincerity.

The repentance master, so-and-so, from beginningless kalpas until this present life, having cast off and received countless bodies—along with masters, teachers, disciples, superiors, inferiors, parents, siblings, and all kin—has, through the fire of the mind, created karmic conditions beyond measure or reckoning. Today, prostrating in reverence for peace and offering this repentance rite, they cast themselves fully to the ground, listen with single-minded devotion, bow their head to the Merciful Honored One, and pay homage to the true sages.

With devoted heart, they bow to the Jade Clarity Heavenly Worthy who bestows blessings.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to cries and saves from suffering.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who cherishes life and delivers beings.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of universally manifest virtue.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy whose mercy pervades the three realms.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms the six paths.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of flying cinnabar and radiant extremity.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Grove and Primordial Cavern.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of inexhaustible numinous response.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of wisdom and diligent progress.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Floating Netherworld.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of eternal salvation and mercy.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of perfect wisdom.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of eternal ascent to the morning heavens.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of luminous wonder.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of enlightenment.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of vast salvation.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of all wonders.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Subtlety.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of wondrous understanding.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Dharma Ocean.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who preserves life and protects destiny.

With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great One who saves from suffering.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of universal mercy who protects the realm.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of boundless expanse.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of carefree joy.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to one’s wishes.

With devoted heart, they bow to the Perfected of Wondrous Conduct.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Perfected of Wondrous Form.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Perfected of Great Mercy who saves from suffering.
With devoted heart, they bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion who removes transgressions.

Today, the master of repentance of this Dao altar, so-and-so, together with the great assembly, reverently beseech the Most High Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southeast, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected, all the Great Divine Youths, who pervade the ten directions, fill the boundless cosmos, and abide in all times—past and future, hidden and manifest—with the heart of the Great Dao, to manifest the power of non-action, so that the karmic offenses born of the master of repentance’s mind-fire may, by virtue of this repentance, be extinguished.

From this day forward, past faults having been repented, may no new transgressions be committed. If one encounters another who awakens the true and upright heart, cultivating all good fruits, regardless of whether they have attained fulfillment or are still preparing, may we turn our minds and thoughts with joy and humility, clearly advancing that person. May their vows for good conditions, the deliverance of all beings in the Dharma Realm, and ourselves, our nine generations of ancestors and seven lineages, the four kinds of birth and six paths of existence, all together attain liberation and return to the Great Dao.

One bow.

*End of the Second Scroll of the Most High’s Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Dissolving Disasters and the Nine Dark Realms*

*Beginning of the Third Scroll of the Most High’s Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Dissolving Disasters and the Nine Dark Realms*

The Venerable Left Immortal Lord Ge Xuan of the Great Ultimate has compiled this text.

**Chapter One: Severing Afflictions**

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, each with focused mind, reverently faces the Merciful Honored One, repenting and severing the karmic offenses of afflictions.

The repentant master, with gathered mind and kneeling in reverence, listens attentively to the scriptural words:

All sentient beings, born from the shelter of their parents’ wombs, may grow in wealth or poverty in youth, rise to nobility or fall into lowliness, commit a single evil or a hundred evils, be male or female—yet they do not comprehend the cycles of rebirth, nor discern its beginning or end.

For afflictions exist. Afflictions arise from clinging to views; clinging to views arises from inversion; inversion arises from delusion; delusion arises from doubt; doubt arises from manifold sufferings; and manifold sufferings arise from all karmic deeds.

Once karmic deeds are created, impermanence presses upon them, leaving no freedom.

The Merciful Honored One addressed Universal Salvation, saying: "Afflictions are what cause sentient beings to take form and dwell in the human world. Not only do the rich and noble, the poor and lowly, men and women all seek clothing and food, but they must also pursue the conditions of life, provide for their needs, sustain their daily use, be bound by royal laws, constrained by hierarchies of honor and humility, unite with kin, and distinguish between love and attachment—even unto old age, sickness, and death. Or, failing to complete their allotted lifespan, they drift with their karma, flowing into the Three Evil Realms, gradually distancing themselves from the paths of humans and heavens. Unaware of the suffering of impermanence, they do not awaken.

Yet those with wisdom and clarity, who embody the absence of thought, who possess insight and perceive delusion, who discern doubt—do not regard these as suffering. They abide in ease and joy, following their thoughts to generate intentions, and their intentions to create karma. They cling to views as truth, invert right and wrong, conjure delusions in response to circumstances, and pursue desires with doubt. Indulging the six senses, they commit sins as numerous as the grains of the Ganges; neglecting the three karmic actions, they sow seeds for boundless hells. All this stems from afflictions, which defile body and mind.

With a body, there are afflictions; without a body, there are no afflictions. Since afflictions exist, one must cultivate and practice.

Universal Salvation asked: "What good must be cultivated to depart from afflictions?"

The Merciful Honored One replied: "Extinguish the three karmic actions and establish the three virtuous practices: the virtuous practice of the mind, the virtuous practice of the body, and the virtuous practice of speech.

First, the virtuous practice of the mind: (1) not coveting, (2) not harboring anger, and (3) not being deluded. Be pure and self-disciplined, desire little and know contentment, restrain greed and abandon the pursuit of profit, be compassionate and patient, gentle and forgiving, subdue anger and remain free from resentment, contemplate the subtle and abide in stillness, comprehend existence and penetrate non-existence, and with wisdom, clearly understand all dharmas. This is called the virtuous practice of the mind.

Next, the virtuous practice of the body: (1) not killing, (2) not stealing, and (3) not engaging in improper sexual conduct. Be benevolent and wise, broadly giving alms, pitying all beings, saving lives and delivering the dying, humble and yielding, taking nothing that is not rightfully yours, and relinquishing body, life, and wealth without reluctance. Be truly pure and clean, far from improper conduct, free from lust and desire, and keep the mind from dissipation. This is called the virtuous practice of the body.

As for the virtuous practice of speech: (1) not lying, (2) not using flowery or deceptive language, (3) not engaging in divisive speech, and (4) not uttering abusive words. Speak truthfully, without falsehood; let your words be genuine, free from embellishment; let your expressions be balanced, upright, and without duplicity; do not create divisions or take sides; let your voice be harmonious, soft, and clear; skillfully expound the Dharma and recite the profound verses. This is called the virtuous practice of speech.

When the three practices are virtuous, there is no doubt. Without doubt, there is no delusion. Without delusion, there is no inversion. Without inversion, there is no clinging to views. Without clinging to views, there are no afflictions. Without afflictions, there are no manifold sufferings. Without manifold sufferings, there are no karmic deeds. Without karmic deeds, there is peace and joy, and one enters the Dao of Non-Action."

Upon hearing the teaching of the three virtuous practices, Universal Salvation realized that all sentient beings could be cured of the illness of afflictions. Praising the Merciful Honored One, he composed this verse:

I bow to the true Dharma Lord among the sages,
Who expounds the medicine for the afflictions of beings.
The priceless treasure within the hearts of beings
Is ever plundered by the six thieves.
The arrow of anger pierces the heart,
The lock of ignorance and attachment has no key.
The shackles of self and others confine the body,
While the demonic thoughts of the six relations plunder it.
Now, relying on the three virtuous practices to drive them away,
For endless kalpas, the four marks shall not cling.

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, along with the repentant master, having heard of these afflictions, must deeply reflect. For countless kalpas, we have witnessed all sufferings. What was once deemed joy is now suffering in this life, yet we cannot awaken, cannot sever afflictions. Instead, they increase, entangling us in past karma, trapping us in this illusory world, obscuring the Great Dao, and preventing us from awakening to the true essence. Afflictions and calamities arise daily, binding us ever tighter.

Now, having encountered the scriptural teachings of the Merciful Honored One, who broadly expounds the Dharma gates and elucidates afflictions, we are lifted from ignorance. May all sentient beings awaken.

The repentant master, from beginningless kalpas until the present kalpa, in this life and today, along with nine generations of ancestors and seven lineages, both the living and the deceased, and all kin—having indulged the three karmic actions of the body, the four of speech, and the ten of the mind, from beginningless ignorance—have created the Three Poisons, the Four Destinies, the Five Hindrances, the Six Dusts, the Seven Leaks, the Eight Defilements, the Nine Knots, and the Ten Entanglements, leaving us without freedom. Afflictions have confined us in cages, casting us into the currents of transmigration.

Today, encountering this repentance ritual is like the sun at noon, the moon at night, the blind regaining sight, the mute speaking, the deaf hearing, the guilty receiving pardon. Prostrating with the five limbs touching the ground, with a single mind, I bow to the Merciful Honored One and reverently pay homage to the true sages.

With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Jade Clarity Heavenly Worthy who bestows blessings.

With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to Cries and Saves from Suffering.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Myriad Blessings of Mysterious Reality.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Flies Through the World.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Yang’s Transformations.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Turns My Body.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Mirror-Pure Heart.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Lofty Mystery.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Peace and Stillness.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Gate of Mystery.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Purity.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Liberates from Birth and Death.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Adornment.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Contemplates the Wondrous Body.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Universal Covering.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Lofty Mystery.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Protects the Spirits.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Turns the Dharma.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of True Mystery.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Flourishing Yang.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life Preservation.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Protects the Realm.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Reach.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Left Mysterious Perfected.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Right Mysterious Perfected.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Perfected of Great Compassion Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere mind, I pay homage to the Perfected of Great Compassion Who Removes Transgressions.

Today, the patrons of this ritual arena, together with the great assembly, reverently beseech the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southern Realm, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Immortals and Great Perfected, all the Heavenly Hosts and Divine Youths—pervading the ten directions, filling the boundless cosmos, past and future, manifest and hidden, all true sages. May they together extend their virtuous power to save and protect all beings. May the repentance sponsor, so-and-so, forever sever afflictions, depart from defilement, and for past and present lives, generate virtuous power to assist those in the Three Wretched Realms, forever escape evil destinies, and may all of us attain rebirth in the pure and joyful lands of the ten directions. May all afflictions, habitual sins, and karmic causes, through this repentance, be wholly dissolved. From this day forward, may we practice the true appearance of the Dao, without laziness or negligence. May we attain the power of wisdom and expedient means, dispel all calamities, safeguard the realm, liberate the six paths—both hidden and manifest—deliver the distant souls of the nine generations and three lineages, and together escape the cages of confinement, ascending together to the shore of the Dao.

One bow.

**Second Section: Repentance of the Dusts and Toils of Suffering**

Today, in this ritual arena, each person directs their mind, gazing up to the Merciful Honored One, repenting the sins of all the dusts and toils of suffering. The repentance sponsor, so-and-so, collects their mind, surrenders their life, takes refuge, and listens attentively to the scriptural words.

All beings, from the moment of birth and the formation of their bodies, bear the round heavens upon their heads and tread the square earth beneath their feet. Their flesh is foul and filthy, their bones and flesh rank and base. They do not avoid the stars and constellations, constantly offending wind and rain, accumulating these yang transgressions, inevitably incurring yin offenses. Within heaven and earth, regardless of high or low status, the categories of sins are boundless. Some sins arise from the three karmas, some from the six roots, some from the inner mind’s perversity, some from attachment to external conditions. Some arise from the Three Poisons giving rise to the Four Perversions, some from the three karmas generating the one hundred and eight afflictions, some from the five views producing the sixty-two views, some from the ten evils giving rise to forty kinds of evil, some from the six senses generating the eighty-four thousand gates of dusts and toils. Or from a single thought in a single moment, the Four Perversions arise, the one hundred and eight afflictions are generated, the sixty-two views are established, the forty kinds of evil are committed, and the eighty-four thousand dusts and toils of suffering are created. How much more so for a day, a month, a year—arising from thoughts and intentions? How much more so after passing through kalpas, giving rise to manifold sins? Thus, the toils of suffering follow one after another, without end.

Now, the root of these sins arises from three kinds. The Universal Savior says: What are the three? The first is vexation, the second is karma, the third is thought. Due to these three, one cannot perceive the sages nor the wondrous and excellent affairs of humans and heavens. If in a single day, a single hour, a single thought, one awakens to these three hindrances—even the three karmas, six roots, one hundred and eight afflictions, sixty-two views, forty kinds of evil, and eighty-four thousand dusts and toils of suffering—all may be purified.

Yet these beings do not believe my words, do not follow the scriptural teachings, do not know how to resolve enmity, do not seek liberation. They accumulate evil as numerous as the sands, their sins filling heaven and earth. The Three Poisons, Ten Evils, Five Views, Six Dusts, Six Defilements, Six Entrances—these give rise to uninterrupted karmic offenses. Or they commit incomplete practices, sever karmic actions through faith, slander the Heavenly Worthies, revile the Three Treasures, destroy the worthy and sagely, ruin the true Dharma, disbelieve in sin and merit. They commit the Ten Evil Karmas: delusion turning truth into falsehood, foolish and confused karma; disloyalty to the sovereign, treacherous and flattering karma; unfilial conduct toward parents, rebellious karma; disrespect toward honored teachers, irreverent karma; betrayal of friends, unrighteous karma; committing the Four Grave Offenses that obstruct the sagely Dao; violating pure precepts, breaking the Eight Observances; transgressing the Five Precepts and Seven Hindrances, incomplete and flawed karma; disbelieving the Ten Precepts, regardless of severity, defiling thoughts with expedient means; failing to observe the six long fasts and ten monthly fasts, inconsistent cultivation; improper conduct within the various dignified deportments; the two thousand four hundred subtle dignified deportments; hindering the cultivation of bodily precepts, mental concentration, and wisdom; committing various offenses during the spring and autumn Eight Kings’ festivals; engaging in manifold evils, violating the six dignified deportments; lacking compassion toward suffering beings, unfeeling and unmindful karma; failing to rescue or aid, lacking salvation and protection; harboring jealousy, generating self-and-other karma; unequal treatment of enemies and loved ones; indulging in the Five Desires without weariness, failing to renounce; seeking ease through clothing, food, gardens, baths, and ponds, generating frivolous karma; or directing leaky merit toward the Three Sages, obstructing the path of leaving the household. Such karmas are boundless and immeasurable, impossible to fully recount.

Universal Salvation asked, "With what mind should one act to extinguish these karmic obstructions and transgressions?"

The Merciful Honored One replied, "First, one must arouse seven kinds of wholesome minds as expedient means to achieve their eradication. What are the seven?

1. Shame and remorse,
2. Fear and dread,
3. Weariness and renunciation,
4. The arising of the supreme wholesome mind,
5. Equal regard for enemies and loved ones,
6. Mindfulness of repaying the kindness of the Heavenly Worthy, the sovereign, the master, and parents,
7. Contemplation that all delusive thoughts and the nature of transgressions are empty.

If one fails to cultivate these wholesome minds and does not arise repentance, calamities will afflict distant ancestors, misfortunes will taint future generations, and in this present life, one will suffer blindness, deafness, and chronic illness. At death, one will fall into the nine dark hells, remaining for ten thousand kalpas before rebirth—emaciated, ghostly, and inhuman in form."

Then the Merciful Honored One spoke this verse:

If one harbors an unwholesome mind,
And without cause commits manifold karmas—
Even a single thread or hair,
Or countless billions—
At death, one enters the eighteen hells,
Enduring every kind of suffering.
Later reborn among starving tigers,
Forever denied a full meal.
Even if one gains a human body,
One is slain by water, fire, or the sword,
Or suffers chronic illness,
Madness, or epilepsy.

Today, in this grand Dharma assembly, as the scripture declares, we ought to be deeply terrified. Within this body lie such toils and afflictions—how, through kalpas uncounted, could we have awakened to them, shrouded as we are in ignorance? Some commit the ten evils themselves; others teach the ten evils; still others praise the ten evils or openly advance them. With every thought and every moment, one dwells upon the ten evils. Even for a single hair’s weight of transgression, one will one day receive its retribution—how could remorse then avail?

Now, we must strive with diligence and repent with vigor. Whether in the six paths or among the four modes of birth, seeing those who suffer or are yet to suffer, I now generate the aspiration that all may equally attain liberation.

The repentance sponsor, so-and-so, prostrates in reverence, dedicating this repentance rite for peace and to offer posthumous merit. With five limbs touching the earth and a single mind, he bows his head to the Merciful Honored One and pays homage to the true sages.

With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy who bestows blessings.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to cries and saves from suffering.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Mysterious Perfection Heavenly Worthy of myriad blessings.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms and delivers the Dragon Kings.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the ten-thousand-kalpa turning wheel.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthies of the ten directions who respond to all names.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy beyond thought and discussion.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who eliminates afflictions.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of lofty and far-reaching virtue.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of dust-like marvels.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy whose body radiates the Dharma.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy whose wisdom is invincible.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the profound and ultimate Dharma.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Supreme Purity Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who advances the Dao.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms and responds.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who knows suffering.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms beings.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of faith and wisdom.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who delivers from distress.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who transcends immortals.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who saves from suffering.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who ensures long life and preserves destiny.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of universal compassion who protects the realm.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy of carefree joy.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to wishes.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Heavenly Worthy whose merit is like the ocean.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Perfected One of wondrous efficacy.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Perfected One of profound understanding.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Perfected One of great compassion who saves from suffering.
With sincere mind, he pays homage to the Perfected One of great mercy who extracts transgressions.

Today, the sponsor of this Dharma assembly and all present reverently aspire that the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the southern direction, all the honored ones and sages, all the great perfected ones, all the great divine immortals, all the great celestial immortals, and all the great youths—pervading the ten directions, filling the boundless cosmos, past and future, responding to every name—all true sages, may with the Great Mysterious Water wash away the karmic afflictions, transgressions, and toils of the repentance sponsor, so-and-so, his parents who gave him life, his masters who transmitted the Dharma and conferred ordination, his uncles, brothers, male and female kin, and all sentient beings bound by present and past conditions, infinite and immeasurable.

By the power of this repentance, may we rely on the power of the Dao, the power of the true sages, the power of the repentance rite, the power of cause and effect, the inconceivable power, and the power of merit, so that all may be extinguished, all views awakened, and the profound principle thoroughly understood. May all beings, without exception, transcend the toils and transgressions of worldly dust, realize the unconditioned, and take refuge in the Great Dao.

**First Prostration**

**Chapter Three: Returning to Faith and Reverence**

Today, in this grand Dharma assembly, each person directs their mind upward to the Merciful Honored One, repenting the transgressions of irreverence and lack of faith.

The repentance sponsor, so-and-so, bows his head and kneels in reverence, listening attentively to the scripture’s words: All sentient beings, creating evil causes and acting inappropriately, harbor minds like raging fire, burning fiercely without discrimination. Whether ugly or fair, their thoughts are sharp as blades, their severity sparing neither strong nor weak. Over time, days accumulate into months, months into years, yet they fail to cultivate even a moment’s goodness. Day by day, their transgressions grow, and their enmities multiply, increasing their suffering karma and consigning them to eternal submersion.

From past conditions to present, from kalpa to kalpa, with every thought and intention, they generate irreverence and lack of faith, slandering the Three Sages, defaming the Three Sages, belittling the Three Sages, defiling the Three Sages, mocking the Three Sages, cursing the Three Sages, reviling the Three Sages, deceiving the Three Sages, arrogantly scorning the Three Sages, contemptuously deriding the Three Sages, devouring the offerings to the Three Sages, deluding the Three Sages, encroaching upon the Three Sages, wasting and damaging the possessions of the Three Sages.

They disparage scriptures and repentance texts, debate their authenticity, recklessly discuss gains and losses, obstinately argue right and wrong, distinguish shallow and deep, and collectively criticize strengths and weaknesses. Their appearance is unclean, their clothing is unclean, their hands and feet are unclean, their sandals are unclean, their breath is unclean.

They drink wine and eat meat, consuming pungent and spicy foods, uttering foul language, their hearts lacking reverence. Some do not wash their hands, some do not burn incense, some do not rinse their mouths, some do not bathe, yet they enter the sacred altar or approach the Dharma seat. Some go to the Daoist sanctuary to listen to the Dharma and sutras, pressing close to the revered images, defiling the true sages—divine immortals, spirit persons, jade lads and jade maidens, vajra guardian kings, heavenly marshals, and mighty warriors, the protective and awe-inspiring deities.

Some, in the presence of the Heavenly Worthy, the great Dao, the scriptures and Dharma, or the monastic Dharma-body, display arrogance and disdain, refusing to bow in reverence or prostrate in sincerity. Some lie down while listening to the great virtuous masters expound the Three Caverns’ Mahayana scriptures. Some, reeking of wine, meat, and pungent foods, ride in carriages or on horses straight into the sanctuary, approaching the Heavenly Worthy to read or recite scriptures and repentance texts. Some, upon seeing others observe fasts and receive precepts, refuse to believe or follow, dismissing them as hypocritical. Some bring men and women together into the sanctuary to listen to the Dharma and sutras, speaking loudly and disrupting the assembly. Some, when speaking or forming intentions, first debate right and wrong, comparing merits and virtues. Some rely on the Three Treasures to cunningly seek wealth. Some misuse the Dharma teachings to deceive men and women. Some embezzle the wealth of the Three Treasures to sustain themselves. Some threaten or coerce monastics, seeking their faults to extort their possessions and support their families. Some carry scriptures and images into the marketplace to preach. Some, while traveling, falsely claim merit to gather wealth for themselves. Some pawn scriptures and images, lending them for profit to provide for their kin. Some, when expounding the Dharma from high seats, take the offerings for their own use. Some, without studying the scriptures, precepts, talismans, or ritual texts, set themselves up as masters, accepting offerings. Some indiscriminately recruit disciples, not selecting the worthy, and transmit the scriptures and Dharma, leaking true secrets. Some, without following the regulations, receive teachings from masters, acting on their own whims to alter or augment the scriptures and Dharma. Some expose sacred images to dust and filth, damaging the permanent abode. Some let halls and temples collapse, defiling the scriptures and Dharma. Some destroy banners, lamps, and merit offerings, disrespecting the radiant countenances. Some steal precious scriptures, treating them like common texts. Some privately copy them without care, mixing them with mundane books, showing no reverence. Some place beds and pillows where they sleep beside them. Some, in their chambers, leave foul and disorderly messes, handling pungent foods while reciting true scriptures. Some betray the Dao and their masters, violating their vows.

All such intentions and mental formations transgress the bright statutes and violate the precepts. These offenses are measureless and boundless. If one commits even the slightest act of irreverence or disbelief, in this life their family will be incomplete, their departed kin will suffer, and they themselves will receive the karmic retribution of leprosy. Upon death, they will fall into the Nine Dark Hells, enduring ten thousand kalpas before rebirth, where they will take the form of wild beasts.

Then, the Compassionate Worthy, for the sake of those yet to awaken, spoke these verses:

Born into the world without reverence,
Defiling the true forms of the Dao.
The lofty sages and immortal perfected,
Spirit persons and divine beings,
Jade lads and jade maidens,
Vajra guardians and mighty warriors,
Attendant protective deities—
All such sacred forms,
If damaged or treated with contempt,
Defiled and disrespected,
Slandering monastics,
Speaking without propriety,
Striking, scolding, oppressing, or neglecting,
Committing lewd acts or mocking,
Arrogant and scornful,
Debating the scriptures and Dharma,
Forcibly arguing right and wrong,
Breaking fasts and precepts,
Stealing the wealth of the Three Treasures,
All manner of irreverence—
Upon death, they fall into the Nine Dark Hells,
Enduring the eighteen realms of suffering.
Their feet tread upon mountains of knives,
Their hands grasp trees of swords.
Naked, they embrace bronze pillars,
Their bare bodies lie upon iron beds.
Fire mountains rest upon their heads,
Iron rods press upon their backs.
Hungry, they eat burning coals;
Thirsty, they drink molten bronze.
Boiling cauldrons seethe and scald,
Fire chariots burn their bodies.
Pounded by pestles, ground by mills,
Hung upside down or stood on their heads,
Sawn apart, sliced by blades,
Needles pierce their limbs and joints.
Narrow gorges crush their bodies,
Frigid ice severs their sinews and bones.
Scorching embers chase them east and west,
Leaping and stumbling without rest.
Abiding in foul and stinking places,
Drowning in dark and turbid waters,
Poured into the four rivers,
Evil birds peck out their eyes.
Bronze dogs bite and tear,
Poisonous snakes compete to devour.
Ox-headed demons break their spines,
Dying and reviving ten thousand times a day.
Unbearable pain—
In life, they suffer leprosy.
Today, the great assembly in this sanctuary,
Hearing these verses as the scriptures describe,
Should deeply reflect in alarm and sorrow.
How can one awaken to such karmic causes?
If such sins are committed, retribution is inescapable;
When remorse comes, it will be too late.
Each should diligently advance,
Sincerely repent their transgressions.
If, within the six paths, one takes the four forms of birth—
Great or small bodies—
They devour one another.
If retribution has not yet been received,
Now, with reverence,
May all be liberated.

The repentance master [Name] prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text for the deliverance of the departed. With five limbs touching the ground, wholeheartedly they arise in devotion:
Prostrating to the Compassionate Worthy, reverently bowing to the true sages.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Jade Clarity Bestowing Blessings Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Hearer of Cries Saving from Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Mysterious Perfection Ten Thousand Blessings Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Cavernous Void Transforming Title Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Boundless Response Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Attaining the Dao Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Constant Joy Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Wondrous Dharma Joy Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Constant Savior of Beings Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Unchanging Form Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Dharma Abode Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Mysterious Palace Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Responsive Transformation Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Great Void Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Dao Ocean Heavenly Worthy.

With sincere devotion, they bow to the Azure Heavens Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Constant Dao Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Subduing Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Great One Savior from Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Longevity and Life-Preserving Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Universally Compassionate Protector of the Realm Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Carefree and Joyous Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Wish-Fulfilling Rebirth Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Ocean of Merit Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Wisdom Treasury.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Vast Faith.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Great Compassionate Savior from Suffering Perfected.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Great Merciful Remover of Transgressions Perfected.

Today, the patrons of this Dao altar and all the assembly reverently pray to the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southern Realm, to all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected, all the Heavenly Immortals, all the Great Divine Youths, all the Great Dragon Spirits—pervading the ten directions, filling the boundless void, manifesting and concealed, all true and sacred beings.
We humbly pray that the realms of suffering be swept away, and the roots of evil be eradicated.
The penitent, so-and-so, from the time of this bodily existence, for all transgressions committed, now repents with utmost sincerity, and with a single thought, beseeches their dissolution.
From this day forward, may we constantly hold faith and reverence, reflect upon past wrongs, and purify the heart in remorse.
May we, in future lives, turn the wheel without cease, attain eternal longevity, and may the departed souls all ascend to the realms of rebirth.
May our present kin ever dwell in blessed lands.
May we realize the formless, and swiftly ascend to the sacred fruit.

One bow.

**Chapter Four: Removing Obstacles**

Today, in this Dao altar, each member of the assembly directs their mind, reverently facing the Compassionate Venerable, repenting the sins of obstacles.
The penitent, so-and-so, kneels with utmost sincerity, attentively listening to the scriptural words:
All sentient beings, through the mind of greed and desire, arouse the six consciousnesses, the six dusts, the six desires, and the six defilements, giving rise to deluded and false thoughts, generating all manner of obstacles.
Clearly committing sins, yet the mind remains unaware.
Repeatedly doing wrong, yet words still claim righteousness.
All due to ignorance—how can one recognize transgressions?
Only seeing others’ faults while praising one’s own virtues, how can one distinguish others’ reverence?
Unaware of my own inferiority, I divide bodies into noble and base, high and low, never equal.
The noble dwell in lofty halls and towering chambers, draped in purple and girded with gold, with vermilion walls and pepper-scented chambers, jade terraces and cinnabar railings.
The base are barefoot servants, following behind and leading ahead, their voices faint, their demeanor lowly.
The wealthy wear light furs and ride fat horses, feasting on fine delicacies, their words resonant as bells, their hearts vast as the sea.
The poor are consumed by hunger and cold, neglecting rites and propriety, their words and deeds at odds, their actions improper.
In these bodily karmas, how can one uphold and maintain? The transgressions multiply—who can awaken?
Yet within the world’s snare, the mind of obstruction arises.
Obstructing others from taking refuge in the Three Treasures and the sacred teachings of the Heavenly Worthy.
Obstructing others from believing in and revering the scriptures and Dao of the Great Way.
Obstructing others from loyalty to the sovereign.
Obstructing others from serving and honoring masters, superiors, and those of the Dharma.
Obstructing others from filial piety toward parents.
Obstructing others from turning scriptures and practicing the Dao for the realm.
Obstructing others from eliminating calamities and seeking blessings for the family.
Obstructing others from diligent service to the realm.
Obstructing others from toiling for the family.
Obstructing others from arousing the mind for the supreme Dao.
Obstructing others from chanting and singing the Dao.
Obstructing others from upholding precepts and maintaining purity.
Obstructing others from liberating lives.
Obstructing others from reciting scriptures to cultivate goodness.
Obstructing others from enduring humiliation and bearing shame.
Obstructing others from joyful almsgiving.
Obstructing others from diligent cultivation.
Obstructing others from dwelling in mountains and valleys, practicing qi absorption and exhalation.
Obstructing others from seeking the Dao and pursuing ascension.
Obstructing others from copying scriptures and adorning scroll ribbons.
Obstructing others from sculpting sacred images to inspire faith.
Obstructing others from constructing numinous altars and Daoist abbeys, and inviting others to reside and maintain them.
Obstructing others from preparing vegetarian feasts and making offerings.
Obstructing others from disciplining the body and refining conduct, polishing the heart and nature.
Obstructing others from making offerings to the Dharma body.
Obstructing others from reverent incense offerings and cultivation.
Obstructing others from equality and non-duality.
Obstructing others from leaving worldly defilements and forever removing afflictions.
Obstructing others from repenting and confessing transgressions to escape calamities.
Obstructing others from maintaining the altar’s incense and lamps day and night.
Obstructing others from cultivating wisdom and intelligence through constant study of scriptures.
Obstructing others from learning arts to adorn their name and body.
Obstructing others through affection and love.
Obstructing others through bonds of sentiment.
Obstructing others through profit and aid.
Obstructing others through instruction and guidance.
Obstructing others through greed and attachment.
Obstructing others through disdain and contempt.
Obstructing others through indulgence and falsehood.
Obstructing others from all manner of good deeds—even the slightest good deed of another.
Once a good deed arises, one must not arbitrarily create obstacles.
Those who create obstacles, for their own sake, do not recognize that good deeds are the path to liberation from worldly dust. Unable to practice themselves, they instead create mutual obstructions.
For every obstacle or hindrance created, one incurs boundless and immeasurable sins, causing one’s present self to suffer old age, illness, solitude, and unfulfilled wishes, and upon death, to enter the Nine Dark Hells, enduring all sufferings. Only after ten thousand kalpas may one be reborn as a fish or turtle, subjected to human carving and slicing.
Without repentance, there is no means of liberation.

At that time, the Compassionate Venerable, saving all sentient beings, spoke this verse:
*In past lives, without a good heart,*
*Obstructing all things.*
*Speaking dark and deceitful words,*
*Claiming past wrongs as the path.*
*Bonds of affection and love,*
*Greed, attachment, and contempt—*
*Clinging together in evil,*
*Upon death, entering the Flowing Sands Hell.*
*Even if reborn as a human,*
*One suffers poverty, cold, and solitude.*
*In this life, enduring long illness,*
*Good medicine turns to poison.*

Today, in this Dao altar, each member of the assembly directs their mind, hearing this verse, truly filled with sorrow and grief.
If one bears such sins of obstruction, when retribution comes, it will be difficult to repent and withdraw.
Now, we must vow to dissolve and remove these karmic obstacles.
The penitent, so-and-so, prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text, fully prostrating with the five limbs, wholeheartedly making this vow.

We bow our heads to the Merciful Honored One, reverently paying homage to the True Saints.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy Who Descends with Blessings.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering at the Sound of Cries.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Mysterious Truth Heavenly Worthy of Myriad Blessings.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Embodies Transformation.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Transmits the Teachings.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Victorious Goodness.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Expounds the Dharma.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Original Radiance.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Treasured Virtue.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Soars through Clouds.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Rides the Scenery.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Dharmakāya’s Power.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy, King of Virtue and Illumination.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Wondrous Transformative Sound.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Constantly Protects the World.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Power.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Immaculate Mind.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy, King of Merit and Virtue.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Unbounded Sovereign Power.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Great One Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Ensures Longevity and Preserves Life.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Protects the Realm.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Vows.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Reach.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy, Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Perfected Person of Wondrous Faith.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Perfected Person of Wondrous Sound.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Perfected Person of Great Compassion Who Saves from Suffering.
With devoted hearts, we reverently pay homage to the Perfected Person of Great Compassion Who Removes Transgressions.

Today, the penitent and the entire assembly of this Dao altar, gazing upward, vow to the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Southern Realm, to all the Venerable Ones and Saints, all the Great Divine Immortals, all the Great Perfected Beings, all the Great Perfected Persons, and all the Divine Youths—pervading the ten directions, filling the boundless cosmos, past and future, hidden and manifest, all True Saints.

By the inconceivable power of the great Dao, the subtle and wondrous power of merit and virtue, and the responsive power of the Merciful Honored One’s name, may the penitent’s nine generations of ancestors, fellow masters and teachers, disciples and dharma companions, as well as parents, uncles, brothers, and all living and deceased family members—across both this life and the next—have all their heavy karmic obstructions, vast as mountains and deep as the sea, dissolved and eradicated through this act of repentance.

May they rely on the power of the divine immortals, the dragon deities, the Three Saints, and the Perfected Persons to forever extinguish these obstacles. May those who have sunk into suffering ascend to rebirth, free from further affliction. From this day forward, may they, upon seeing others cultivate all manner of good deeds, never again generate obstacles. May the seeds of goodness grow ever stronger, universally delivering all sentient beings to together transcend into the Pure Land.

One bow.

*Thus concludes the third scroll of The Supreme Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Disaster Dispelling and the Nine Dark Realms.*
*Beginning of the fourth scroll of The Supreme Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Disaster Dispelling and the Nine Dark Realms.*

*Compiled by the Left Immortal of the Great Ultimate, Ge Xuan.*

**Chapter One: Ceasing Anger and Resentment**

Today, the entire assembly of this Dao altar, each directing their minds, gazing upward to the Merciful Honored One, repent for the karmic offenses of anger and resentment. The penitent, so-and-so, collects their thoughts, kneels in reverence, and listens to the scriptural words:

All sentient beings, arising from clinging views, give rise to anger and resentment. The source of anger and resentment lies solely in the mind. When the mind generates anger and resentment, it is like fire and wind. When wind and fire blaze fiercely, they soon subside of their own accord. Yet these sentient beings, unable to let go, cling to foolish views, giving rise to anger and resentment. Sometimes, from greed and attachment, the six senses are stirred, defiled by the six dusts, and the thought of anger arises. Or they resent the Heavenly Worthies of the great Dao, deeming their words lacking in truth and uprightness, uttering only frivolous speech, ever devoid of faith. Or they resent heaven and earth, cursing the cold and heat, embracing only ignorance, unashamed before the vastness that covers and supports all. Or they resent the sun, moon, and stars, exposing their bodies without shame, unabashed before their illumination, constantly complaining of their slowness or swiftness. Or they resent the scriptures, dismissing them as empty words, failing to study and explore them, often slandering or praising them. Or they resent their parents, neglecting filial duties, utterly lacking in devotion and care, ungrateful for their toil. Or they resent their brothers, lacking the bond of shared roots, treating them as outsiders, their affection no deeper than distant friends. Or they resent their family members, failing to cultivate kindness and gentleness, deficient in respect toward superiors and unrestrained in their treatment of subordinates. Or they resent the precepts and fasts, performing them without reverence, frequently violating them, lacking in sincerity and devotion. Or they resent the ruler, failing to praise the peace of the realm, harboring thoughts of rebellion and murder, not establishing loyalty and goodness. Or they resent those who expound the teachings, refusing to listen to good causes, uttering only harsh words, confounding truth and falsehood. Or they resent the temples and monasteries, failing to revere and support them, engaging in excessive slander, unwilling to contribute to their construction and maintenance. Or they resent the departed, lacking in memorial rites, not creating good causes to aid their journey in the dark realms. Or they resent the divine principles, neglecting sacrifices, instead trusting in heretical shamans, engaging in licentiousness and killing. Or they resent the elderly, failing to show filial piety, devoid of compassion, attributing their condition to karmic retribution. Or they resent the prisons, not examining the circumstances, constantly speaking of hardships, aiding in the addition of shackles and restraints. Or they resent the poor and lowly, wrongfully oppressing them, making it difficult for them to voice their grievances, unmindful of their hunger and cold, perpetually subjecting them to suffering. Or they resent the birds and beasts, unmindful of their feathers and fur, only indulging in greed and cruelty, seeking only to slaughter and cook them. Or they resent their servants, unable to endure their lowly status, only knowing how to inflict suffering.

Such anger and resentment—whether already committed or not, whether toward kin or strangers, whether by men or women, whether by humans or non-humans—when the mind conceives and the intention arises, giving rise to anger and resentment, it is like wood giving birth to fire, fire arising naturally. The transgression deepens, the fault becomes most grave, and the departed ancestors remain confined in the dark realms, unable to attain liberation.

Thereupon, the Merciful Honored One, observing these sentient beings recklessly indulging in anger and resentment, sighs with compassion and speaks this verse:

All you men and women,
Listen carefully and reflect well.
Before the Heavenly Worthy of the great Dao,
Never give rise to anger and resentment.

Before kings and parents,
In scripture halls and Daoist sanctuaries,
Beside preachers who expound and praise the Dharma,
Never give rise to anger and resentment.
Should you see renunciates,
Or virtuous ones who revere goodness of heart,
Who give alms to the poor,
Or prisoners and wayfarers,
Who tread upon the orphaned and exposed,
The sick and the fatherless—
Yet still, some men and women
May conceive anger and resentment.
Like wood giving birth to fire,
Fire arises naturally in return.
Only by relinquishing clinging views
And awakening to the impermanent Dao
can this be overcome.

Thereupon, the Merciful Honored One spoke again:
If sentient beings commit even a single act of anger or resentment,
In this life they will suffer from wind and perverse illnesses.
At death, they enter the Eight Cold and Eight Hot Hells,
Then pass through the Needle-Peak Hell,
Where only after ten thousand kalpas are they reborn—
Their bodies as frogs, toads, or *hóu* fish.
Even if they return to the human realm,
They remain dull-witted, clumsy, and malevolent.
Without repentance, they sink forever into darkness.

Thus, the Merciful Honored One, mindful of those yet unawakened,
proclaimed these verses once more:

In this world, many harbor anger,
Ever nursing minds of poison and harm.
Their thoughts ever constricted,
They rage at men, they rage at women,
At livestock and servants—
Such bodies, seared by sorrow.
Wielding knives or clubs,
They seek only to harm.
Fuming with resentment,
Never knowing even brief joy.
At death, they enter the cold and hot hells,
Where needles pierce their bodies,
Through heart and liver,
Through intestines and flanks.
Blood flows without measure.
Later, they are reborn as frogs,
Or mute in the moon’s light,
Or as *hóu* fish.
Floating in anger upon the water,
Hawks and kites descend to seize them,
Tearing and devouring their flesh.
Even if reborn among humans,
They suffer the retribution of dullness,
Ever ugly and awkward,
Their words lacking skill,
Their speech offending others,
No one to show them pity.

Today, in this grand assembly,
As the scriptures declare,
All should reflect deeply:
Those who bear such sins
Will endure retribution most profound.
Now, in repentance,
May all attain liberation together.

The repentant one, [Name], prostrates in reverence,
Offering this text of repentance for peace and deliverance.
With five limbs touching the earth,
Attending with single-minded focus,
They bow their head to the Merciful Honored One,
And pay homage to the true sages:

With devoted heart, they bow to
The Heavenly Worthy Who Descends with Blessings of Jade Clarity,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to Cries and Saves from Suffering,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Great Numinous Void,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Purple Clarity’s Highest Summit,
The Nine-Colored Heavenly Worthy of Dragon Form,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Preaches in the Fragrant Grove,
The Heavenly Worthy Whose True Countenance Radiates Light,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Lamp of Dharma and Sea of Wisdom,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Truly Awakens and Delivers from Suffering,
The Heavenly Worthy of Compassionate Wisdom Who Delivers from Suffering,
The Heavenly Worthy of Mystic Brilliance Who Extends Lifespan,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Universally Shades All Boundaries,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Transforms the Three Realms,
The Heavenly Worthy of Non-Action,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Entrusts the Substance,
The Heavenly Worthy of Numinous Talismans,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Grove,
The Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Light,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to Those to Be Delivered,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Preserves Life and Protects Destiny,
The Heavenly Worthy of Grand Unity Who Saves from Suffering,
The Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Guards the Realm,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Limits,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue,
The Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes,
The Perfected One Who Universally Saves,
The Perfected One Who Universally Delivers,
The Perfected One of Great Compassion Who Saves from Suffering,
The Perfected One of Great Compassion Who Eradicates Transgressions.

Today, the repentant one of this assembly,
Along with all present,
Raises their aspirations toward the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Numinous Treasure in the southwest,
And all the honored ones, all the sages,
All the great Perfected Ones, all the great immortals,
All the great divine youths,
