Who pervade the ten directions,
Fill the boundless void,
And manifest as all true sages—
May they together emit rays of compassion,
And together extend their sheltering protection.

The repentant one, [Name], from kalpas without measure,
Has committed sins of anger and resentment without limit.
Today, in prostration and repentance,
They pray for these to be extinguished,
To escape retribution,
And attain perpetual purity.
From this day forward,
May they never again harbor anger or resentment,
May they clearly understand clinging views,
And embody the true and eternal.

May the departed spirits of their ancestors,
And all their kin—past, present, and future—
Forever sever the bonds of transgression,
Never traverse the Nine Dark Realms,
Nor the four modes of birth or six paths of existence,
But together receive the fruits of karma,
And inherit the supreme Dao.

One bow.

**Chapter Two: Repentance for Delusion**

Today, in this grand assembly,
Each person directs their mind,
Bowing their head to the Merciful Honored One,
Repenting the sins of delusion.

The repentant one, [Name], with reverent faith,
Attends to the scriptural words:
All sentient beings arise from the primal qi in delusion,
Clinging to existence.
Though they accumulate merit and diligence,
They cannot escape obstruction.
Thus, they cultivate good fruits,
That they may attain liberation.

Yet these sentient beings,
Not understanding how to cultivate merit,
Accumulate good virtues,
But give rise to the three poisons,
And commit acts of delusion.
Some curse heaven and earth,
Or revile spirits and gods.
Some rebel against rulers and fathers,
Failing in loyalty and filial piety,
Turning to perversity,
Establishing laws that disrupt order,
Favoring their own kin within,
Flattering others without,
Disbelieving in sin and blessing,
Conceiving thoughts against all bounds,
Claiming their nature is self-arising,
Eternal and indestructible,
Making no distinction between good and evil,
No difference between elder and younger,
Passing through lives and rebirths,
Ever acting in delusion.
Some, before sacred images,
Or in places of scripture and Dharma,
Or before Dharma masters,
Or beside kings, parents, or teachers,
Or among fellow students, monastic kin,
Or among the six relations—branches and vines of flesh and blood—
Wives, concubines, sons, and daughters,
Or beneath heaven and earth, sun, moon, and stars,
Or in temples of numinous spirits,
Or before the traces of sages in the empty sky,
Or among humans, non-humans, insects, beasts, and birds,
Commit acts of delusion,
Mock those who practice goodness and give alms,
Or perform meritorious deeds,
Thus incurring sins of slander and defamation.

All such acts are called delusion, arising ever from the heart. Should one commit delusion in even a single name or place, the offense entangles distant ancestors and brings calamity upon the living, leaving no recourse for remorse. Bound in darkness, they suffer in this life from perverse winds and grievous afflictions, meeting death only to enter the Frigid Night Hell, where after ten thousand kalpas they are reborn in the body of a venomous serpent. Without repentance, they sink forever in the evil destinies.

Moved by compassion for those yet unawakened, the Merciful Venerable One spoke this gatha:

In the world of men, those who are deluded,
Who disbelieve in sin and merit,
Mock those who cultivate virtue and merit,
And say there is no past life.
They show no reverence for sun and moon,
Nor for heaven, earth, and stars.
All numinous and holy beings,
They slight and scorn without exception.
Ever committing unwholesome deeds,
They engage in every kind of evil.
Clinging stubbornly to their own nature,
At death they enter the Eighteen Hells,
Enduring every torment and affliction,
Reborn after ten thousand kalpas as serpents.
Their hearts ever filled with venom,
Their bellies devoid of organs.
Hungry and thirsty, they find no food,
And all who see them seek to kill.
Even if reborn among humans,
They still suffer the retribution of delusion.

Today, the great assembly in this Dharma hall, hearing these verses, are filled with awe and dread. Should any bear such transgressions, their retribution will be exact and unerring. Let us all awaken, lest we suffer the same fate. When the day of our sinking comes, even if we seek repentance, it may be too late. Or we may endure the torments of hell, hungry ghosts, and beasts, unable to transcend, until together we resolve to seek liberation.

The penitent, so-and-so, prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text, throwing himself fully to the ground, concentrating his mind in single-pointed resolve. He bows his head to the Merciful Venerable One, paying reverence to the true and holy.

With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Jade Purity Bestower of Blessings Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Hearer of Cries Savior from Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Supreme Numinous Void Sovereign Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Lofty Mysterious Void Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Boundless Self-Mastery Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Lofty Jade Emperor Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Dragon Han Brahma-Savior Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Supreme Purple Void Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Transcendent Perfected Sage Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Attainer of Fruition Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Jade Radiance Subtle Light Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Supreme Expedient Means Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Radiant Protector of Life Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Manifestation of Expedient Vision Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Wondrous Fruit Pearl Radiance Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Pervasive Opener of Mysteries Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Dharma-Realm Responsive Compassion Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Mind-Responsive Awakener Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Deliverer of the Dark and Bright Realms Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Great Wisdom Ocean Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Fearless Power Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Compassionate Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Treasure Repository Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Great One Savior from Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Longevity Protector of Life Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Universal Compassion Protector of the Realm Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Ocean of Merit Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Carefree and Joyous Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Wish-Fulfilling Rebirth Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Wisdom-Contemplating Perfected One.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the World-Responsive Perfected One.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Great Compassion Savior from Suffering Perfected One.
With sincere devotion, he pays homage to the Great Compassion Remover of Transgressions Perfected One.

Today, the patrons of this Dharma hall and the great assembly, gazing toward the southwest, invoke the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected Ones, all the Great Worthies and Saints, all the Great Holy Assemblies, pervading the ten directions and filling the boundless void, manifesting all true and holy beings. Through the great compassion and salvation of the Dao, they resolve to universally deliver all.

The penitent, so-and-so, for his ancestors of past lives, his birth parents, his karmic parents, his preceptor who conferred the precepts, the masters who established the altar and sponsored the rites, his uncles and brothers, his own kin and in-laws, his wives, sons, and daughters, and all his living and deceased family—should any bear boundless and immeasurable deluded transgressions, whether already committed or yet to be, whether already awakened or yet unawakened—by virtue of this Dharma hall today, he repents and seeks their eradication. From this day forward, he vows never to commit them again. May all beings forsake the three evil destinies and together attain liberation, gradually realizing the unconditioned and reaching the shore of the Dao.

One bow.

**Repentance of Stinginess and Greed, Third Scroll**

Today, in this Dharma hall, each member of the great assembly directs his mind upward, gazing toward the Merciful Venerable One, repenting the transgressions of stinginess and greed.

The penitent, so-and-so, collects his mind and gathers his thoughts, listening attentively to the scriptural words. All beings dwell in the floating world, where a hundred years pass in but a few days. In the midst of this fleeting time, like the flash of a spark from struck stone, how can one endure? Like a moth darting into flame, they seek their own destruction. Unable to awaken and comprehend, they remain entangled without respite. Day by day, their transgressions accumulate, and with each passing moment, their sins and sufferings grow. Clinging to miserliness, they are ever burdened by greed, amassing wealth as high as mountains, yet their hearts remain unsatisfied. They plan for a single day’s life as if it were a thousand years. Yet when they were born, they brought not a single coin, and when they die, they take not a single coin away. In a single morning’s departure, all is emptiness. Boundless stinginess and greed become the seeds of transgression.

Or before the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Dao, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or before the great treasury of scriptures, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or before the Dharma bodies of those who have left the household life, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or in places of fasting, precepts, and offerings, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or in places of burning incense and lighting lamps, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or in the construction of monasteries, halls, and temples, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or upon the field of merit and virtue, they harbor stinginess and greed.

Or before emperors and kings, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or before fathers and mothers, sons and daughters, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or before the worthy and the elders, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or regarding others’ or their own wealth and possessions, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or at the sight of food and drink, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or at the sight of carriages and horses, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or at the sight of clothing and adornments, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or at the sight of vast fields and estates, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or at the sight of magnificent dwellings, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or at the sight of servants and slaves, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing dilapidated temples and monasteries, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing towering forests and mountains, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing lush blossoms and rotting fruit, they harbor stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing the poor, the aged, and the sick, they fail to think of relief and deliverance, harboring stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing prisoners in suffering, they neglect compassion and remembrance, harboring stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing travelers in distress, they refuse to aid and rescue, harboring stinginess and greed.
Or upon seeing the hungry and cold with emaciated bodies, they withhold what is needed, harboring stinginess and greed.

Even to the slightest—whether their own possessions, others’ belongings, public goods, or common property; be it a thread, a hair, a blade of grass, a tree, a flower, a fruit, a grain of rice, or a pinch of wheat—they either gluttonously consume or hoard with miserly attachment. Toward others, they act with stinginess and contempt, refusing to perform good deeds or make offerings. They torment themselves with accumulation, burdened by worry and vexation. They wish wealth for themselves and poverty for others. When their bodies perish, they are like a boat without oars, like a cart without wheels—only evil deeds remain, with no goodness to record. Thus, the karmic causes lead them to fall into the evil destinies.

Thereupon, the Compassionate Venerable One, moved by pity for all beings, spoke this verse:

If in past lives one was stingy and greedy,
clinging and miserly without cease,
amassing wealth like mountains and peaks,
yet the heart ever craves as if to swallow rivers and seas.
Never content, even in places of fasting and precepts,
in making images or copying scriptures,
in constructing monasteries and halls,
or in burning incense and lighting lamps—
wherever merit is made,
not a single hair’s worth is offered,
yet still seeking benefits through contrivance.
At death, they enter the Hell of Cold Ice,
where their bodies are frozen and shattered,
every joint broken and destroyed.
In later lives, they dwell among border tribes,
or become a household dog,
guarding without rest,
fierce and despised by all.
Only after ten thousand kalpas do they receive rebirth,
yet as humans, they are incomplete:
hands withered or feet lame,
eyes blind or ears deaf,
noses crooked or mouths askew,
chests protruding or spines bent.
Their forms are hideous and misshapen,
nowhere met with pity.

Today, the great assembly in this Daoist ritual, having heard these words of scripture, are filled with dread. If such sins exist, they will bear retribution in future lives. Now, with earnest devotion, they wish to cleanse past transgressions. May all beings—whether in hell, as hungry ghosts, or as animals—suffering from such karmic retribution, through the power of this repentance ritual, the power of the Great Dao, and the power of merit, all attain liberation.

The repentant one, [Name], from limitless kalpas past to the present kalpa, in this life and this day, along with teachers, parents, their own person, and all kin—whether in this life or past lives, the living and the deceased—has committed boundless and immeasurable sins of stinginess and greed, never having purified them, nor even been aware of them. Today, prostrating for peace and in memorial, they recite this repentance text, bowing with the five limbs to the ground, listening with single-minded sincerity.

They bow their heads to the Compassionate Venerable One, reverently paying homage to the true sages.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Jade Clarity Bestowing Blessings Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Hearer of Cries Saving from Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Great Numinous Void Sovereign Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Golden Mirror Wondrous Countenance Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Precept-Born Prolonging Life Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Boundless True Image Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Omnipresent Verifying Fruition Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Ever-Aiding Universal Salvation Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Naturally Empty and Still Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Expedient Causes and Effects Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Multitudinous Wondrous Compassionate Light Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Jeweled Cause Dharma Ocean Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the True Constancy Delivering Life Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Hundred Million Majestic Names Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Protector of the Nation Eternal Peace Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Great Wisdom Eye Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Vast Propagator of the Teaching Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Expedient Wisdom Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Turning Dharma Wheel Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Jeweled Forest Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Empowering the Dao Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Great One Saving from Suffering Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Prolonging Life Preserving Destiny Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Carefree and Joyous Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Wish-Fulfilling Rebirth Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Merit Ocean Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Vast Faith Perfected Person.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Wondrous Virtue Perfected Person.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Great Compassion Saving from Suffering Perfected Person.
With devoted hearts, they pay homage to the Great Compassion Removing Sins Perfected Person.

Today, the repentant one of this ritual and the great assembly, gazing toward the southwest, reverently beseech the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected Persons, the Great Compassionate and Great Merciful Perfected Persons, the Youth Saving from Suffering, the Youth of Supreme Wisdom, the Youth Attending to Medicine—manifesting throughout the ten directions, filling the boundless and mysterious realms, appearing as all true sages. May they generate compassionate vows and the power of universal salvation. May the repentant one, [Name], in their three lives—past, present, and future—along with their nine generations of kin, their own person, spouse, and children, all sins of stinginess and greed, through this repentance ritual, have their names stricken from the register of offenses. May all beings who have not yet attained liberation, and those already delivered, together through this repentance, be freed and realize the supreme Dao.

**First Prostration**
Recitation of the Chapter on Almsgiving, the Fourth

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, each turning their mind, reverently faces the Merciful Honored One, repenting the sins of withholding almsgiving.

The repentant one, [Name], awakening to understanding, bows deeply and kneels in earnest, receiving the scripture’s words: All beings, while embodied in this world, indulge in insatiable desire, ever greedy throughout the day—when do they ever relinquish? Forsake?

Their kin fill the chambers, gold and jade overflow the halls, yet their hearts remain unsatisfied, still harboring stinginess and attachment. They do not cherish beneficence, but fix their thoughts on miserliness and avarice.

Yet almsgiving yields boundless merit, benefiting all in ways beyond conception. There are three kinds of almsgiving: the almsgiving of the Dao, the almsgiving of the body, and the almsgiving of wealth.

The almsgiving of the Dao entails constantly sharing one’s teachings—the scriptures and doctrines of the Three Caverns—with skillful means. Whether provisional or ultimate, expansive or concise, they guide beings to enter the One Vehicle, forever severing the bonds of attachment and ascending to the realm of eternal bliss. From kalpa to kalpa, the Wheel of the Dao turns unceasingly. Past and future alike remain unwavering, without regret. This is the foremost, beyond all conception.

The almsgiving of the body means offering one’s own life to rescue and relieve all beings from illness, water and fire, blades and weapons, and countless calamities—all receive shelter and protection. Through expedient means, one spares neither body nor life. Seeing all the starving as if suffering one’s own hunger, seeing all the freezing as if enduring one’s own cold. Even to the point of offering one’s own labor to replace another’s peril, without reservation. Or serving the Dharma-bodies of those who have left the household, attending to their needs—gathering herbs in the mountains, running errands at their side, constructing and repairing temples, sweeping halls, planting orchards, performing all meritorious deeds. Digging wells by the roadside, repairing bridges and paths, never shirking toil, only striving with wholehearted devotion. The merit is towering, beyond all reckoning.

The almsgiving of wealth has two forms. The first is inner wealth: one’s body, limbs, the hundred bones and nine orifices, skin and nails—exerting all effort to save and deliver, sparing nothing, offering it to others. The second is outer wealth: money, land, cities, and estates; wives, children, servants, and slaves; oxen and horses; gold, silver, pearls, and jade; silks and brocades; toys and adornments—all scattered and given freely, unattached in the heart.

There are also nine kinds of almsgiving, each distinct, yet all yielding benefit according to the intention behind them:
1. Almsgiving to the true, responsive, and transformed images of those who have entered the Dao;
2. Almsgiving to the Mahāyāna scriptures and teachings;
3. Almsgiving to the sacred forms of immortals and perfected beings;
4. Almsgiving to the numinous temples, monasteries, halls, pavilions, chambers, and cloisters of the Mysterious Altar;
5. Almsgiving to the Dharma-bodies of male and female renunciates—black caps and yellow robes, all monastic garments and implements—ensuring their offerings are never lacking;
6. Almsgiving to the permanent endowments: incense, oil, lamps, candles, estates, and servants;
7. Almsgiving to bells, chimes, banners, flowers, canopies, seats, and all ritual implements;
8. Almsgiving of vegetarian meals—rice, flour, oil, and incense—to the Dharma-bodies of renunciates and those who uphold the precepts, observe fasts, and diligently cultivate the Dao;
9. Almsgiving to the poor, orphaned, widowed, sick, imprisoned, and all in peril or suffering.

The Merciful Honored One declares: The merit of these various forms of almsgiving is beyond conception. Moreover, why were the people of antiquity free from disasters? The Merciful Honored One says: The people of antiquity were simple and sincere at heart, embracing the Dao and holding fast to virtue. They were neither greedy nor desirous. Later ages grew shallow and frivolous; people became deceitful, seeking only wealth, unaware of karmic conditions. They valued possessions over life, leading to the ruin of families and nations. Within, they harbored myriad evils; without, they forged alliances with the violent and reckless. Enmity and hatred followed one after another, with no means of awakening. Thus, the Dharma-gate of almsgiving was established to encourage generosity.

Yet today’s fourfold assembly clings to wealth and does not value life. To relinquish their wealth is as if relinquishing their very lives—hence the saying, “life and wealth.” If one can practice almsgiving, then:
- No inner thieves arise,
- No outer thieves appear,
- Inner and outer are at peace,
- All suffering is dispelled.

Through almsgiving today, stinginess and avarice are shattered. The transformative power of the sages reaches unseen realms, and blessings are received according to one’s merit.

If beings do not practice the almsgiving of the Dao, the almsgiving of the body, the almsgiving of inner wealth, the almsgiving of outer wealth, or the nine kinds of almsgiving—
- Seeing vegetarian feasts prepared, they refuse to give;
- Seeing those who uphold the precepts and cultivate practice, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the true scriptures expounded, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the sacred images of the Heavenly Worthies, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the Dharma-bodies of renunciates suffering cold, they refuse to give;
- Seeing lamps lit in offering, they refuse to add to the almsgiving;
- Seeing incense burned and lamps extinguished in places of offering, they refuse to replenish the almsgiving;
- Seeing banners and images in the Dao altar insufficient, they refuse to give;
- Seeing ancient sacred sites damaged, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the halls and temples of numinous monasteries in disrepair, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the cases and covers of the Great Treasury of Scriptures incomplete, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the implements of offering not conforming to the Dharma, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the recitation of hymns and praises in the ritual processions, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the permanent endowments insufficient, they refuse to give;
- Seeing the sounds of bells and chimes not harmonious, they refuse to give;
- Seeing construction unfinished, they refuse to give;
- Seeing prisoners, the poor, the elderly, the sick, the meritorious, or the fields of blessing, they refuse to give.

Or they do not give with expedient means, with compassion, with persuasion, with teaching, with reduction, with a good heart, with clear instruction, with skillful methods or partial teachings, with impartiality, with loyalty and filial piety, with good intentions, with influence, with medicine or healing arts, or with generosity.

For all the above, those who refuse to give—even in this life, their families will never know peace.

Couples, man and wife, part midway in life.
Their own bodies maimed, afflicted by foul disease,
they perish and descend into the Nine Dark Realms,
passing through all the hells,
for ten thousand kalpas to receive the bodies of serpents and dogs.

Thereupon the Merciful Honored One, pitying their unawakened state, spoke in verse:

If one is wealthy and noble,
virtuous, good, and wise,
possessing healing arts and influence,
yet refuses to give in any way—
saying, “I am rich in this world,
and shall enjoy eternal bliss,”
not believing in rebirth,
then poverty is but the guest of wealth.

In this life, they die suddenly,
their families separated in their prime.
Dead, they enter the dark and bitter prison,
their hearts pierced by iron (chains).
Reborn in the bodies of serpents and dogs,
fierce and savage, ever guarding their dens.
Even if they regain human form,
they remain dull and ignorant, devoid of understanding.
Destined to lonely poverty and lowly station,
they serve others for generation upon generation.

Today, the great assembly in this Dao altar,
hearing what the sutra has declared,
is seized with terror.
If any among us bear such sins,
how could we know it?
In the world to come, we must receive the retribution.
Today, through this ritual recitation,
we must apply ourselves with diligence,
wishing together to repent,
that all may be dissolved and extinguished.
May the six paths and four modes of birth
all attain liberation.

The repentance sponsor, so-and-so, prostrates for peace,
invoking blessings and making vows with this repentance text,
bowing with the five limbs to the ground,
concentrating the mind in single-pointed devotion.
He bows his head to the Merciful Honored One,
reverently saluting the true and sacred.

With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Clarity who bestows blessings.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy who saves from suffering at the sound of cries.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Numinous Void.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Vast Transformation and Merciful Countenance.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Moistening and Non-Action.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Divine Penetration and Myriad Transformations.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy who ferries across the wondrous multitude.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Mysterious Transformation and Liberation.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of True Light who delivers from suffering.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Non-Action and Blessing.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of the Wondrous Dao and Vast Illumination.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy who expounds expedient means.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Vastly Flowing Kindness and Transformation.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Good Awakening.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy seen within the Boundless Edge.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Good Karma.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy who liberates through the Dharma.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy who transmits the teachings.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Great Wisdom-Eye.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Independent Power.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who saves from suffering.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and Nation-Protection.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Expanse.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere heart, he reverently salutes
the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to wishes.

The repentance sponsor and the great assembly
now turn their hopes to the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Numinous Treasure in the southwest,
to all the honored ones and sacred beings,
to all the great perfected ones,
to all the great divine youths,
who pervade the ten directions,
fill the boundless cosmos,
and manifest before all honored and sacred ones.
May they bestow the power of the Dao,
together with the power of expedient means,
so that the repentance sponsor, so-and-so,
his parents, teachers, fellow students,
and all his six relations,
for the three periods of time past,
may have their sins of refusing to give—
whether already repaid or yet to be repaid—
all dissolved and liberated through this repentance ritual.
May his family,
life after life,
be born into wealth and nobility,
endowed with wisdom and intelligence,
and bestow kindness upon all.
May all suffering beings
attain peace together,
quickly awaken to non-action,
and swiftly ascend to the sacred fruit.

One bow.

The fourth scroll of *The Supreme Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Disaster-Dissolution and the Nine Dark Realms* concludes.

The fifth scroll of *The Supreme Compassionate Dao Altar Repentance for Disaster-Dissolution and the Nine Dark Realms*

Compiled by Ge Xuan, the Left Immortal of the Great Ultimate
First Chapter: *Against Frivolous and Deceitful Speech*

Today, in this Dao altar, the great assembly,
each directing their minds,
looks up to the Merciful Honored One,
repenting the sins of frivolous and deceitful speech.

The repentance sponsor, so-and-so, collects his mind, kneels, and listens attentively to the sutra’s words:
All sentient beings,
driven by the four delusions,
rely solely on the six senses.
They take a single good deed
and call it boundless;
they commit myriad sins
yet claim no fault.
Seeing others’ faults,
they amplify and slander;
seeing others’ accumulated virtue,
they criticize and destroy it.
They speak only of themselves,
claiming their virtue and conduct are complete,
hiding their cunning with eloquent tongues,
adorning their words with splendid rhetoric.
Parted for a moment,
they say it was half a year;
seeing each other for a day,
they act as if it were a hundred years.
Such foolish obstinacy
is all frivolous and deceitful speech.

Or before the Heavenly Worthy and the great Dao,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before the Three Caverns’ scriptures,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before dharma masters and great virtuous ones,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before the lord-emperor and king,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before parents and honored kin,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before the worthy and the elders,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before the foolish, lowly, and base,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before the deaf, blind, and six afflicted,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before the revered and wealthy,
they speak frivolously and deceitfully.
Or before teachers, dharma friends, and those of the dharma body,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.
Or before senior companions,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.
Or relying on wealth and nobility,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.
Or relying on intelligence,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.
Or relying on authority and wisdom,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.
Or before those they know,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.
Or before the sacred hosts of the heavens,
the perfected ones of the ten directions,
the stars, the sun, the moon,
and all numinous powers,
they engage in frivolous and deceitful speech.

Whenever one sets the mind to engage in frivolous and deceitful speech, in flowery words devoid of truth, one incurs grave transgressions. In this present life, one’s own body suffers twisted mouth and crooked face; at death, one falls into the Avīci Hell of Torn-Out Tongues, where only after ten thousand kalpas does one take rebirth in the body of a wild beast. Without repentance, one can hardly transcend to the Pure Land.

Thereupon, the Compassionate Venerable, for the sake of those yet unawakened, spoke this gāthā:

If in this present body one speaks frivolously and deceitfully,
dissembling before the Three Jewels,
before father and mother, before sons and daughters,
before the sovereign and the common folk—
wherever people gather,
one slanders and harms the loyal and the worthy,
sows discord among friends,
and envies those more virtuous than oneself.
One spreads rumors and stirs up strife,
indiscriminately speaks of right and wrong,
turns falsehood into truth,
and calls white black.
One gossips about others’ strengths and weaknesses,
presumes to know their likes and dislikes.
Wherever one goes, one creates discord and chaos;
at death, one falls into the Hell of Torn-Out Tongues.
Iron awls pierce the tongue,
mountains of rock press upon the body.
The tongue is stretched to a hundred feet,
nailed fast with iron spikes.
Drip by drip, blood flows forth;
in the next life, one takes the form of a wild dog,
devouring all manner of filth,
day and night lost in deluded thoughts.

Today, the great assembly of this ritual arena, having heard this gāthā, reflects: since beginningless kalpas, all sentient beings have transmigrated and suffered retribution—by what means may one awaken and know this? Now, I repent and vow to cultivate diligence. May the merit of this day bring us all to liberation together.

The repentant one, so-and-so, prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text in homage. With five limbs touching the earth and single-minded reverence, we listen attentively.

We bow our heads to the Compassionate Venerable, paying homage to the Perfected and Sacred Ones.

With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Clarity who bestows blessings.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to cries and saves from suffering.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Mystery.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Natural Transformation through Wisdom.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy beyond form.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who perceives form.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Self-Mastery and Wisdom.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Wisdom.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Virtue Pervading All.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who gives birth to the myriad beings.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who harmonizes yin and yang.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Virtue and Power.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Infinite Wisdom.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who abides through the Three Times.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who established heaven and earth.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Sun and Moon’s Radiance.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Unceasing Compassion.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Jeweled Light that Illuminates All.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who transforms the Three Realms.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Golden Splendor and Vast Brilliance.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who saves from suffering.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who grants longevity and preserves life.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion who protects the realm.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to one’s vows.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Reach.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Sunlight.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Moonlight.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Great Compassion who saves from suffering.
With sincere devotion, we pay homage to the Perfected One of Great Compassion who removes transgressions.

Today, the repentant one of this ritual arena, together with the great assembly, reverently beseeches the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Western Direction, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected Ones, and all the Great Divine Youths—those who pervade the ten directions, fill the boundless void, and manifest throughout all realms—to together open the gate of great forgiveness and save these sentient beings.

May the repentant one, so-and-so, their nine generations of ancestors and seven generations of descendants, their own person, and all their karmic relations—both the living and the deceased—who, through measureless kalpas of abandoning and assuming bodies, have committed the above transgressions of frivolous and deceitful speech, and who, without the power of the Dao, have not attained liberation, through this act of repentance, have their sins extinguished. From this day forward, may they never again commit such offenses, abandoning false and flowery speech to practice only simplicity and truth.

May all sentient beings universally embody the Great Dao.

One bow.

**Chapter Two: Repentance for Malicious Speech and Double-Tongued Words**

Today, in this Daoist sanctuary, all assembled devotees turn their minds in reverence toward the Merciful Honored One, repenting the karmic offenses of malicious speech and double-tongued words. The repentant one, so-and-so, kneels in humility, collects their thoughts, and listens attentively to the scriptural teachings.

All sentient beings bear heavy burdens from the karma of speech, and none is graver than the sin of double-tongued words, where cunning eloquence takes precedence. They belittle the humble to flaunt their wit, mock their superiors, and scorn their inferiors; they treat the noble and the kin with arrogance, unmoved by their plight, deeming their own judgments flawless. They indulge in rich flavors, heedless of excess; they crave foul and rank foods, consuming without restraint. Some deceive the worthy and delude the sagely, slander the true and revile the Dao, spread rumors of others’ faults, and boast of their own righteousness. They curse the wind and rain, repeat hearsay as truth, turn existence into nothingness, and refine the coarse into the delicate. They sow discord among the good, praise the foolish, slander one to another, and another to the first—condemning others’ words while justifying their own. They estrange others’ kin, befriend the foolish, turn intimacy into estrangement, and transform affection into enmity. Their words are ornate yet false, their fabrications passed off as truth; their speech strays from meaning, they slander rulers and fathers, disparage teachers and friends, undermine the loyal and good, suppress those superior to themselves, and harm the innocent. Their vanity and deceit know no bounds; their mouths proclaim virtue while their hearts conceal vice. The paths of such transgressions are manifold, and the sins they weave run deep. Face-to-face, they sigh in regret, turning good into evil, constantly gathering omens and false accusations, ever drawn to perverse teachings. They invoke heaven and earth, summon ghosts and spirits—yet in all their utterances, not a single word is true or upright.

Some commit malicious speech and double-tongued words before the Heavenly Worthy, the great Dao, the scriptures, and the revered masters. Some do so before kings, parents, the virtuous, and the dharma-body. Some before the deities of heaven, the sun, the moon, the void, and the sacred assemblies. Some before all manner of boundaries—wells, stoves, doors, households, and various kin. Some before humans and non-humans alike. Such speech and tongues, scheming in all directions, deceive even the empty void. The roots of these measureless sins all stem from the tongue; even if likened to the sands of the Ganges, they could not be exhausted.

The slightest infraction—even a hair’s breadth—brings a distinct retribution: in this life, a twisted mouth, a paralyzed tongue, muteness, a blocked nose. In death, they fall into the Molten Copper Hell, where only after ten thousand kalpas do they reemerge, reborn as venomous creatures—centipedes, snakes, and vipers. If they do not repent, how can these sins be extinguished?

Thus, the Merciful Honored One, moved by their unawakened state, spoke in verse:

*In past lives, with malicious tongues,*
*They cursed kin and stranger alike.*
*Unmindful of good or evil words,*
*They spoke whatever came to mouth.*
*They called to heaven and cried to earth,*
*Summoned ghosts and dragged along spirits.*
*Even the Three Treasures, heaven and earth,*
*The sun, moon, and stars—none were spared.*
*Over wells and stoves, flowing waters,*
*At doorways and crossroads,*
*Beneath shrines, forests, and mountains,*
*They cursed the loyal and good.*
*Regardless of rank or station,*
*Parents, flesh and blood,*
*Servants, slaves, and attendants—*
*Wherever they dwelt, poisonous words followed.*
*In death, molten copper was poured,*
*Their bodies wreathed in smoke.*
*Later, reborn as wasps and centipedes,*
*Their mouths sought to harm all things.*
*Or as clams and mussels,*
*Buried in sand and mud,*
*Retreating into their shells at will.*
*Even if reborn as humans,*
*They would still be mute and stammering.*

Today, in this Daoist sanctuary, all assembled, as the scriptures declare, have committed the offenses of malicious speech and double-tongued words—retribution knows no error, and none of us can escape. If these sins remain, what fate awaits us in days to come? Thus, we cycle endlessly through hells, hungry ghosts, and animal realms, our karmic debts unceasing.

Now, I prostrate in repentance, beseeching the Dao with sorrow, praying that the Dharma’s grace may universally dissolve these bonds. May the repentant one, so-and-so, kneeling in devotion, recite this repentance text for peace and to honor the departed, prostrating with utmost sincerity, listening with a single mind.

I bow my head to the Merciful Honored One, reverently saluting the true and sacred.

With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Clarity, Bestower of Blessings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Answers Cries and Saves from Suffering.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Mystery.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Myriad Treasures and Radiant Light.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Manifestations.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Constantly Saves and Delivers.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Lofty Purity and Emptiness.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to Karmic Conditions.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Protects the Nation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Universally Delivers Beings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Compassion.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Inexhaustible Intent.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Pacifies the Realm.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Preserves Heaven and Earth.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Delights in the Land.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Blessings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to Beings’ Hearts.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Fulfills All Realms.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Broadly Dissolves Disasters.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Gives Life to Myriad Things.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Supreme Unity, Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life Preservation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and Nation Protection.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Limits.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy, Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of the Dharma-Body, Natural Wisdom.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Mysterious Emptiness and Supreme Virtue.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion and Salvation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Mercy and Sin Eradication.

Today, the repentant one in this Daoist sanctuary, together with all assembled, reverently pray to the Supreme Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Western Realm, the myriad honored ones, the sacred, the great perfected, and the great youths—all the true and sacred beings manifest throughout the ten directions. With sincere devotion, may they broadly open the path of deliverance.

May the repentant one, so-and-so, their nine generations of ancestors and seven generations of descendants, both the living and the deceased, and all their kin—who have committed the above offenses of malicious speech and double-tongued words—through this act of repentance, have their sins extinguished.

From this day forward, I vow never again to commit such acts.
In life after life, may I be endowed with voice and eloquence,
to speak with wisdom and discernment,
to harmonize and benefit all,
to adapt to the shallow and the profound,
and universally deliver the six paths and four kinds of birth,
all sharing in the great Dao of unity.

*One bow*

**Third Section: Breaking Lustful Desires**

Today, in this Daoist sanctuary, each member of the assembly directs their mind,
bowing their heads to the Merciful Honored One,
repenting the sins of lustful desire.

The repentant one, so-and-so, kneels in reverence and takes refuge,
attentively listening to the scriptural words:
All sentient beings, if they give rise to lustful desire,
are confined in dark prisons,
drowned in the river of craving,
with no hope of escape,
forever sunk in suffering.

From the distant past until now,
through the cycles of birth and death over kalpas,
the bones accumulated by their bodies would form great mountains,
the mother’s milk they have drunk would equal the waters of the four great seas,
and the blood they have shed would surpass even this.
Parents, siblings, and the six relations—all have exhausted their allotted years.
The tears they have shed would be like the waters of the four great seas.
Thus it is said: with craving, there is birth; with the end of craving, there is extinction.
It is known that birth and death arise from lustful desire.
The sin of lustful desire causes sentient beings to fall into hell,
to receive the bodies of hungry ghosts.
If reborn as animals, they take the forms of doves, sparrows, owls, and other birds.
Such beings may entertain lustful thoughts
before the scriptures, Dharma masters, or in sacred halls and numinous observatories of the Heavenly Worthy,
or in pure places, divine temples, or near sacred sites.
They may violate the chaste,
seize and harm others,
separate mother and child,
take away another’s sons and daughters,
disrupt bonds of affection,
sever ties of love,
showing no regard for the virtuous.
They may expose themselves beneath the Three Luminaries,
or in thought and mind defile the Dharma bodies of male and female renunciates.
Or they may engage in impure acts with the five kinds of persons.
All such beings who direct unwholesome thoughts toward the Dharma bodies of renunciates
are like those who burn and destroy sacred images and palaces—
upon death, they fall into the Nine Dark Hells of Fengdu,
never to be reborn for kalpas.
Their descendants for nine generations suffer short lives and bitter poverty.
For each and every such act of lustful desire,
their households in this life encounter unjust calamities,
official troubles and heavy misfortunes,
their own bodies afflicted by wind and evil,
year after year stricken with illness.
Upon death, they enter the Nine Dark Hells,
only to be reborn after ten thousand kalpas,
receiving the retribution of filthy, worm-ridden bodies.
If they do not repent, they will forever remain sunk in suffering.

For those yet unawakened, the Merciful Honored One spoke this verse:

In past lives, they engaged in illicit lust,
recklessly and without restraint.
They violated the wives and concubines of others,
separating them from their kin.
The six relations were all involved,
as were the bodies of renunciates.
Even among the six kinds of animals,
they made no distinction between good and evil.
In pure places,
within sacred halls and numinous observatories,
before scriptures or near images,
they exposed themselves beneath heaven and earth,
under the sun, moon, and stars,
showing no regard for ghosts and spirits.
By famous mountains and great marshes,
in shrines and divine temples,
everywhere they indulged in lustful desire—
upon death, they fall into the Nine Dark Hells.
Men embrace great bronze pillars,
women lie upon beds of scorching iron.
Their bodies engulfed in smoke and fire,
their flesh and fat all charred and rotted.
Further tormented by boiling cauldrons,
beaten day and night with iron rods.
Later cast into the Hell of Icy Cold,
their bodies torn apart,
pounded in mortars, ground in mills,
sawed asunder, hacked by blades.
Even if they regain human form,
they are afflicted with madness and evil diseases.

Today, the assembly in this Daoist sanctuary,
as described in the scriptures, is deeply terrified.
If such sins exist, how can one become aware of them?
Among the four kinds of birth and six paths,
seeing those who suffer and those yet to receive punishment—
through this act of repentance, may all attain liberation.

The repentant one, so-and-so, prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text,
bowing with the five limbs touching the ground.
Kneeling to the Merciful Honored One, they reverently pay homage to the true and sacred beings.

With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Purity Who Bestows Blessings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Rescues from Suffering at the Sound of Cries.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Mystery.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Transformative Self-Mastery.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Embodies Heaven and Earth.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Five Hundred Million Forms.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Shakes Heaven and Earth.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Golden Wheel and Jade Light.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Perfects the Land.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Abides with Sentient Beings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Ninefold Radiance.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Lotus.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Removes All Defilements.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Bestows Blessings in All Directions.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Serene and Compassionate Transformation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Protects Souls Without Hindrance.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Universally Illumines All Beings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Turns the Dharma According to the Mind.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Delivers from Distress.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy King of Still Mountains.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Fragrant Flowers Filling Heaven.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Vast and Skillful Salvation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Rescues from Suffering.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life Preservation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and State Protection.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Extent.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion and Solar Wisdom.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Wisdom and Lunar Compassion.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion and Salvation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Mercy and Sin Eradication.

Today, the repentant one in this Daoist sanctuary, together with all assembled,
reverently pray to the Supreme Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Western Realm,
the myriad honored ones, the sacred, the great perfected, and the great youths—
all the true and sacred beings manifest throughout the ten directions,
filling the boundless void and hidden or revealed in all realms.

May the power of this Daoist sanctuary, the power of chanting praises, and the power of self-transformation enable the repentant one, [Name], along with their birth parents, extended kin, uncles, brothers, personal relatives, and all living and deceased across two generations—should any bear the karmic burden of lust and desire as described above—to now sincerely prostrate, repent, and cleanse their transgressions. From this day forward, may they perceive form as emptiness, sever karmic retribution, and refrain from further transgression. May they cherish the body as a treasure, guard conduct as a pearl, encounter no obstacles, and enter the shore of non-action, ascending together to the fruition of the Dao.

**First Prostration**
**Chapter Four: Distant Aversion and Attachment**

Today, the assembled in this Daoist sanctuary, each directing their minds, face the Merciful Honored Ones and repent the sins of aversion and attachment between self and others. The repentant one, [Name], gathers their heart, kneels in reverence, and listens attentively to the scriptural words:

All sentient beings, when first setting intention, are often foolish, their actions seldom sincere. Attachment accumulates like mountains, yet they claim it is never enough. Aversion discards as if filth, yet they resent not having cast it away entirely. Thus, their minds fail to awaken and comprehend, distinguishing self from others, judging strength and weakness. Words and deeds diverge, entangled in worldly nets, indulging in obstinate folly. They gaze without satiety, listen without discernment, yielding to greed and delusion, forsaking tranquility and harmony. What pleases the eye, they stare at without ceasing; what pleases the ear, they listen to without tiring. They speak only of others’ faults to extol their own virtues. When the mind is pleased, they overlook ugliness; when words are affectionate, they disregard closeness or distance.

Thus, sentient beings may harbor aversion or attachment before the seats of true and sacred beings, or before kings, parents, or revered teachers. They may conceive such thoughts before uncles, brothers, men, or women, or before the heavens, earth, sun, moon, or the boundless void. They may foster such desires at sacred sites or before divine altars. These immeasurable, boundless sins of aversion and attachment between self and others—should one commit even a single instance or kind—lead to rebirth in the hells of manifold suffering, with no hope of escape. Even if reborn, they shall assume non-human forms. Without repentance and liberation, they shall forever sink in suffering.

Then the Merciful Honored One expounded further in verse:

Aversion and attachment arise from self and other,
Self-generated, singular in intent.
What was deemed evil now seems good,
Aversion lengthens, attachment shortens.
Those despised are cut off in form and shadow,
Yet still the foolish heart is not sated.
Those loved stand like mountains,
Yet still they claim it is never enough.
All things share a single body,
Yet distinctions of beauty and ugliness arise.
Self and other emerge from the mind,
Good and evil all stem from nature.
Upon death, they enter the great hells,
Enduring every torment and poison.
Blades pierce the heart,
Iron awls tear the tongue.
A hundred joints are nailed with iron,
Later reborn as geese or ducks,
Or as fish and turtles,
Slaughtered, unable to speak.
At the mercy of others’ lives and deaths,
Subject to every manner of cooking and preparation.
Later, reborn as humans,
They become the mute, deaf, or dumb.

Today, the assembled in this Daoist sanctuary, as the scripture declares, are filled with sorrow. If such sins are committed, how can their retribution be endured? Moreover, the repentant one, [Name], along with their nine generations of ancestors, parents, revered teachers, uncles, brothers, themselves, and all kin—from limitless and beginningless kalpas to this very life and day, through countless rebirths—have harbored these sins of aversion and attachment between self and others, never awakening. Now, establishing this Daoist sanctuary for peace and offering this repentance, they prostrate with five limbs to the earth, wholeheartedly invoking:

With devoted heart, I bow to the Jade Clarity Heavenly Worthy Who Bestows Blessings.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves Through Sound.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Mystery.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Western Numinous Forest Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Discipline-Generated True Wisdom.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Vast Emptiness and Great Mystery.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of All-Pervading Great Movement.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Myriad Blessings and Radiant Brilliance.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Primordial Essence and Celestial Sovereignty.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Transforms the Dao Through Myriad Movements.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of True Illumination Through the Dao’s Movement.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Accords with the World.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Wondrous Splendor and True Sovereignty.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Myriad Transformations in the Golden Palace.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Orthodox Dao and Non-Action.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy and Dharma King of Penetrating Emptiness.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Three Clarities’ Purple Palaces.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of True Dao’s Illumination and Accomplishment.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Countenance and Radiant Light.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Wondrous Compassion Who Eradicates Suffering.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Three Lights’ Turning Wheel.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of True Virtue and Salvation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Saves from Suffering.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Preserves Life and Longevity.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Protects the Realm.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Boundless Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Ocean of Merit and Virtue Heavenly Worthy.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of True Stability and Radiance.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Radiant and Wondrous Sound.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion and Salvation.
With devoted heart, I bow to the Perfected One of Great Mercy and Sin Eradication.

Today, the repentant one in this Daoist sanctuary, together with all assembled, reverently pray to the Supreme Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Western Realm, the myriad honored ones, the sacred, the great perfected, and the great youths—all the true and sacred beings manifest throughout the ten directions, filling the boundless void and hidden or revealed in all realms. May they bestow their benevolent power, enabling the repentant one, [Name], their nine generations of ancestors, seven lineages of kin, and all living and deceased relatives to beseech liberation from the aforementioned karmic offenses. From this day forward, may they never again commit such transgressions. May all who have sunk in suffering, through the power of this repentance, ascend to the shore of the Dao.

**First Bow: The Fifth Precept on Non-Stealing**

Today, the assembly of this Daoist sanctuary, each with sincere heart, bows their heads to the Merciful Honored One, repenting the karmic offenses of theft. The repentant one, [Name], collects their mind, kneels in reverence, and surrenders body and soul, heeding the scriptural words: all sentient beings, lacking integrity, must not take even a blade of grass or a single leaf without just cause—how much less may they steal. Yet beings, deluded by present gain, seize what is not theirs through manifold unjust means.

Some breach walls or dig through barriers, waylay travelers, or plunder by force. Some default on debts, break contracts, or deceive with words and heart. Some take what is not theirs, reasoning none will know—yet the heavenly net is vast; where can they escape? Some steal from the Heavenly Worthy’s scriptures, dharma treasures, or ritual implements. Some take offerings meant for perfected sages, or the sacred tools of worship. Some plunder the three-tiered altars, the treasures of the numinous halls, or the vessels of fasting assemblies. Some steal from the materials used to sculpt sacred images, or the alms of the faithful who uphold precepts. Some take the seven treasures donated to the Three Treasures, or the jewels of jeweled thrones, jeweled canopies, jeweled chariots, jeweled banners, jeweled crowns, jeweled mirrors, jeweled trees, jeweled flowers, jeweled halls, jeweled steeds, or the sacred robes and cloud-patterned vestments. Some steal from the jeweled repositories of scriptures, the treasures of jeweled halls, or the jeweled caskets and relics. Some take the possessions of exalted perfected ones, or the oil and incense meant for lamps and offerings. Some plunder the common stores of the assembly, the tribute granaries of the state, or the precious treasures of immortals, jade maidens, vajra guardian kings, or celestial lions. Some steal from the dharma-bodies of male or female officials, or the fruits and vegetables of the Three Sages’ blessed lands. Some take sacrificial animals from spirit temples, or precious substances like giant clams, agate, lapis lazuli, amber, gold, silver, pearls, jade, copper, iron, silk, brocade, or fine linen. Even a single coin, a single thread—whether little or much—all incur grave transgression.

Some break into storehouses, pick locks, alter seals, or tamper with labels and caskets. Some hoard military supplies, evade taxes, or withhold even a fraction of what is due, seeking only personal gain. Some steal the vestments or ritual implements entrusted to dharma masters, or the fresh offerings not yet presented to the spirits. Some take from loving parents, siblings, friends, or neighbors; from travelers’ luggage; from the destitute, the aged, or the infirm. Some seize goods meant for trade, the seeds and livestock of farmers, or take by deceit, coercion, or force. Some claim public authority, or take through neglect, fraud, or jest. Some take by force, subterfuge, or false pretenses; by greed, unreturned loans, or barter; by refusal to repay, by deception, or by hiding the truth. Some beg with false humility or demand with threats. All such crooked acts incur fault and blame.

If it is not one’s own, even a hair’s weight must not be coveted—all such taking is theft. Even lost items found on the road, carried by wind or birds, delivered by spirits or gods—clothing, bedding, utensils, carriages, horses, cloth, grain, or the tiniest speck—if concealed, become the karmic offense of theft. This shortens one’s lifespan, brings misfortune to nine generations of ancestors and seven lineages of kin, and offers no escape. In life, one suffers illness; in death, one falls into hell. Even if reborn, one becomes an ox or beast of burden. Without repentance, one remains forever sunk in suffering.

Thus, the Merciful Honored One spoke these verses:

*In past lives, they stole and plundered,*
*Taking the Three Treasures’ wealth.*
*Alms given in faith, offerings made in devotion,*
*Or the possessions of kings and people—*
*None of it theirs, yet at the sight,*
*They harbored thieving hearts,*
*Always scheming to steal.*
*They robbed travelers by force,*
*Threatened, coerced, or framed the innocent.*
*They tunneled through walls, plundered by night,*
*Or lurked in empty places,*
*Seizing cattle, servants, slaves,*
*Wealth, jewels, and treasures—*
*All by cunning means.*
*In death, they enter the hell of fire-carts,*
*Their bodies scorched and shattered.*
*In later lives, they become oxen or horses,*
*Repaying their debts to others.*
*Yoked, their flesh and fat are torn away,*
*Nostrils and mouths ripped apart.*
*Hungry and thirsty, they suffer endlessly,*
*Unable to speak.*
*At others’ mercy, they are slaughtered,*
*Only to be reborn as humans—*
*Then robbed and killed in turn,*
*Repaying the sins of past lives.*

Today, the assembly of this Daoist sanctuary must reflect deeply on these scriptural words, which inspire true dread. With utmost sincerity, they must bow in repentance, seek mercy, and pray that all beings—whether already suffering retribution or yet to face it—may, through this act of repentance, attain universal liberation.

The repentant one, [Name], prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text, throwing themselves to the ground with utmost devotion. Bowing their head to the Merciful Honored One, they reverently pay homage to the sacred beings:

With sincere heart, they bow to the Jade Clarity Heavenly Worthy Who Bestows Blessings.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Rescues from Suffering at a Cry.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Mystery.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Equal and Vast Compassion.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Abides in the World and Delivers Beings.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Manifestations.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Transcends All Karmic Bonds.

With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Eradicates All Thoughts.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Unfettered Freedom.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Preaches the Dao from Ten Thrones.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Burns Incense and Delivers Beings.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Recites Scriptures and Rescues from Suffering.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Upholds Fasts and Relieves All Beings.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Maintains Precepts and Protects the World.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Whose Dao-Invocation Dissolves Disasters.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Scatters Flowers and Prolongs Life.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Palace Ever-Bright.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Brings Prosperity and Great Peace to the Nation.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Rescues from Dire Perils.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Guards Life as a Divine Spirit.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Whose Dharma-Wheel Spreads Transformation.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Rescues from Suffering.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Bestows Longevity and Preserves Life.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Protects the Nation.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Bliss.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Extent.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected of Stellar Radiance.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected of Fiery Radiance.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion Who Rescues from Suffering.
With sincere heart, they bow to the Perfected of Great Mercy Who Eradicates Transgressions.

Today, the master of repentance in this Daoist ritual, together with the great assembly, each directs their mind and aspires toward the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Western Direction, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected, and all the Great Divine Youths—those who pervade the ten directions, fill the boundless void, and manifest throughout all realms of reality.

By the power of dissolving disasters and guarding life,
By the power of rescuing from suffering and eradicating transgressions,
By the power of boundless merit and virtue,
By the power of innumerable immortals,
By the power inconceivable—

The master of repentance, [Name], along with their teacher, fellow disciples, Daoist companions, all dharma kin, the seven generations of ancestors, the nine lineages of descendants, their birth parents, uncles, brothers, all branches and vines of kinship—from beginningless time until this very day—have committed the aforementioned sins of theft, used false weights and measures, deceived the good and kind, sought gain through improper means, spread fear and violence, engaged in stealth and coercion, invoked spirits and ghosts, deceived themselves, indulged in cruelty, disregarded joy and anger, ignored the poor and destitute, and given free rein to greed and savagery, accumulating manifold transgressions.

Relying on this repentance ritual, may these sins be eradicated.
From this day forward, in life after life, may they attain the wish-fulfilling pearl, ever possess the seven treasures, wear finest garments, taste the hundred flavors of sweet dew, and receive all manner of medicines and remedies as desired, bestowing them upon all beings without exception, never again committing theft.

May all beings be free from the thought of theft, ever content, unstained by attachment, ever delighting in wise generosity, relieving the poor and rescuing the suffering, offering head, eyes, brain, and marrow as readily as spittle.

With a mind of dedication, may they accomplish the supreme Dao.
One bow.

The Fifth Scroll of the Supreme Compassion Daoist Ritual Arena for Dissolving Disasters and the Nine Dark Realms Concludes
The Sixth Scroll of the Supreme Compassion Daoist Ritual Arena for Dissolving Disasters and the Nine Dark Realms

Compiled by Left Immortal of the Great Ultimate, Ge Xuan

First Repentance: On the Killing of Living Beings

Today, in this Daoist ritual arena, all present turn their minds toward the Compassionate Honored One, repenting the karmic offenses of killing living beings.

The repentant master, [Name], gathers his mind, kneels in reverence, and listens attentively to the scriptural words:

All sentient beings, so long as they dwell within the human realm, remain entangled in the web of the world. Having never encountered a virtuous friend and constantly associating with the foolish, they accumulate habits that become deeply ingrained. Like the mingling of fragrant and foul, they are stained by manifold transgressions. They give free rein to reckless cruelty, perpetrating suffering without cause, never awakening a heart of compassion. They kill living beings, devouring flesh and bone.

At times, for the sake of parents, themselves, brothers, wives, children, or extended kin, they gather in villages and hamlets, slaughtering countless beings without a thought for their lives.

They kill cattle, sheep, mules, horses, pigs, dogs, and other domesticated creatures, those raised and fed by humans. They boil and butcher deer, foxes, rabbits, tigers, leopards, and wolves—those dwelling in mountains and forests—slaughtering the six kinds of livestock without a moment’s hesitation, heedless of whether they are fat or lean.

Some pierce with blades until blood flows; others scald until skin peels away. Though life has yet to depart, their bellies are slit open, bones removed, sinews stripped, intestines torn out, and flesh carved away. The agony they endure is beyond measure, and the karmic retribution they incur is impossible to repay.

They kill sacred birds—phoenixes, cranes, geese, ducks, turtledoves, pigeons, crows, magpies, owls, and kites—along with all manner of flying creatures. They stretch tall nets, raise long poles with sticky paste, pluck feathers and singe wings, or maim them in treetops. Desperate for death yet unable to die, longing for life yet denied it, they sever their feet, remove their heads, cut off their wings, gouge out their eyes, all to fill the kitchen and sate their hunger.

They kill soft-shelled turtles, alligators, tortoises, snails, clams, crabs, and other armored creatures. They drain rivers and dig trenches, set bamboo traps and scatter sand, cast nets and weirs, or use baskets to ensnare scales and fins. They boil and butcher them on islands, piling bones into mountains, their stench carried on the wind. Though they have taken countless lives, their desire remains unquenched.

They kill snakes, vipers, scorpions, bees, wasps, dung beetles, midges, centipedes, locusts, ants, and all manner of crawling things. They kill mosquitoes, horseflies, lice, fleas, mayflies, moths, and other creatures born of transformation—every wriggling, flying, or submerged being.

Though these may be venomous creatures, they too seek peace. They thrive in heat and dampness, perish in cold and ice, all partaking in the transformations of creation, never entering the kitchen. To kill them without cause—how can such suffering be endured?

They fly hawks and hunt with dogs, draw bows and nock arrows, their hearts stirred by greed and savagery, knowing only the taking of life. They set mountains ablaze, drain forests and rivers dry. They wield arrows and blades, grasp spears and halberds, killing living beings. They crush with hands, trample with feet, press down while sitting or lying, killing living beings. They till fields and plant crops, build walls and erect barriers, killing living beings. They construct houses, dig pits, and excavate earth, killing living beings. They dismantle fences, clear grass, and level ground, killing living beings. They gather firewood, fell trees, pluck flowers, and pull up grass, killing living beings. They light lamps and raise candles, killing living beings. They divert water into burrows or pour boiling water on the ground, killing living beings. They wash their hair, bathe their bodies, drink water, and eat meals, killing living beings. They thresh grain and husk wheat, split open wombs and crush eggs, killing living beings. They swat ropes, fan away mosquitoes, open their mouths, close their eyes, raise their hands, or stamp their feet, killing living beings. They kill before sacred images, scriptures, or in the presence of the Dharma; they carry creatures home from the ritual arena to slaughter. In anger or frustration, without cause, they kill living beings. In joy or revelry, indulging their desires, they kill living beings. They slaughter for sacrifices to ghosts and spirits, or for the sick, seeking to avert unseen misfortune. They prepare medicinal decoctions using living creatures, killing them. Some die in their hands, others perish on the butcher’s block, roasted in raging fires, their lineages severed, their reproduction halted, their life roots destroyed, utterly annihilated.

They kill creditors, enemies, or good people from the four directions. They abort fetuses and crush eggs, not sparing even birds and beasts. They kill out of fear, out of dread, by their own hand, or by instructing others. They kill through cursing, poisoning, or drugging. They kill through spells, anger, or joy.
