They kill deliberately, accidentally, with words, hands, intent, thoughts, glances, or in combat.

In all such acts of killing, with every movement of hand or body, they cruelly harm all manner of creatures. Each bears its own sin, and none can escape retribution.

Thus speaks the Compassionate Honored One:
He who amasses boundless wealth will surely bring suffering upon himself;
He who accumulates excess sin will repay his past debts.
Without remorse, without a heart to save, he remains mired in delusion.
Calamity flows to his ancestors, and upon death, he enters the hells of interrogation and punishment, enduring every torment.
Even if he is reborn, his form will be that of a different species.
Without repentance, how can he transcend this fate?

Then the Compassionate Honored One proclaimed again in lamentation:
In past lives, you killed living beings—
Cattle, sheep, pigs, chickens, dogs,
Geese, ducks, pheasants, rabbits,
Deer, tigers, leopards, and their kin,
Owls, crows, swallows, sparrows,
Jackals, wolves, foxes, raccoon dogs,
Mules, donkeys, horses,
Fish, turtles, cicadas, maggots,
Snails, clams, shrimp, mussels,
Dung beetles, ants, and their like,
Leeches, mosquitoes, fleas, lice,
Centipedes, midges, and all manner of worms.
You slaughtered them all, never awakening a heart of kindness.
Whoever you encountered, you harmed without mercy,
And upon death, you fell into the hells,
Enduring every suffering, tormented day and night.
In that place of unbearable agony,
All those cattle and sheep
Will come to demand their lives,
Saying, “You ate my flesh.”
Or, “You killed my body,”
Claiming you had no right.
Today, we meet again—
You must repay your past debts.

Even as you seek escape, there is no path—
The demon-king unfolds the scroll of transgressions.
Upon examination, the truth is known:
Life for life, each must be repaid.

If reborn in another form,
You enter the assembly of beasts,
Again becoming oxen, sheep, or dogs,
Even geese, ducks, and their kind.
Subjected once more to slaughter,
You repay the sins of your past life.

Today, in this grand repentance hall, all present—
As the sutras declare—
Every sentient being,
For killing without cause,
Or causing others to kill,
Has committed acts swift and innumerable.
To repay life and settle karmic debts,
Who can take another’s place?
In life, one suffers punishment,
Relying on the strength of kinship;
But upon death, entering the Three Wicked Paths,
Who will come to your rescue?

Such karmic retribution is clear and exact.
Now, we beseech repentance to □,
To wash away past transgressions.
The repentant one, [Name], prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text in memorial.
Five limbs touching the earth, with wholehearted devotion,
We bow our heads to the Merciful Honored One,
Reverently paying homage to the true and sacred.

With sincere hearts, we pay homage to:
The Heavenly Worthy of Jade Purity Who Bestows Blessings,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Rescues from Suffering at a Cry,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Great Brilliance,
The Heavenly Worthy of Golden Radiance and Light,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Delivers from the Nine Hells,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Great Mystery Without Form,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Abides in the World and Saves Beings,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Manifestations,
The Heavenly Worthy of Inner Reality,
The Heavenly Worthy of Forced Designation,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Aids the Dharma,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Saves Lives,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Pardons the Sufferings of Beings,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Flourishes the Nation and Transforms People,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Responds to the World in Myriad Forms,
The Heavenly Worthy of Unfathomable Illumination,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Scatters Fragrant Offerings,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Dharma-Image Pervading the World,
The Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Rescues from Suffering,
The Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation,
The Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and Nation-Protection,
The Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Extent,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merits,
The Perfected of Boundless Heart,
The Perfected of Numinous and Universal Reality,
The Perfected of Great Compassion Who Rescues from Suffering,
The Perfected of Great Mercy Who Eradicates Transgressions.

Today, in this repentance hall, the repentant one and all present
Raise their aspirations toward the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Numinous Treasure in the northwest,
All the venerable ones, all the sages,
All the immortals, all the assemblies,
All the great perfected ones,
All the great divine youths,
Who pervade the ten directions,
Fill the boundless cosmos,
And manifest as all true and sacred beings—
Together, may they pour the Dharma-water
To cleanse all sentient beings.

The repentant one, [Name], since time without beginning,
Along with nine generations of ancestors,
Teachers, parents,
All Dharma-kin,
Uncles, brothers,
Six relations and family,
Both the living and the dead—
Have accumulated boundless, measureless sins of killing,
Now in the hells, hungry ghost, and animal realms,
Receiving retribution and repaying debts,
Unsettled until now, but settled today.

By virtue of this repentance and deliverance,
May we forever break free from the snares of attachment.
From this day forward,
We vow never to create or commit such acts again.
May we regard the bodies of sentient beings as our own,
And see the killing of sentient beings as the killing of ourselves.
With manifold compassion,
Cherish them as we cherish ourselves.
May all beasts attain human birth,
Awaken to the profound principle,
And realize the supreme Dao.

**First Prostration**

**Second Section: Washing Away the Crimes of Destruction**

Today, in this grand repentance hall, each person directs their mind,
Bowing their heads to the Merciful Honored One,
Repenting for boundless, measureless crimes of destruction.

The repentant one, [Name], collects their thoughts and kneels in reverence,
Attentively listening to the sutra’s words:
All sentient beings, by virtue of having form,
From time without beginning until today,
Parents, brothers,
One’s own body and family,
Shedding and assuming forms through countless rebirths—
Have failed to emulate loyalty and goodness,
Instead harboring much harm and ruin,
Indulging in arrogance and dissipation,
Failing to restrain themselves,
Seizing and plundering servants and slaves,
Destroying without cause,
Harming sentient beings,
Committing countless defilements.

Moreover, when serving as officials,
Failing to emulate integrity and diligence,
Often engaging in destruction,
Disloyal to the state,
Constantly resorting to flattery and deceit,
Unattuned to the times,
Disdaining the great Dao,
Concealing good and practicing evil,
Not judging by principle,
Envying the worthy and resenting the capable,
Deceiving superiors and bullying subordinates,
Relying on official power and influence,
Refusing to act with fairness,
Allowing personal likes and dislikes to sway their hearts,
Indulging in favoritism and rejection.

Or perhaps they have:
Besieged cities and razed towns,
Burned others’ homes,
Sold good people into bondage,
Enticed others’ servants and slaves,
Wrongfully oppressed the innocent,
Bullied the virtuous.

Or they have:
Destroyed images of the sacred and venerable.

Or perhaps they have:
Destroyed Daoist temples and sacred altars,
Or ruined public monasteries and permanent endowments,
Or damaged the great canon of scriptures,
Or broken the vessels and implements for offerings.
In all things, they fail to cultivate reverence,
Seeking only to destroy.
As echo answers sound,
So too do words of ill omen bring forth their due.
When qi is coarse, the voice is harsh;
When the heart is pleased, you are at ease.
For all beings, reverence and faith come first,
And solemn adornment resides in mindfulness.
To commit such acts of destruction is to accumulate all manner of karmic transgressions,
Causing one’s kin across the three lifetimes to suffer retribution,
Ever bound to evil affinities,
And at death, to enter the bitter hells of suffering,
Where they shall endure the punishment of shaved heads and severed hair.
If they do not repent,
They shall forever bear the weight of sinking and drowning.

Thereupon, the Compassionate Venerable One, moved by pity for those yet unawakened, spoke again in verse:

In former lives, they scorned and slighted,
Damaging all manner of things,
And the forms and images of the sacred,
The temples, the profound altars,
The permanent endowments, the Daoist sanctums.
Relying on power, they bullied the good and kind,
Their hearts cruel and oppressive.
At death, they enter the hells of bitter suffering,
Where kin ever contend in strife,
Tormenting one another in turn.
In later lives, though born as humans,
They suffer the retribution of shaved heads and severed hair.
Their kin endure sorrowful wailing,
Like tumbleweeds, when shall their wandering cease?

Today, the great assembly in this Daoist sanctuary,
Having heard the inconceivable words of the Compassionate Venerable One,
Where karmic consequences are made manifest,
And transmigration endlessly continues,
Now arouse the mind of resolve,
And seek mercy through rites of repentance.
May those in the hells, the hungry ghosts, and the realm of beasts,
By the power of this repentance,
The power of merit and virtue,
And the inconceivable power,
All attain liberation.

The repentant one, [Name], prostrates for peace,
And offers this repentance text in supplication.
With five limbs touching the earth,
And a single mind, they listen attentively.
Bowing in reverence to the Compassionate Venerable One,
They pay homage to the true and sacred.

With sincere devotion, they pay homage to:
The Heavenly Worthy Who Descends with Blessings from the Jade Clarity,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering at a Cry’s Sound,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Great Florescence,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Manifests in Accord with the World,
The Heavenly Worthy of Infinite Wondrous Forms,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Transforms Across Myriad Kalpas,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Mountain of Merit and Virtue,
The Heavenly Worthy of Pure Flowing Light,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Preaches the Dharma Without Obstruction,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Opens Conditions and Delivers Beings,
The Heavenly Worthy, King of Pure Wisdom and Virtue,
The Heavenly Worthy of Inexhaustible Form,
The Heavenly Worthy of Emptiness and Formlessness,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Lifespan,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Constantly Preaches the Dharma,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Bestows Wealth Abundantly,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Universally Bestows the Dharma,
The Heavenly Worthy Without Equal,
The Heavenly Worthy of Infinite Illumination,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Perfects All,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Great One Who Saves from Suffering,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Preserves Life and Ensures Longevity,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Universally Protects the Realm,
The Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wishes,
The Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Reaches,
The Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue,
The Perfected of the Great Solar Canopy of Compassion,
The Perfected of the Lunar Purity of Great Mercy,
The Perfected of Great Compassion Who Saves from Suffering,
The Perfected of Great Mercy Who Removes Transgressions.

Today, the patrons of this Daoist sanctuary,
Together with the great assembly,
Take refuge and aspire toward the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Numinous Treasure in the northwest,
All the Venerables and Sages,
All the great heavenly immortals,
The earthly immortals,
All the great Perfected,
All the great Perfected Who Save from Suffering,
All the great youths,
The Youths of the Primal Boundary,
Who pervade the ten directions,
And fill the boundless realms,
All the true and sacred ones of the past and future.
May they, by the power of the Dao,
The power of merit and virtue,
The power of supreme goodness,
The power of the heavenly immortals,
And the power of spiritual penetrations,
Cause the repentant one, [Name],
For the immeasurable kalpas of transgressions from destroying and plundering,
Through this repentance rite,
To wash away faults and offenses,
And forever dispel obstacles and afflictions.
May they not suffer retribution,
But ascend to realize the fruits of the Dao,
And reach the shore of non-action.

One bow.

**Chapter Three: On Not Violating the Fast**

Today, in this Daoist sanctuary, all assembled turn their minds as one, bowing their heads to the Merciful Honored One, repenting the transgressions of breaking the fast.

The repentant one, [Name], gathers the heart, kneels in reverence, and listens attentively to the scriptural words: All sentient beings, from the moment they receive form until this very day, have been bound by stinginess, greed, and craving—drinking wine, eating meat, chewing without restraint, nourishing flesh and blood, fostering pus and decay. Day by day, afflictions and illnesses arise, and the roots of sin grow ever deeper.

Moreover, through birth, aging, sickness, and death, through scorching heat, dampness, cold, and wind, through bitter pain and corrosive suffering, they are assailed by noxious qi, and a hundred diseases invade the body. Thought after thought, impermanence ceaselessly presses on, day and night unrelenting. The bodily form and the knowing nature differ in each, yet all revolve in endless cycles, trapped for ten thousand kalpas without escape.

These sentient beings, their minds often corrupted, treat the fasts and precepts with irreverence. As the years advance and old age approaches, as sickness and distress entwine them, in this one life, one lifetime, they toil for self-preservation, all because of their voracious consumption of impure foods. Their organs steam and ferment, offending the true and sacred ones. The winds of karma fan their bodies, causing gold and jade to dissolve, their forms to wither prematurely.

Yet I, who neither drink nor eat, embrace the Dao in its naturalness, transforming without limit, living forever without death. I constantly expound the scriptures and teachings, seeking to deliver all beings. If, in their ignorance and delusion, they cannot believe or follow, I am ever concerned, never at rest. Thus, I offer the fast as a means to dispel their sickness and suffering.

Moreover, the hosts of the Three Clarities, who long ago realized the truth of the Dao, always observe the fasts with diligence, never growing lax. How much more so the six fasts of the lunar months, the ten days of upright conduct, the eight seasonal nodes, the three primal festivals, the jiazi and benming days, the three assemblies of the gengshen, and all other fasts and gatherings—subtle and wondrous beyond thought—all established by the Merciful Honored One to guide and receive sentient beings, enabling them to cultivate practice and escape the perils of demonic obstacles.

Yet you, all you sentient beings, though you know the names of these fasts, do not arouse reverent hearts. And even when you do, you often violate them. Some mix impure foods, blending the foul with the sacred, sharing the same kitchen without purifying themselves, treating all with careless disdain. Others eat after midday, their minds still stained, slandering the utmost truth, equating it with falsehood. Their words are deceitful, their hearts swayed by love and hatred. Such foolishness leads to countless violations of the fast.

Some break the Fast of the Great Perfected, some the Fast of the Golden Register, some the Fast of Divine Incantations, some the Fast of the Yellow Register, some the Fast of Illuminating the True, some the Fast of Spontaneous Perfection, some the Three Primal Fasts, some the Fast of Mud and Ash, some the Fast of the Cavern Spirits—fasts such as these, whether established for the state, for the deliverance of ancestors, for the rescue of the drowning, for the sake of departed kin, or for the benefit of others. At first, they arise with faith and devotion, but later, regret takes hold. Their sins deepen, and they suffer boundless torment.

If, for the sake of the Dharma-body of ordained men and women, whether ten, a hundred, or even more, the fast is distributed according to its scale, ensuring no partiality, then all who speak of fasting must do so with a giving heart—not with ostentation, nor with meager offerings. Those who are ordained should share equally in the fast. To select or discriminate is to treat it with disdain. To fail to arouse reverence is to break the fast.

Furthermore, if one takes for oneself even a single coin from the offerings of a fast, the construction of images, or any other materials, one must repay tenfold within ten years. If not repaid, the retribution is severe illness, deformity, and eternal banishment from the human realm. They will roost like birds, sleep exposed like beasts. Even if reborn as humans, they will be afflicted by the six chronic illnesses—deaf, blind, and lacking the five senses. If one uses the food of the fast to make offerings to the Dharma-body, or the banners and canopies for venerable images, yet does so without reverence, later growing remorseful, the karmic consequences are beyond description.

When life ends, they are reborn as hungry ghosts—necks thin as bowstrings, bellies swollen like drums, bodies burdened by iron wheels, flames scorching them on all sides. To cover themselves with cloth is like touching a mountain of fire. When they eat or drink, it turns to pus and blood. If they suffer this in the present life, they lie bedridden with malignant disease, their bodies festering and foul, shunned by all. For years and months, flesh wastes away, sinews dissolve. Once cast into hell, they will scarcely be reborn in heaven. In future lives, even if born among humans, they will be deaf, blind, and afflicted by the six illnesses, bereft of beauty, inferior to others. All their kin will treat them as outcasts. If they become husband and wife, they will part midway, leaving orphaned sons and widowed daughters to depend on others. Poor, cold, and hungry, their forms will be ugly, barely clinging to human form.

All such sins arise from breaking the fast. If one does not repent, they will sink ever deeper. Thus, the Merciful Honored One, for the sake of those yet unawakened, speaks these verses:

Those who break the fast in life
Are reborn as hungry ghosts.
Hungry, they eat raging fire;
Thirsty, they drink molten bronze.
Their bodies char and wither,
Treading the edge of frost and blade.
Day and night without respite,
Their suffering knows no end.
Even if a time of liberation comes,
They are no better than dogs and horses—
Hungry, cold, poor, and lowly,
How could they possess full form?

I now extend my compassion,
My wisdom boundless through kalpas.
I establish this great Dharma-bridge
To save the foolish and deaf.
I bow my head to the Supreme Dao,
Roaming freely in the Palace of the Great Ultimate.

Today, all assembled in this sanctuary, having heard these verses, having heard this scripture, having heard this repentance, all sentient beings who have committed such deeds must undergo retribution. Today, they vow and set their minds to dedicate their merit to the Three Saints, that they may avoid such sins. Whether in the six paths of rebirth or the four modes of birth, whether they have already suffered or have yet to face retribution, all now confess openly, aspiring to attain liberation.

The repentant one, [Name], prostrates for peace and in offering to the ancestors, bowing fully to the ground, vowing with a mind of devotion. Bowing to the Merciful Honored One, paying homage to the true and sacred ones.

With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Purity who bestows blessings.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to cries and delivers from suffering.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Great Splendor.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Golden Form and Wondrous Countenance.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy whose form pervades the void.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthies of the Ten Directions, great in power.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who preserves life for a thousand ages.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of inexhaustible numinous response.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who manifests in colored form.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to those with karmic affinity.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who embodies and reveals himself.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of penetrating illumination.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who unites all truths.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Golden Portal.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of dragon virtue.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of radiant illumination.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of penetrating emptiness.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who ferries beings across.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of profound mysteries.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who fulfills ten thousand vows.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who protects life.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Great Luo.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who opens the way for all.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of long life and life-preservation.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity who delivers from suffering.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of universal compassion who guards the realm.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of carefree joy.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to vows.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of boundless expanse.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, ocean of merit and virtue.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Heavenly Worthies who fulfill all four perfections.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Perfected of Dharma Liberation.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Perfected of the Wheel of Heaven.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion who delivers from suffering.
With wholehearted reverence, we bow to the Perfected of Great Mercy who removes transgressions.

Today, the assembly in this sanctuary, together with the benefactors, reverently aspire that the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Numinous Treasure in the northwest, all the venerable ones and sages, all the great divine immortals, all the great heavenly immortals, all the great earthly immortals, all the great water immortals, all the great Perfected, all the great youths, the immortals of the sacred mountains and grotto-heavens, the sages of rivers and ancient sites, all the assemblies of holy ones, all the wondrous forms—the forms of the Perfected, the forms of jade youths, the forms of jade maidens, the Dharmakāya forms—pervading the ten directions, filling the realms of profound emptiness, all the true and sacred ones, with minds of vast deliverance, minds of Dao-power, minds of the Perfected, minds of the youths, may enable the repentant one, [Name], and their nine generations of ancestors across three lifetimes—their past bodies, future bodies, and present bodies—possessing boundless, immeasurable karmic ties, past and present, or transgressions of breaking precepts, to repent today and, by the power of the Dao, attain universal liberation.

From this day forward, facing the sacred and the true, with purified minds and bodies, they reverently uphold the precepts, aspiring that the merit and virtue may uplift their nine generations of ancestors, rescue those sunk in suffering, and deliver themselves, all their kin, and all beings of the six paths and four modes of birth, that all may ascend the shore of the Dao.

**First Bow**
**Chapter Four: Transgressions Against Scriptures and Precepts**

Today, the assembly in this sanctuary, each with focused mind, prostrates in homage to the Merciful Honored One, repenting for transgressions against scriptures and precepts.

The repentant one, [Name], gathers their mind and kneels in earnest, listening attentively to the scriptural words. All sentient beings possess the three karmas and the six senses. From kalpa to kalpa, in this life and today, they commit theft, sexual misconduct, stinginess, greed, anger, ignorance, frivolous speech, falsehood, harsh words, divisive speech—boundless, immeasurable transgressions that entangle the body, leaving no means of liberation.

The scriptures and precepts clearly expound the Dharma gates, varying in number and differing in rank. They admonish and guide beings to diminish karmic roots. Some receive the Three Precepts, Five Precepts, Six Precepts, Seven Precepts, Eight Precepts, Nine Precepts, Ten Precepts, Twelve Acceptable Precepts, Fourteen Precepts for Upholding the Body, Twenty-Four Precepts, Twenty-Seven Precepts, Thirty-Six Precepts, or even the Forty Precepts of the Lower Grade of the Cavernous Mystery, the Sixty Precepts of the Middle Grade, the Eighty-One Precepts of the Upper Grade, the One Hundred Eighty Precepts, or the Three Hundred Precepts of the Upper Clarity for Observing the Body, and the Seven Hundred Twenty Precepts of the Cavernous Spirit. Each has its sequence, guiding the deluded multitude.

Those who uphold the precepts gain boundless, immeasurable blessings; those who do not uphold them incur boundless, immeasurable karmic retribution. Moreover, the scriptures of the Three Caverns circulate among humans. If beings cannot believe and accept them, how much less the precepts? These are the city walls and dwelling houses of beings, where jade youths and jade maidens, vajra spirit-kings, and guardians come to attend and protect, praising on all sides, dispelling calamities, delivering from misfortune, preserving life, and prolonging years. The compassionate light of the true and sacred ones brings joy to all heavens. Thus, blades and weapons, floods and fires, tigers, wolves, insects, and snakes, illnesses, prisons, ghosts, thieves, hunger, cold, and afflictions are forever eradicated. One then obtains sons when seeking sons, daughters when seeking daughters, wealth, nobility, intelligence, and dignified appearance, earning respect among people—benefits beyond conception. In past lives, they are reborn in heavenly palaces and pure lands, amidst flower terraces and jeweled trees, with natural clothing and food, wondrous offerings from celestial kitchens, cloud canopies and dragon chariots, carefree and joyous, constantly hearing the scriptures, standing in attendance to the Merciful Honored One. In future rebirths, they will encounter the true Dao.

All sentient beings, if they uphold the precepts, are like a precious sword that severs all, like a Dharma boat that ferries all, like a fierce fire that burns all, like pure water that washes all. Those who uphold the precepts guard against wrongdoing, restrain evil, discipline body and mind, subdue demonic foes, and move the numinous and sacred. Yet you, all beings, whether having received them personally or witnessed others receiving them, have failed to revere and believe, constantly harboring arrogance, committing countless transgressions, accumulating slander, treating them as mere play, neglecting to uphold them, acting contrary to their words, writing carelessly, reciting irreverently, altering the text, and deviating from the scriptures.

Some may read the *Taiqing Treasury Scriptures*, the *Shangqing Treasury Scriptures*, or the *Yuqing Treasury Scriptures*—whether reciting them themselves or witnessing others recite them—yet treat them with frivolity, failing to arouse reverent mindfulness. They disdain the sacred words, extol the Great Dao without offering devotion, and neglect their protection with half-hearted care. Some transcribe them with poor paper and ink, binding them shoddily with crooked cords and slanted rollers, staining or losing the text. Others annotate and alter the meanings, their ignorance obstructing the principles, devoid of veneration. Such transgressions, with deep karmic roots, if left unrepented, will forever bar one from the cycles of rebirth.

Should they remain in the world, they will be afflicted by malignant illnesses, their bodies frail and feeble, their breath faint and weak, their speech coarse and clumsy, ignorant of rites and music, unable to discern right from wrong. When their life ends, they will fail to ascend to the Pure Land, their sins plunging them into profound darkness, where suffering ceaselessly torments them. No rebirth awaits them—only relentless trials, each debt repaid in full, enduring agony with groans, their flesh and bones severed by karmic bonds. They will bear the torment of a single body: climbing a thousand-fathom sword-tree, grasping its branches to ascend, only to sink into a cauldron of boiling water, crushed beneath its weight until utterly consumed. Only then may they find respite—all from violating the precepts, born of disbelief.

Thus the Compassionate One spoke in verse:
*Those who transgress scriptures and precepts in life*
*Shall enter the hell of blades and needles in death.*
*Pierced on all sides, their bodies endure*
*Ten thousand pains beyond endurance.*
*They traverse the blade-mountains, then plunge*
*Into cauldrons of boiling water.*
*Death they seek but cannot find—*
*Only after ten thousand kalpas may they be reborn.*

Today, the assembly of this grand ritual, as the scriptures foretell, trembles with dread. For the transgressions we have committed—violating scriptures and precepts, boundless and measureless, grave and weighty sins—we shall suffer their retribution in future lives or even in this present existence. Now, we prostrate ourselves in sincerity, making confession and repentance. May all beings across the four modes of birth and six realms of existence, sharing the same karmic cause and effect, each attain liberation.

The repentant sponsor, [Name], humbly offers this text of repentance for peace and merit-transference, prostrating with the five limbs touching the earth, wholeheartedly invoking the sacred. Bowing in reverence to the Compassionate One, we pay homage to the true and holy sages:

With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Purity who bestows blessings.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy who rescues upon hearing cries of suffering.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Great Brilliance.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Sun and Moon Radiance.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Attained Dao.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mountain of Virtue and Treasure.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy, King of the Mountain of All Treasures.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ten Supreme Virtues.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of All Wisdom.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Power of Dao-Wisdom.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Nature of Dao and Things.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Virtue.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Dharma Joy.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Transformation and Transmission.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Good Precepts.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Dissemination.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great One who Rescues from Suffering.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life-Preservation.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and Nation-Protection.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Bliss.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Rebirth According to Aspiration.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Expanse.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Virtue.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Perfected One of Salvation.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Perfected One who Delivers from Suffering.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Perfected One of Great Compassion and Salvation.
With devout hearts, we bow to the Perfected One of Great Mercy and Sin-Eradication.

Today, the repentant sponsor of this ritual and the entire assembly lift their aspirations toward the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the Northwest, together with all venerated sages, all great immortals, all great perfected ones, and all great divine youths—manifesting across the ten directions and throughout the boundless cosmos. May they, in unison, bestow the power of the Dao and arouse compassionate hearts. May the repentant sponsor, [Name], their parents of three lifetimes, their present parents, and all their kin—who have violated precepts and defied scriptures, accumulating manifold sins—through this act of repentance, attain liberation. From this day forward, through all future lives, may they don the dark crown and yellow robe, assuming the dharma-bodies of male or female officials. May they together uphold the precepts, receive the precepts at the same altar, accept the registers of precepts, study under the same master, undergo the same ordination, be jointly recommended, and simultaneously be delivered. Whether as male or female officials or youths, may they forever vow to observe the precepts, reverently tend the incense fire, remain ever vigilant, instruct and guide their dharma-disciples, uphold their vows, and walk the supreme Dao.

May the power of virtue and wisdom, through skillful means, rescue and deliver all sentient beings, freeing them from worldly defilements. May all who hear or witness this be filled with joy, ascend to the realization of non-action, and return to the Great Dao.

One bow.

The *Tai Shang* Merciful Compassion Ritual Arena for Dispelling Disasters and the Nine Dark Realms: Repentance Scroll Six Concludes
*The Tai Shang Merciful Compassion Ritual Arena for Dispelling Disasters and the Nine Dark Realms: Repentance Scroll Seven*

Compiled by Ge Xuan, the Left Immortal of the Supreme Ultimate

**Chapter One: Dispelling Disobedience and Rebellion**

Today, the great assembly of this ritual arena, each turning their minds, bow their heads to the Merciful Honored One, repenting the sins of disobedience and unfilial impiety.

The repentance master, so-and-so, gathers their mind, kneels reverently, and listens attentively to the scriptural words. All sentient beings, from the moment they receive the illumination of sun and moon, drift with the turning of fate, endowed with skin and hair, all owing to their parents.

The Universal Savior says: Without examining the causes and conditions of parents, the weight of their kindness and obligation, how can one know the requital of their nurturing?

The Merciful Honored One says:
If the form is straight, its shadow must be upright;
If the form is not straight, its shadow must be crooked.
If the voice is clear, its echo must be pure;
If the voice is not clear, its sound must be turbid.
Filial piety and impiety follow this principle.

If one is filial and fraternal, within a single household, the old and young live in peace. The world holds them in esteem, divine spirits guard them, and descendants carry on the lineage, their filial kindness unbroken. They attract filial devotion, treasuring it as a precious jewel.

Yet if one is unfilial, generation after generation, within a single household, all become enemies. Though they speak of parents, they treat them as foes, summoning the disobedient to be their children. Parents and siblings keep separate finances and meals, share gardens but divide vegetables, split fields and grain, hide delicacies, and eat in secret. Though in human form, they are worse than birds and beasts. Divine spirits do not protect them; all their deeds in life are inauspicious. Upon death, they enter hell, enduring every suffering. Only after ten thousand kalpas are they reborn, as the *bailao* bird, whose young, upon hatching, devour their mother. Only after leaving the nest do they return to the human realm, where the unfilial gather as fathers and sons, harming one another, mutually resentful. No suffering in the world exceeds this.

Yet without a father, one would not be born; without a mother, one would not be raised. Thus, heaven and earth cover and nurture, entrusting life to the mother’s body. The two *qi* congeal, and for ten months she carries the child, burdened and heavy, sitting and lying uncomfortably. When the time is full, at the moment of birth, the mother is terrified, her life hanging by a thread. Her heart aches, her spirit grieves, and in an instant, she fears for her life. On the day of delivery, internal and external pains assail her, agony intertwined. She loses her voice in wailing, enduring great torment, trembling in fear, shocked and sighing.

Once born, the mother rejoices beyond measure, wrapping the child in swaddling clothes. For three months, she lies on her side, ever wary of evil spirits. When hungry, the child needs food—only the mother feeds them. When thirsty, the child needs drink—only the mother nurses them. Calculating the milk she drinks, it amounts to eight *hu* and four *sheng*. For a thousand days, the mother carries the child, washing away dirt and grime, placing them in dry spots while taking the wet, swallowing bitterness and offering sweetness. Without the father, there is no closeness; without the mother, there is no nurturing.

In the *Kaihuang* kalpa of old, there was a sentient being whose parents were aged, their strength and vitality waning. From dawn to dusk, their child never came to inquire after them. The parents dwelled alone in an empty room, like strangers. They had little clothing and scant food, hunger and cold piercing their bodies. Their hands and feet were stiff, their ears deaf and eyes dim. They slept on a single bed with a thin mat, each day feeling like a year. Their bodies were frail and emaciated, infested with ants and lice. Mosquitoes bit their flesh, and they could not sleep all night, sighing and groaning. Seeing their child’s unfilial conduct, they leaned on a staff to call out, heads bowed and breath subdued, wishing to voice their grievances but unable to finish their words. Their child raised their voice, glaring angrily, and cursed their parents. Turning away, they retreated, leaning on the wall to return home, beating their chest in sorrow, eyes swollen from weeping, crying out in misery, wishing they had died sooner.

The mother said to her elder son: When you were small, had I not raised you, fed you, and shielded you, you would not have survived. For ten months, I carried you like a heavy burden, my breath panting, more labored than running. At times, I suffered chills and fever, unable to sit or lie comfortably. My belly split, my chest felt full, my hair fell out, and I grew thin, unable to eat. A month before birth, I was constantly anxious, fearing we would not part. On the day of delivery, my life was like a flickering candle. My limbs and veins felt as if cut by knives, my five viscera and six bowels burned like fire. After you were born, joy and fear mingled; the pains and sorrows cannot be fully described. For three years, I carried you day and night, never apart. I endured filth, lost sleep, and missed meals, watching your complexion to tend to your hunger and fullness. If you fell ill, my heart ached for you. Hearing your suffering, I could not eat. My mouth and throat were parched as I sought every blessing. Gold and silver, clothes and toys—I wished for your safety and spared nothing.

I remember when you were small, you followed me everywhere, never leaving my side. You ate when I ate, slept when I slept. A single day without me, and you would not eat all day; a single night without me, and you would cry without sleep. How have you grown to suddenly become my enemy? Now, though I have you, it would be better if I had never borne you. I wish I could die soon and be free of you.

Thus, that child truly incurred the grave sin of disobedience and unfilial impiety. Upon death, they entered the Fengdu Hell of the North, enduring every suffering, experiencing all bitterness, dying and being reborn ten thousand times—none of it can be fully recounted.

Then, the Merciful Honored One, for those yet unenlightened, spoke this verse:

Good naturally meets good,
Evil returns to its evil root.
In life, lacking kindness and filial piety,
In death, one sinks forever.
Enduring all sufferings,
Passing through the eighteen gates.
If not on the day of my three pardons,
One will never hear of liberation.
Reborn as the *bailao* bird,
Flesh and bone torn by one’s young.
When the retribution is complete and one returns to the human path,
One meets again as child and grandchild.

Today, the great assembly of this ritual arena, hearing these scriptural words, must awaken greatly.

From past lives to this present existence, should any have committed the karmic transgressions of disobedience and unfilial conduct, in days to come they may yet suffer this retribution. Let them now diligently advance, arouse the mind of repentance, and vow that all beings who receive such retribution may together attain liberation. The repentant one, [Name], prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text in memorial rites, bowing with the five limbs to the ground, single-mindedly arousing the vow.

With bowed head, I pay homage to the Merciful Honored One, reverently saluting the true sages.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Jade Purity Heavenly Worthy who bestows blessings.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy who rescues suffering upon hearing cries.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mysterious Upper Jade Palace.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy who saves and delivers the world.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Pristine Radiance of Cosmic Qi.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Wondrous Sound and Self-Mastery.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Self-Mastery and Dharma Victory.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mysterious Capital and Myriad Longevities.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy, King of Everlasting Joy.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Salvation and Deliverance.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Constantly Increasing Superior Goodness.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Congealed Splendor and Golden Flowers.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Purple Purity who delivers souls.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Wondrous Dharma and Expedient Means.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy who engenders and completes the myriad existences.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Moisture Dharma Ocean.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Manifest Transformation and Responsive Assembly.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Harmonious Embrace and Nurturing Life.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Realizing Fruition and Perfect Illumination.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Brahma Golden Body.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Dao’s Intent.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Cultivating Wondrous Practices.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Profound Constancy and Quiescence.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Awesome Virtue.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Radiance and Wondrous Brilliance.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Constant Response and Manifestation.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Supreme One who rescues from suffering.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy who preserves life and protects destiny.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and National Protection.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy who grants rebirth according to vows.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Expanse.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Perfected of Eastern Florescence.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Five Emperors Perfected.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion and Salvation from Suffering.
With sincere reverence, I bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion and Deliverance from Sin.

Today, the patrons of this ritual arena and the great assembly, gazing upward, vow to the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the North, to all the honored ones and sages, all the great perfected, all the great immortals, all the great divine youths, who pervade the ten directions, fill the boundless cosmos, and manifest as all true sages. With cinnabar flowers and pure water, may they cleanse the three lifetimes’ kin of the repentant one, [Name], from the infinite kalpas past to this very day—should any have committed the karmic transgressions of disobedience and unfilial conduct, whether enacted or yet to be received—through this repentance, may all be extinguished, and may they not suffer retribution. From this day forward, in life after life, may they revere their parents as heaven and earth, as emperors and kings; may they stand in awe of their parents as the stars and the sun and moon. In the state, may they be utterly loyal; in the family, utterly filial. Toward all beings, human and non-human, may they fully observe kindness and obedience. May they awaken to past transgressions and early realize the Great Dao.

One bow.

**Chapter Two: Vowing to Repay the Kindness of Mercy**

Today, in this ritual arena, each member of the great assembly directs their mind and takes refuge in the Merciful Honored One, speaking of the karmic causes and effects of repaying the kindness of mercy. The repentant one, [Name], collects their thoughts, kneels in reverence, and listens attentively to the scriptural words. All beings cycle through birth and death, revolving through the dark realms. Now, I radiate great light, penetrating the five directions and ten lands. All suffering beings are delivered, save only those guilty of disobedience, who cannot ascend. Know that the kindness and righteousness of parents is profound and weighty. The boundless heavens cannot be repaid; even grinding one’s bones to powder and carving one’s flesh cannot fully requite it. If one can cultivate steadfast resolve, outwardly practicing filial devotion and nurturing, inwardly harboring vast compassion, then not only one’s own parents, but all beings are one’s parents. All beings are one’s brothers. All beings are one’s sisters. All beings are one’s flesh and blood. All beings are one’s sons and daughters. All beings are those who nurture and raise. All beings are those one loves and protects. Do not harm their lives; do not consume their flesh. Whether in past lives, future lives, or the present life, regard all beings as kin. Through manifold expedient means, this is called repaying kindness. Should any man or woman wish to perform meritorious deeds to repay the kindness of heaven and earth, the sovereign, their teachers, and their birth parents, let them proceed in order: first for heaven and earth, second for the emperor, third for their teachers, fourth for their birth parents, fifth for all beings of the great earth, and sixth for all their own kin. Yet among worldly men and women, from the moment they emerge from their mother’s womb, through one year, ten years, a hundred years, or a hundred and twenty years, they must prepare in advance. Beginning with the first seven-day period, cycling repeatedly, even unto distant years, let the meritorious deeds they perform follow this order: first, commissioning images; second, commissioning scriptures; third, erecting long banners of forty-nine feet, establishing forty-nine Dharma bodies, providing vegetarian feasts, and constructing ritual arenas to invite scriptures and images. Let the Dharma masters’ ritual lamps number forty-nine vessels, or more as their capacity allows. Let lamps be arranged like chariot wheels, burning for three days and nights, seven days and nights, or forty-nine days and nights, dedicated to the sovereign, the emperor, their teachers, Dharma kin, parents, siblings, and all their own kin. With hearts laid bare and utmost sincerity, they pay homage to my invoked titles, repent their own transgressions, pray for blessings and grace, repay the kindness of mercy, offer wholehearted devotion, and extol with praise.

All past transgressions, once repented, must be amended with renewed cultivation. Diligently observe fasts and precepts, turn the heart toward compassion and goodness, and extend almsgiving to the fields of merit—whether to the poor and lowly, the disabled, the sick and solitary elders, prisoners, hungry ghosts, or all sentient beings. Those who lack benevolence should be exhorted to embrace virtuous causes. For travelers from afar in dire need, provide succor, rescue them from peril, and offer clothing and food to ensure their sufficiency. Then, renew the vow to honor parents with filial piety. The wealthy should commission images and copy scriptures to deliver beings from the three wretched destinies and the five sufferings, and to liberate those sunk in the depths of torment. According to their vows, they may attain rebirth—this is the repayment of kindness.

If any man or woman, through accumulated deeds, has ever slandered the Three Treasures, been disloyal or unfilial, offended the sovereign or ruler, teachers, or parents, or committed the five grave transgressions—such deep and weighty sins that they fear falling into hell at life’s end and suffering myriad torments—let them, for the sake of the sovereign, ruler, teachers, or parents, generate resolve and make vows: transcribe scriptures and repentance texts, even a single line or verse; venerate my invoked titles, one or two or many. On the day of their passing, they shall not enter hell nor endure former karmic retribution, but proceed directly to heaven to receive boundless joy.

If any man or woman, for the sake of the sovereign, ruler, teachers, parents, or their own kin, observes the Three Primes and Eight Festivals, either at home or at sacred altars, venerates my sacred titles, repents sins and averts misfortune, holds grand vegetarian feasts, prepares fragrant offerings piled high as mountains, gathers fruits and herbs, presents flowers, and arranges pure offerings—vigilantly seeking blessings and grace through the night—then may the nation and household be secured, the great earth delivered, and all sentient beings rescued. Let none commit the ten evils or grave offenses, and may the sins of nine generations of ancestors, whether already suffered or yet to be, all be extinguished. If on such days the meaning of the scriptures is expounded, and the ignorant and benighted are guided to awaken loyalty, filial piety, and the resolve to save others, this merit shall be foremost.

Then, the Compassionate Honored One, for the sake of those yet unawakened, spoke this verse:

All people in the world,
Should cultivate filial piety in body and mind.
Revere and cherish heaven and earth,
As you would your own parents.
Ultimately attain the fruit of the Dao,
With wondrous practices renewed each day.
I now expound the sublime Dharma,
To deliver those sunk in suffering.
Karma unfolds in endless retribution,
Turning the wheel of kalpas day and night.
I establish this great Dharma bridge,
To ferry you across the river of craving.
Wondrous indeed are the Three Caverns’ scriptures,
Transcending those with karmic affinity.

Today, the master of repentance in this ritual arena, along with the assembly, having heard the scriptural teachings on repaying kindness through myriad causes, all awaken to the need for gratitude and vow never to act in defiance. Today, prostrating for peace and offering this repentance text, they bow with their entire being, wholeheartedly generating resolve.

With reverence, they bow to the Compassionate Honored One,
And pay homage to the true sages.

With sincere devotion, they bow to the Jade Clarity Bestower of Blessings Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves Through Sound.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mysterious Upper Jade Palace.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jeweled Splendor.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy, King of All Wisdom.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Clarity’s Spiritual Transformations.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Pure Conduct and Right Contemplation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Preaches in the Nine Dark Realms.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Radiant Divine Merit.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Manifests in All Directions.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Golden Splendor and Wondrous Radiance.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Empty Tranquility and Right Contemplation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Transforms the Three Realms.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Hundred Million Heavenly Worthies Who Respond to Names.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves According to Vows.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Essence and Dharma Ocean.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Rescues Lives from the Purple Palace.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Illuminating Lofty Conduct.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Pervades All Beings Without Limit.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Supreme Wondrousness.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Jeweled Adornment.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean Treasury.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Auspicious Response.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Unity Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Preserves Life and Longevity.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion Who Protects the Nation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Extent.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Bliss.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Vows.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Wondrous Awareness.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Compassionate Wisdom.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion Who Eradicates Transgressions.

Today, the patrons of this ritual arena, along with the assembly, reverently pray that the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the North, all the honored ones, sages, great perfected, great heavenly immortals, great earthly immortals, and all the great youthful saviors who pervade the ten directions, fill the boundless cosmos, and manifest in response to names—may they sprinkle the waters of the Jasper Pool to purify body and mind. Through their unimpeded power, may the repentance master here generate resolve and turn toward all manner of good causes, thereby attaining immeasurable blessings, fulfilling every wish, and accomplishing all aspirations. From this day forward, they vow to repay kindness to the best of their ability. May all karmic adversaries from past kalpas, all sins great and small, along with those of their teachers, parents, uncles, brothers, their own kin, and the three generations of affinal relatives—whether from past lives, now liberated, or presently living—be enabled to establish merit and repay virtue. Through the power of this repentance, may all beings, whether male or female, embody the mysterious wind of unity and take refuge in the Great Dao.

One bow to the third repentance rite: *Dissolving Residual Karmic Obstructions*

Today, the great assembly of this Dao altar, each with focused mind, reverently faces the Compassionate Honored One to repent and release the multitude of residual karmic obstructions. The repentance master, with sincere heart and kneeling posture, listens attentively to the scriptural words:

All beings arise from the primordial qi of the undifferentiated. Through the kindness of parents—carrying, nurturing, breastfeeding—they gradually grow, yet unable to discern, they become entangled in desire, and the roots of transgression flourish. If not for repentance, if not for the expounding of scriptures and precepts, gently guiding them into the right Dao, they would forever remain bound by the ignorance of aversion and attachment, fettered to the mundane world.

Parents can only give birth to us; they cannot perfect us. It is our teachers who reveal the scriptures and precepts, enabling us to transcend afflictions. Thus, the kindness of teachers surpasses even that of parents.

Yet we see beings who, from the moment they establish themselves in the world, fail to recognize the profound debt owed to their teachers. Instead, they respond with scorn and abuse, withhold what is needed, deny sweet sustenance, refuse clothing and food, treat them as strangers, or even plot harm. Such acts align them with rebellious children, inviting karmic retribution in return.

We see beings who observe fasts and precepts—some, occupying high positions, humiliate those beneath them; others, relying on wealth and status, oppress the orphaned and impoverished...

Some abuse their power to oppress the lowly and weak; others, holding office, make extortion their intent, inflicting cruel punishments at will, enriching themselves at public expense, and acting against the Dao/Way. They encroach upon the blessed lands of the Three Treasures, occupying their pure sanctuaries. Some commission revered images, transcribe scriptures, or establish sacred observatories, construct refectories, and hold fasts and rituals. Yet as leaders, they steal property, engage in fraudulent trade, or misappropriate the wealth of monastic endowments or donors. They live alongside parents, siblings, and kin, yet in all their dealings, they deceive and rob one another. They shift fences to encroach on others’ land, seize fields and gardens, exploit public authority to seize others’ inns and shops, cheat merchants in trade, use false weights and measures, reduce lengths and widths, conceal fractions of grain, falsify calculations, substitute coarse for fine, exchange short for long, and devise a hundred deceits to gain the slightest profit. They burn others’ homes, falsely implicate the innocent, envy others’ wealth and status, spread slander, and vent rage upon their parents. They lend capital to exact exorbitant interest, indulge in greed and desire, seize others’ property by force, refuse to repay debts, and deny their obligations. They kill without cause, engage in illicit sacrifices, defy public and private authority, file baseless accusations, act with arrogance and rudeness, deceive superiors and betray subordinates. Some strip the belongings of ordained practitioners, desecrate graves to steal coffins, or cast nets and traps to cunningly seize creatures from ponds, pools, rivers, the Huai and Ji, seas and streams, springs, lakes, and waterways. Such karmic offenses are manifold and beyond count. If beings commit even one such transgression, they incur grave retribution, burdening billions of ancestors across ten thousand generations, as well as their parents, themselves, and their six relations and nine clans. The deceased and those of past lives suffer misfortune, descending into hell, where each is ground by millstones, enduring retribution for ten thousand kalpas before rebirth—if reborn at all, they may not survive infancy, living out their days in solitude. Such karmic conditions are predestined. Today, in this ritual assembly, as the scriptures declare, the sins and blessings, good and evil of beings return in retribution, seen and heard like a turning wheel, swift as an echo. Let each gather their thoughts and cultivate in accord with the teachings. If years pass in vain, and age and illness press upon you, when body and life perish in a single day, what means remain to escape this sinking into darkness? Through this rite of repentance, may all—those present, past, and yet to incur such karmic offenses—receive the moisture of the Dharma, universally attain liberation, and be freed from bondage.

The repentant one, [Name], prostrates in reverence, bowing with body, mind, and heart, to offer this text of repentance for peace and merit-transference. With five limbs touching the earth and a single mind, they raise their thoughts in devotion:

With bowed head, they pay homage to the Compassionate Venerable One, reverently saluting the true and sacred.

With sincere devotion, they bow to the Jade Clarity Bestower of Blessings, Heavenly Worthy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering at a Cry.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mysterious Upper Jade Palace.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Wondrous Dharma.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of True Stillness and Compassion.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Flowing Gold and the Purple Ultimate.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Illumines the Dark Night.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Suffering’s Liberation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Nine Nights’ Jeweled Light.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Radiant Wondrous Splendor.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Jeweled Pearl.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion and Salvation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Divine Penetration and Profound Abyss.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Vast Illumination.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Manifestation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Perfected.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Illuminating Beneficence.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Wisdom’s Response.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Wondrous and Marvelous.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Mighty Spirit.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Eternal Abiding.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Flowing Light and the Dharma Realm.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Longevity and Life Preservation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Great One Who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and State Protection.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Extent.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of the Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Heavenly Worthy Who Grants Rebirth According to Wish.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Wisdom’s Countenance.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Wisdom’s Contemplation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion and Salvation.
With sincere devotion, they bow to the Perfected of Great Compassion and Sin-Removal.

Today, the repentant one of this ritual assembly, together with all present, reverently beseech the Supreme Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy of the North, all the Venerables and Sages, all the Great Perfected Ones, all the Great Perfected Persons, all the Great Divine Youths, and all the boundless hosts of divine immortals and sacred assemblies—those who pervade the ten directions, fill the vast expanse, and manifest as all true and sacred beings. With the water of cinnabar blossoms, may they cleanse the hearts and mouths of the repentant one, [Name], their billions of ancestors across ten thousand generations, their parents, uncles, brothers, themselves, their sons and daughters, all their kin, and both the living and the dead. From kalpas past to the present, from this life to this very day, for all the karmic offenses and sins they have committed, and all the residual karmic burdens they have accrued in this world, whether now confined in the prisons of hell, may they repent and be swiftly purified, depart from evil paths, enter good conditions, avoid the five destinies, and universally attain carefree joy. May they drink from the single Dharma, be reborn in eternal bliss, realize the unconditioned, and together ascend the Great Dao/Way.

One bow. *Seeing Karmic Retribution*, Fourth Chapter.

Today, the great assembly of this Daoist ritual, each with sincere intent, reverently bows to the Merciful Honored One, repenting and expounding the karmic causes and effects of retribution. The repentant one, [Name], kneels with devoted heart, attentively heeding the scriptural words:

All beings who deface or destroy the true and sacred images of the Perfected, or the Three Caverns’ scriptures, shall in this life suffer leprosy as retribution, and upon death enter hell, where only after ten thousand kalpas may they be reborn—into the body of a wild beast. If they return to the human realm, their tongues shall rot and decay.

Those who slander the Dharma-body of the renunciates shall in this life suffer the retribution of festering sores, and in past lives be reborn among the six kinds of livestock.

Those who desecrate or damage sacred temples and altars shall in this life have their eyebrows and beards fall out, their bodies fester and waste away, and in past lives be reborn as venomous serpents.

Those who show disrespect to the sacred images and true countenance of the Heavenly Worthy and the Great Dao/Way shall in this life be dull-witted and foolish, and in past lives be reborn in poverty and lowliness.

Those who do not believe in the scriptures or the retribution of past lives shall in this life suffer deafness and blindness, and in past lives be reborn among birds and beasts.

Those who do not believe in the karmic causes and effects of sin and merit shall in this life be enslaved as servants, and in past lives be reborn among barbarian tribes.

Those who slight or disdain the Dharma-body of the renunciates shall in this life be lame and crippled, and in past lives be reborn among swine and dogs.

Those who defile the sacred grounds of the Three Treasures shall in this life be ugly in appearance, and in past lives be reborn in filth and dung.

Those who engage in licentious acts with the Dharma-body of the renunciates shall in this life suffer the retribution of loneliness and widowhood, and in past lives be reborn in latrines and cesspits.

Those who steal the wealth and property of the Three Treasures shall in this life be impoverished, and in past lives be reborn as servants.

Those who steal the communal possessions of the monastic community shall in this life suffer from wind-borne diseases, and in past lives be reborn in animal forms.

Those who steal the offerings of the fourfold assembly shall in this life be afflicted with madness, and in past lives be reborn as fools.

Those who consume the vegetables and fruits of the Three Treasures shall in this life suffer from wasting thirst, and in past lives be reborn as starving tigers and venomous serpents.

Those who steal the food offerings of the fast shall in this life be struck dead by thunderbolts, and in past lives be reborn as vipers and serpents, or upon death enter the realm of hungry ghosts.

Those who steal the Dharma-robes and ritual implements shall in this life be naked and exposed, and in past lives be reborn as starving dogs.

Those who steal the scriptures, images, and vestments shall in this life suffer painful retributions, and upon death enter hell, where they shall remain for ten thousand kalpas without release.

Those who break the fast or violate the precepts shall in this life suffer from throat diseases, and in past lives be reborn deaf and blind.

Those who kill living beings shall in this life suffer from chronic illness and short lifespans, and in past lives be reborn among the six kinds of livestock.

Those who consume meat or partake of impure foods shall in this life suffer from poverty and disease.

Those who indulge in wine and give free rein to their passions shall in this life be afflicted with madness and lack steadfastness of mind.

Those who mock or ridicule the renunciates shall in this life bear the appearance of gibbons and apes.

Those whose hands or feet are maimed or broken have come from disrespect toward the Three Sages.

Those whose eyes are afflicted with cataracts have come from disbelief in the scriptures.

Those whose tongues are shriveled or retracted have come from defacing the scriptures.

Those who are mute and unable to speak have come from slandering the Dharma-body of the renunciates.

Those whose noses are blocked and cannot smell have come from indulging in wine, meat, and the five pungent roots.

Those whose bodies fester and ulcerate have come from destroying the true and sacred images.

Those whose eyebrows and beards fall out have come from failing to revere the sacred images.

Those whose lips curl, teeth protrude, and noses collapse have come from disrupting ritual arenas.

Those who are hunchbacked, crook-chested, or have twisted spines and short legs have come from arrogance and disdain.

Those who are afflicted with madness, perverse illnesses, and delusion have come from disbelief in karmic causes and good deeds.

Those whose appearance is marred by sores and ulcers have come from cursing and reviling without cause.

Those whose eyes are bloodshot and mouths are twisted have come from mockery and rudeness.

Those who are foolish and lack wisdom have come from deceit and falsehood.

Those who encounter bandits and robbers, or are plundered of their wealth, have come from failing to repay debts.

Those who drown or are swept away by water have come from trapping and netting aquatic creatures.

Those who are devoured by venomous serpents have come from killing and harming others.

Those who are burned and scorched by fire have come from hunting and setting mountains and forests ablaze.

Those who are devoured by fierce tigers have come from scheming and harboring malice.

Those who suffer from hunger, cold, and starvation, their bodies unclothed, have come from stealing the food of the fast.

Those whose parents, spouses, and children are separated from them have come from jealousy, adultery, breaking the harmony of others, and severing bonds of love.

Those who are shorn of hair, with deep-set eyes and long noses, have come from hunting and taking life.

All such bodily forms in this life arise from past offenses and karmic transgressions, from dying and passing through hell, and even in future rebirths, the retribution shall know no respite.

The Merciful Honored One addressed the Universal Savior, saying: “You must wholeheartedly believe and uphold this, clearly instructing future generations, so that all men and women may fully understand the karmic retributions of past lives, the manifold causes and conditions. Today, the great assembly of this Daoist ritual, as the scriptures declare, suffers these various retributions in this life due to deeds committed in past lives. You must awaken and reflect deeply. Do not say that hell is unreal or that heaven is a falsehood. You must arouse sincere and earnest mindfulness, with deep remorse and gravity. May all beings follow and obey the teachings, entering the Dharma-gate, just as one who wishes to traverse a perilous path must find a ladder or boat. Without such merit, by what means can one cross over?”

The repentant one, [Name], prostrates for peace and offers this repentance text in supplication. With the five limbs touching the ground, and with wholehearted devotion, bows to the Merciful Honored One and reverently salutes the true and sacred ones.

With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Clarity who bestows blessings.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who responds to cries and saves from suffering.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of the Mysterious Upper Jade Palace.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who universally reveals the Dao/Way.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who saves and delivers from the sea of suffering.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who liberates according to conditions.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Universal Teachings.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, the Sagely King who delivers the world.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Contemplation and Practice.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, the Root of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Illumination.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of the True Rank.

With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, Source of the Dharma.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, Great Perfected King.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy Supreme in the Dharma.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of the Full Moon.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who Delivers Beings through Cause and Effect.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Lofty Mysterious Emptiness.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Lofty Pure Primordial Radiance.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Jade Purity and Mysterious Luminosity.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who Transmits and Circulates the Dharma.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Transformative Generation.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, Supreme Master.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, Great One who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who Preserves Life and Protects Destiny.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Universal Compassion and National Protection.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Carefree Joy.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy who Grants Rebirth According to Vows.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy of Boundless Extent.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Heavenly Worthy, Ocean of Merit and Virtue.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Perfected One of the Central Yellow.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Perfected One of Universal Transformation.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Perfected One of Great Compassion who Saves from Suffering.
With sincere devotion, bows to the Perfected One of Great Mercy who Delivers from Transgressions.

Today, the repentance master of this Daoist ritual, together with the great assembly, reverently beseech the Heavenly Worthy of the Supreme Numinous Treasure of the Northern Realm, all the Venerable Ones and Sages, all the Great Perfected Ones, and all the Great Divine Youths—those who pervade the ten directions, fill the realms of mysterious emptiness, and manifest in all forms.

May they, in their compassionate radiance, together extend deliverance.

The repentance master [Name], from kalpas immeasurable and beginningless down to the present kalpa, in this present life and on this very day, for the sake of nine generations of parents, three lineages of ancestors, uncles and brothers, and all kin by blood or marriage—past, future, and present—who may have fallen into evil destinies, languished in dark confinement, or endured manifold sufferings—may those now living, who bear the consequences of their karma and suffer from illness and afflictions, through this repentance, have their transgressions universally dissolved and together attain peace and bliss.

From this day forward, may I regard all sentient beings as myself; may I vow to renounce all evil deeds upon witnessing them; and may I resolve to learn from all virtuous conditions upon encountering them. Awakening to the fruits of karma, may I cultivate practice in accordance with the teachings.

May I, in life after life, never lose my human nature. May all sentient beings, in the worlds to come, together be born in the Land of Bliss and equally partake of the Mysterious Wind.

Prostrating in reverence, I take refuge in the Supreme True Dao.
One bow.

The *Tai Shang*’s Compassionate *Dao* Altar: *Nine Dark Hells Repentance for Disaster Dispelling*, Scroll Seven—Concluded
The *Tai Shang*’s Compassionate *Dao* Altar: *Nine Dark Hells Repentance for Disaster Dispelling*, Scroll Eight
Compiled by Supreme Left Immortal Lord Ge Xuan

**First Chapter: Deliverance from the Sufferings of Fengdu Hell**

Today, the great assembly of this *Dao* altar, each with concentrated mind, reverently faces the Compassionate Honored One to deliver those suffering in Fengdu Hell.

The repentant master, kneeling in prostration, listens attentively to the scriptural words: Hell is neither existent nor nonexistent.

The Universal Savior asks, “Why is it said to be nonexistent?”
The Compassionate Honored One replies, “If all sentient beings do not indulge the three karmic actions, do not give rein to the six senses, do not commit the ten evils, nor perpetrate the five rebellious acts or any transgressions, then upon death they will not enter the nine dark hells of Fengdu but proceed directly to the heavenly realms, carefree and at ease. This is what is meant by nonexistent.”

“Why is it said to be not nonexistent?”
